Definition of Minimum Travel Distance for Qasr
Defines the minimum travel distance and how it is calculated.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the minimum travel distance required for qasr in the Hanafi school and identify which legal concessions are tied to this distance.

Core Idea
Three days' moderate travel with rest is the measure for qasr, but not for every rukhsa.

This passage from Nur al-Idah defines the minimum travel distance that triggers legal concessions such as shortening prayer. It specifies the distance as three days' journey using a moderate pace, then lists which rulings change and which do not. The accompanying commentary clarifies how to calculate this distance over different terrains and conditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition
Read the opening sentence: what is the minimum travel distance that changes rulings? Extract the core parameters (three days, shortest days, moderate pace, rest stops).
The definition is time-based, not distance-based, reflecting classical travel conditions.
2
List the affected rulings
The passage enumerates concessions that depend on this distance (qasr, iftar, wiping over khuffain more than a day, waiving udhiyah) and those that do not (leaving Jumu‘ah, ‘Eid, congregation, etc.). Separate them clearly.
This distinction is crucial to avoid conflating different rulings.
3
Understand the calculation method
Examine how the three-day journey is calculated: moderate pace (camels/feet), rest stops for eating, sleeping, etc., and terrain adjustments (mountains, sea). Note that faster or slower travel is not considered.
The standard is the middle pace; extremes are ignored.
4
Use predominant probability
The commentary states that certainty is not required; ghalabat al-zann (predominant probability) suffices in estimating the distance. This is a practical facilitation.
This principle is typical in Hanafi fiqh to avoid undue hardship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أقل سفر تتغير به الأحكام مسيرة ثلاثة أيام من أقصر أيام السنة بسير وسط مع الاستراحات، والوسط سير الإبل ومشي الأقدام في البر وفي الجبل بما يناسبه، وفي البحر اعتدال الريح، أي إبل القافلة

ثلاثة هذا التقدير للسفر الذي تقصر فيه الصلاة، ويباح فيه الفطر، ويمسح فيه أكثر من يوم وليلة، وتسقط به الأضحية، وأما المبيح لترك الجمعة والعيدين والجماعة والمبيح للتنفل على الدابة وللتيمم، ولاستحباب القرعة بين نسائه، فلا يقدر بهذه المدة. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٤۲۱ أيام قدر بالأيام دون المراحل والفراسخ، وهو الأصح. مراقي الفلاح: ٤٢١] بسير وسط : فلو أسرع بريده فقطع ما يقطع بالسير الوسط في ثلاثة أيام في أقل منها قصر، وكما إذا سار فيها سيراً خارقا للعادة، وصرح في "التبيين": أنه يكتفى في تقدير المسافة بالمدة المذكورة بغلبة الظن، ولا يشترط اليقين. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٤٢١] مع الاستراحات فينزل المسافر فيه للأكل والشرب وقضاء الضرورة ،والصلاة، ولأكثر النهار حكم كله، قاصداً محلاً، وبكر في اليوم الأول وسار إلى وقت الزوال حتى بلغ المرحلة، فنزل بها للاستراحة وبات بها، ثم بكر في اليوم الثاني وسار إلى ما بعد الزوال ونزل، ثم بكّر في الثالث وسار إلى الزوال فبلغ المقصد، قال شمس الأئمة السرخسي : الصحيح أنه مسافر. [مراقي الفلاح: ٤٢١] فإذا خرج وفي الجبل إلخ أي ويعتبر السير الوسط في الجبل بما يناسبه؛ لأنه يكون صعوداً وهبوطا ومضيقاً ووعرا، فيكون مشي الإبل والأقدام فيه دون سيرهما في السهل، فإذا قطع بذلك السير مسافة ليست ببعيدة . من ابتداء اليوم ونزل بعد الزوال، احتسب به على نحو ما قدمناه يوماً، فإذا بات ثم أصبح وفعل كذلك إلى ما بعد الزوال ثم نزل، كان يوماً ثانياً، ولا يعتبر أعجل السير، وهو سير البريد، ولا أبطأ السير، وهو مشي العجلة التي تجرها الدواب، فإن الأمور أوساطها، وهو هنا سير الإبل والأقدام [مراقي الفلاح: ٤٢١] وفي البحر أي وفي البحر يعتبر اعتدال الريح على المفتى به فينظر إلى السفينة كم تسير في ثلاثة أيام ولياليها عند استواء الريح بحيث لم تكن عاصفة ولا هادئة فيجعل ذلك أصلاً، فإذا سار أكثر اليوم به كان ككله وإن كانت المسافة دون ما في السهل حاشية الطحطاوي ومراقي الفلاح: ٤٢١)
The minimum travel that changes rulings is a journey of three days, from the shortest days of the year, with moderate pace including rest stops. Moderate pace is the pace of camels and walking on land, and in mountains what is appropriate, and at sea moderate wind, i.e., the camels of the caravan. Three: this measurement for travel in which prayer is shortened, fasting is permitted, wiping more than a day and night is allowed, and sacrifice is waived. As for that which permits leaving Friday, the two Eids, congregation, and which permits supererogatory prayer on a mount and tayammum, and the recommendation of casting lots among one's wives, it is not measured by this duration. With moderate pace: if he travels quickly like a postal rider and covers what is covered by moderate pace in three days in less than that, he shortens, and similarly if he travels in an extraordinary manner. In al-Tabyin it is stated that in estimating the distance by the mentioned time, one relies on predominant probability, and certainty is not required. With rest stops: he dismounts for eating, drinking, relieving himself, and prayer, and most of the day has its ruling. Starting on the first day he travels until noon until he reaches the stage, dismounts for rest and spends the night, then starts on the second day, travels until after noon and dismounts, then starts on the third day, travels until noon and reaches the destination. Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi said: the correct view is that he is a traveler. And in the mountain: moderate pace in the mountain is what is appropriate because it has ascents, descents, narrowness and ruggedness, so walking of camels and feet there is less than on plains. So if he covers a distance not far in this pace from the beginning of the day and dismounts after noon, it is counted as a day. Then if he spends the night and does the same until after noon and dismounts, it is a second day. Neither the fastest pace (postal rider) nor the slowest pace (ox-driven cart) is considered; the best of things is their middle, which here is the pace of camels and feet. And at sea: moderate wind is relied upon for the fatwa. One looks at how far the ship travels in three days and nights when the wind is balanced, not stormy nor calm, and takes that as a basis. If it travels most of the day with that, it is like the whole day, even if the distance is less than on land.
Source pages p. 139

Commentary
This passage defines the minimum travel distance that triggers legal concessions (rukhsas). The author states that the minimum is three days' journey using the shortest days of the year, with moderate walking pace including rest stops. Moderate pace is defined as the pace of camels and foot travel on land, appropriately adjusted for mountainous terrain, and moderate wind at sea. The passage then clarifies which concessions are affected by this distance: qasr of prayer, breaking fast, wiping over khuffain for more than a day, and removal of the obligation of udhiyah. Other allowances such as leaving Jumu'ah, 'Eid, congregation, performing nafl on a mount, tayammum, and the recommendation of casting lots among wives are not conditioned on this distance. The commentary provides detailed examples for calculating the distance, including faster travel, rest stops, and specifics for mountainous and sea travel. The moderate pace is emphasized as the standard, and the estimation is based on predominant probability.

Key Terms
سفر (safar): Journey of three days with moderate pace and rest that triggers legal concessions.
قصر (qasr): Shortening of four-unit obligatory prayers to two units during travel.
سير وسط (sayr wasat): Moderate pace, the typical pace of camels and walking, used as the standard for measuring travel distance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the minimum travel distance for shortening prayer?
A) One day
B) Three days
C) Four days
D) It depends on the mode of transport

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school defines the minimum travel distance for qasr as three days' moderate travel with rest, based on the shortest days, and this distance triggers certain concessions but not all.

Travel for Disobedience: Does It Grant Concessions?
Classifies travel and states the dispute on sinful travel.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on sinful travel and identify the inter-madhhab dispute regarding the applicability of rukhsa.

Core Idea
Even sinful travel triggers rukhsa in the Hanafi school, contrary to the majority.

Travel is not monolithic in the eyes of the law. Some journeys are virtuous, some neutral, and some sinful. But does the intention behind the journey affect the legal concessions (rukhsas) granted to a traveler? This passage from Nur al-Idah lays out the three categories and alerts us to a key disagreement: while the first two types are universally accepted as causes for rukhsa, the Hanafi school uniquely extends this to sinful travel as well. Let us examine this dispute and its practical impact.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Three Types of Travel
Read the passage and list the three categories of travel mentioned: travel of obedience (e.g., Hajj, Jihad), permissible travel (e.g., trade), and sinful travel (e.g., highway robbery).
2
Classify by Agreement
Note which two categories are agreed upon by all schools as causes for rukhsa. The passage states that the first two are unanimously causes.
3
State the Hanafi Position
Identify the Hanafi stance on sinful travel: it is also a cause for rukhsa. The phrase 'indana (according to us) indicates the school's view.
4
State the Opposing Position
Identify which schools disagree (Malik, al-Shafi'i, Ahmad) and their position: sinful travel does not bring concession. Note the schools listed.
5
Determine the Practical Difference
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf: a person traveling to commit a sin may shorten prayers and break fast according to Hanafis, but not according to the other schools.
This difference directly affects a traveler's obligations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المسافر: اعلم أنّ السفر على ثلاثة أقسام سفر طاعة كالحج والجهاد وسفر مباح كالتجارة، وسفر معصية: كقطع الطريق والأولان سببان للرخصة اتفاقاً، وأما الأخير فكذلك عندنا، خلافاً لمالك والشافعي وأحمد، فإنهم قالوا : سفر المعصية لا يفيد الرخصة. [ حاشية الطحطاوي بحذف وزيادة: ٤١٩]
The traveler: Know that travel is of three types: travel of obedience like Hajj and Jihad, permissible travel like trade, and sinful travel like highway robbery. The first two are causes for concession by agreement. As for the last, it is also [a cause] according to us, contrary to Malik, al-Shafi'i, and Ahmad, for they said: sinful travel does not bring concession.
Source pages p. 139

Commentary
This passage classifies travel into three categories: obedience, permissible, and sinful. It states that all three cause rukhsa (concessions) according to the Hanafi school, while the majority of other schools (Maliki, Shafi'i, Hanbali) hold that sinful travel does not entitle the traveler to concession. The passage does not provide the Hanafi proof but establishes the difference of opinion. The practical consequence is that a person traveling to commit a sin may shorten prayers and break fast according to Hanafis, but not according to the other schools.

Key Terms
سفر طاعة (safar ta'ah): Travel for an act of obedience like Hajj or Jihad.
سفر معصية (safar ma'siyah): Travel intended for a sinful purpose, such as highway robbery.
رخصة (rukhsah): Legal concession (e.g., shortening prayer, breaking fast) granted to a traveler.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, does travel for a sinful purpose like robbery allow the traveler to shorten prayers?
A) No, because it is sinful
B) Yes, because travel itself is the cause
C) Only if the travel is long
D) It depends on the mode of travel

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school uniquely holds that sinful travel is a cause for rukhsa, unlike the majority of other schools.

Conditions for Qasr (Shortening Prayer) in the Hanafi School
Lists the conditions for qasr including intention and passing the dwellings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions for qasr in the Hanafi school and apply them to determine whether a traveler must shorten his prayer.

Core Idea
Qasr is wajib for the traveler who intends a valid journey, passes the town's dwellings and its attached outer area, and is independent in his travel ruling.

The Hanafi school holds that shortening the four-unit obligatory prayer is an obligation (wajib) for the traveler once specific conditions are fulfilled. This passage from Nur al-Idah enumerates those conditions with precise legal detail. Understanding these conditions ensures correct application of this dispensation and avoids sinful completion of the prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage begins by stating that the traveler 'shortens the four-unit obligatory prayer' (فيقصر الفرض الرباعي). The commentary clarifies that this shortening is obligatory (wajib) such that completing the four units without valid reason is sinful.
Qasr applies only to four-unit fard prayers (Zuhr, Asr, Isha). It does not apply to two- or three-unit fard (Fajr, Maghrib) nor to sunnah prayers.
2
List the three conditions for qasr
The passage mentions three conditions: (1) intention of travel (نوى السفر), (2) passing the dwellings of residence and the attached outer area (جاوز بيوت مقامه وفنائه), and (3) independence in ruling (الاستقلال بالحكم) – the traveler must not be a dependent (e.g., child) following another's travel.
These conditions must all be present for qasr to be obligatory.
3
Detail the condition of intention
The intention must be decisive (قصداً جازماً) and connected to the travel action. The passage discusses cases like starting prayer as a resident then intending travel midway (Abu Yusuf says complete as muqim), and the travel of a disobedient person (e.g., sinful journey) – even they must shorten, except if the sin is the sole purpose initially.
The intention must be formed before the prayer begins; accidental travel does not qualify.
4
Detail the condition of passing dwellings and fina'
The traveler must pass all the dwellings of his town (بيوت مقامه) and also the attached outer area (فنائه), which includes areas like grazing lands and burial grounds used for the town's needs. Even if the fina' is separated by a field or a bowshot (غلوة, ~300-400 steps), it must be passed. Passing the boundary of the town alone is not sufficient.
The fina' is considered part of the town; passing it is required. If there are separate localities historically connected to the town, they must also be passed.
5
Apply the conditions to a scenario
Consider a traveler driving from a city. He must intend a journey of travel distance, pass the last houses and the attached suburban areas (fina'), and be an independent adult (not a child or wife following). If any condition is missing, he must complete the prayer fully.
The modern equivalent of fina' includes city-limits signs and adjoining residential/commercial outskirts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فيقصر الفرض الرباعي من نوى السفر ولو كان عاصيا بسفره إذا جاوز بيوت وصلية مقامه وجاوز أيضاً ما اتصل به من فنائه، وإن انفصل الفناء بمزرعة أو قدر غلوة

فاعل يقصر
خبر
بيان لـ"ما"
لا يشترط مجاوزته، والفناء المكان المعد لمصالح البلد كركض الدواب ودفن الموتى. مبتدأ ويشترط لصحة نية السفر ثلاثة أشياء: الاستقلال بالحكم
صبي
بيوم
لا
يقصر،
فيقصر إلخ المراد وجوب القصر حتى لو أتم فإنه آثم وقيد بالفرض؛ لأنه لا قصر في الوتر والسنن، وقيد بالرباعي؛ لأنه لا قصر في الفرض الثنائي والثلاثي، فالركعات المفروضة حال الإقامة سبعة عشر، وحال السفر إحدى عشر. [البحر الرائق: ٢٠٦/٢] ، وإن كان في حال نزول وقرار وأمن يأتي بالسنن، وإن كان سائراً أو خائفاً فلا يأتي بها، وهو المختار. [مراقي الفلاح: ٤٢٢] من نوى السفر: أي قصده قصداً جازماً، ولابد من القصد قبل الصلاة، حتى لو افتتح الصلاة في السفينة حال الإقامة في طرف البحر، فنقلها الريح فنوى السفر، يتم صلاة المقيم عند أبي يوسف؛ لأنه اجتمع الموجب للإتمام وما يمنعه فرجحنا الموجب احتياطاً، والمراد القصد المعتبر، حتى لو قصد . مسافة سفر فبلغ قبل بلوغ المقصد بخلاف الكافر إذا أسلم بناءً على أن نية الكافر إنشاء السفر معتبرة بخلاف الصبي، ولا يعتبر القصد ما لم يتصل به عمل السفر، ولو لم يقصد لا يكون مسافراً ولو طاف الدنيا جميعاً، فلو قصد السياحة أو ذهب صاحب جيش لطلب عدو، أو ذهب لطلب آبق أو غريم ولم يعلم أين يدركه أتم في الذهاب وفي موضع المكث وإن طالت المدة، أما في الرجوع فإن كانت مدة سفر قصر، وإلا لا. [حاشية الطحطاوي بحذف: ٤٢٢] عاصيا بسفره : بأن سافر لطلب الزنا أو قطع الطريق، ولو طرأ عليه قصد المعصية بعد إنشاء السفر فإنه يترخص بالاتفاق. واعلم أنه يكون عاصياً بقصد فعل المعصية، سواء وجدت منه المعصية بالفعل أم لا. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٤٢٣] جاوز إلخ: أطلق في المجاوزة، فانصرفت من الجانب الذي خرج منه، ولا يعتبر مجاوزة محلة بحذائه الآخر، فإن كانت في الجانب الذي خرج منه محلة منفصلة عن المصر، وفي القديم كانت متصلة بالمصر لا يقصر الصلاة حتى يجاوز تلك المحلة [البحر الرائق ۳۰۳/۲] بيوت مقامه عبر بالجمع؛ ليفيد اشتراط مجاوزة الكل، فيدخل فيه محلة منفصلة وفي القديم كانت متصلة؛ لأنها تعدُّ من المصر. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٤٢٣] وجاوز أيضاً : أي ويشترط أن يكون قد جاوز أيضاً ما اتصل بمقامه من فنائه كما يشترط مجاوزة ربضه وهو ما حول المدينة من بيوت ومساكن، فإنه في حكم المصر، وكذا القرى المتصلة بربض المصر يشترط مجاوزتها في الصحيح. [مراقي الفلاح ٤٢٣] قدر غلوة من ثلاث مائة خطوة إلى أربع مائة. [مراقي الفلاح: ٤٢٣] الاستقلال بالحكم: أي الأنفراد بحكم نفسه بحيث لا يكون تابعا لغيره في حكمه [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٤٢٤]
من
الجانب
So he shortens the four-unit obligatory prayer, he who intends travel, even if he is disobedient in his travel, when he passes the dwellings of his residence and also passes what is attached to it of its outer area, even if the outer area is separated by a cultivated field or the distance of a bowshot. ... [Commentary continues with detailed conditions]
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling and conditions for qasr (shortening) of prayer. It states that every traveler who intends travel of the requisite distance, even if for a sinful purpose, must shorten four-unit fard prayers once he passes the dwellings of his town and its attached outer area (fina'). The commentary explains that qasr is obligatory (wajib) such that completing the prayer is sinful. It details the conditions for valid intention: decisive and connected to action, and distinguishes between an adult, a child, and a disbeliever. It also clarifies what constitutes passing the dwellings: one must pass all attached and separated localities that are considered part of the town. The fina' includes areas used for the town's needs, such as grazing and burial. The passage also discusses the case of a person who starts prayer as a resident then intends travel during prayer.

Key Terms
فناء (fina'): The outer area attached to a town, used for purposes like grazing animals and burying the dead.
غلوة (ghalwah): A bowshot, approximately 300 to 400 paces.
الاستقلال بالحكم (al-istiqlal bi al-hukm): Independence in ruling, i.e., the traveler must not be a follower in travel (e.g., a child or wife) for his own ruling to apply.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What must a traveler pass to be allowed to shorten prayer?
A) Only the last house of the town
B) The dwellings and their attached outer area (fina')
C) The city limits sign
D) The entire town including farms

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, qasr is an obligation for the independent traveler who decisively intends travel, passes the town's dwellings and its attached outer area, and does so before beginning the prayer.

Conditions for Qasr in Travel
Ruling on conditions and exceptions for qasr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions required for a valid travel intention (niyyat al-safar) and identify which travellers are exempt from qasr because they lack these conditions.

Core Idea
Qasr is wajib only when the traveller is independent, pubescent, and journeying at least three days.

This passage from Nur al-Idah outlines the key conditions that must be met for a traveller to validly shorten their prayers. Understanding these conditions ensures that the obligation of qasr is applied correctly and that one does not shorten when it is not permitted, nor complete when shortening is required.

Guided Path
1
Identify the basic act and its ruling
Qasr means shortening the four-rakat obligatory prayers to two rakats. It is required when travel is validly intended and the traveller has left the inhabited area.
2
Extract the three conditions for valid travel intention
The passage states three things are required: independence in ruling (istiqlal), puberty (bulugh), and the duration not being less than three days.
Independence means not being a dependent whose rulings follow another, like a wife or soldier.
3
Recognize the spatial condition
One must pass the built-up area of one's residence including attached open spaces (fina'), unless separated by a field or bowshot.
This applies from the direction one departs.
4
Apply the conditions to categories of people
Four groups do not shorten: those who haven't passed the inhabited area, minors, dependents without follower's travel intention, and those intending less than three days.
For dependents, if the follower intends travel, the dependent follows that intention.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فيقصر الفرض الرباعي من نوى السفر ولو كان عاصيا بسفره إذا جاوز بيوت ومقامه وجاوز أيضاً ما اتصل به من فنائه، وإن انفصل الفناء بمزرعة أو قدر غلوة. ويشترط لصحة نية السفر ثلاثة أشياء: الاستقلال بالحكم والبلوغ وعدم نقصان مدة السفر عن ثلاثة أيام، فلا يقصر من لم يجاوز عمران مقامه، أو جاوز وكان صبيا أو تابعا لم ينو متبوعه السفر كالمرأة مع زوجها والعبد مع مولاه والجندي مع أميره أو ناويا دون الثلاثة، وتعتبر نية الإقامة والسفر من الأصل دون التبع إن علم نية المتبوع في الأصح، والقصر عزيمة عندنا، فإذا أتم الرباعية وقعد كالعبد والمرأة والجندي القعود الأول صحت صلاته مع الكراهة وإلا فلا تصح إلا إذا نوى الإقامة لما قام مقدار التشهد. ولا يزال يقصر حتى يدخل مصره أو ينوي إقامته نصف شهر ببلد أو قرية.
One shortens the four-rakat obligatory (prayer) when one intends travel, even if one is disobedient in his travel, when he has passed the houses of his place of residence and also passed what is attached to it of its open space, and if the open space is separated by a cultivated field or the distance of a bowshot. And for the validity of the intention of travel three things are required: independence in ruling, puberty, and the duration of travel not being less than three days. So one does not shorten who has not passed the inhabited area of his residence, or passed but was a child or a dependent whose follower did not intend travel, like a woman with her husband, a slave with his master, a soldier with his commander, or one intending less than three (days). And the intention of residence and travel is considered from the original (follower) not the dependent when the intention of the followed is known in the most correct (view). And shortening is a determined obligation ('azimah) according to us. So if he completes the four-rakat (prayer) and sits for the first sitting like the slave, woman, and soldier, his prayer is valid with dislike (karahah). Otherwise it is not valid unless he intended residence when he stood for the amount of tashahhud. And he continues to shorten until he enters his city or intends residence for half a month in a town or village.
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This passage from Nur al-Idah covers the rulings of qasr (shortening prayers) for the traveller in the Hanafi school. It begins by stating the basic ruling: one shortens the four-rakat obligatory prayers when one has a valid intention to travel and has left the built-up area of one's residence, including attached open spaces (fina'), unless separated by a field or bowshot. The condition of passing applies from the side one departs from. Three conditions are required for a valid travel intention: independence (not being a dependent whose rulings follow another), puberty, and the intended journey being at least three days (approximately 48 miles or 77 km according to the school). Four categories of people do not shorten: (1) one who has not passed the inhabited area, (2) a child (below puberty), (3) a dependent who follows another's intention (e.g., wife, slave, soldier) unless they know their follower's intention—in which case they follow it; if the follower intends residence, they must complete prayers, even if unaware until later, though they are not required to inquire in the most correct opinion, and (4) one who intends less than three days' travel. The school holds that qasr is an 'azimah (determined obligation), not a rukhsah (concession), so intentionally completing a four-rakat prayer as a traveller is sinful. If one completes it and sits for the first sitting (tashahhud), the prayer is valid with karahah (dislike) because the extra two rakats become nafl but delay the obligatory salam. If one stands for the third rakat without sitting, the prayer is invalid unless one intended residence at that moment. Qasr continues until the traveller enters his home city or intends to stay for half a month (15 days) in any town or village; intention to stay less does not end qasr. This passage also notes that intention of residence or travel is valid only in inhabited places, not deserts or ships.

Key Terms
القصر (al-qasr): Shortening the four-rakat obligatory prayers to two rakats during travel.
الاستقلال بالحكم (al-istiqlāl bi al-ḥukm): Independence in ruling – not being a dependent whose prayer rulings follow another (e.g., wife, slave, soldier).
التابع (al-tābiʿ): A dependent who follows another in travel rulings, such as a woman with her husband or a soldier with his commander.
الفناء (al-fināʾ): The open space attached to a town used for purposes like grazing or burial.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following travellers is required to shorten (qasr) according to this passage?
A) A 12-year-old boy travelling with his father for 5 days.
B) A woman travelling with her husband who intends a 4-day journey.
C) A soldier whose commander intends a 1-day journey.
D) An adult man travelling alone for a 2-day journey.

Key Takeaway
Qasr is only valid when the traveller is independent, pubescent, and journeying at least three days.

Legal Ruling and Consequences of Qasr
Ruling on legal nature of qasr and consequences of completing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the legal nature of qasr as an 'azimah, explain the consequence of completing four rakats, and identify when the ruling of qasr ends.

Core Idea
Qasr is a determined obligation, not a concession; completing four rakats without sitting invalidates the prayer.

This part of the passage clarifies the binding nature of qasr in the Hanafi school. Unlike other schools that view it as a concession, Hanafis consider it an obligation. It also addresses what happens if a traveller mistakenly completes four rakats, and when the obligation to shorten ceases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hukm of qasr
The passage states 'al-qasr 'azimah 'indana' – shortening is a determined obligation, not a concession. Deliberately completing four rakats is sinful.
This is a key difference with the Shafi'i school.
2
Analyse the consequence of completing four rakats
If one sits for the first tashahhud after two rakats, then stands for two more, the prayer is valid but makruh (disliked) because extra rakats become nafl but delay the obligatory salam. If one stands for the third rakat without sitting, the prayer is invalid unless one intended residence at that moment.
The same ruling applies to dependents (slave, woman, soldier) as mentioned.
3
Understand the ending of qasr
The traveller continues to shorten until he enters his home city (mصر) or intends to stay for half a month (15 days) in any town or village.
Intending less than 15 days does not end qasr.
4
Note the ruling for dependents in this context
The passage mentions that the same rules apply to the examples of slave, woman, and soldier regarding completing four rakats.

Commentary
This passage from Nur al-Idah covers the rulings of qasr (shortening prayers) for the traveller in the Hanafi school. Key Terms
العزيمة (al-ʿazīmah): A determined obligation that must be performed; not a concession.
الكراهة (al-karāhah): Dislike; an act that is discouraged but not forbidden (makruh tanzihi).
الإقامة (al-iqāmah): Intention to reside; here, intending to stay for 15 days ends qasr.

Conditions for Qasr: The Four Prerequisites
Conditions for qasr and four sub-cases of non-shortening

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four conditions for qasr and identify which travelers are excluded from shortening.

Core Idea
Qasr is wajib only for a traveler who has passed the built-up area, is adult, independent, and traveling at least three days.

The Hanafi school sets four precise conditions for qasr (shortening the four-rak'a prayers to two). Missing any one of them means the traveler must pray complete four rak'as. This lesson unpacks each condition and the sub-cases where qasr is not valid, as detailed in Nur al-Idah and its commentaries.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? Qasr of four-rak'a prayers (zuhr, asr, isha) for a traveler. The ruling is that qasr is a determined obligation ('azima) when conditions are met, not a mere concession.
The text states 'al-qasr 'azimatun 'indana' – this is the Hanafi position.
2
List the four conditions
The passage explicitly gives four conditions: (1) passing beyond the built-up area of residence, (2) adulthood (bulugh), (3) independence (not being a dependent follower), (4) travel duration of at least three days.
3
Explain each condition's sub-case
For each condition, the text provides a negative case where qasr is not performed: not passing beyond, being a child, being a follower (woman with husband, slave with master, soldier with commander), or intending less than three days.
For the follower, the principal must intend travel; the follower's own intention is not considered unless he knows the principal's intention.
4
Apply the conditions to dependent travelers
Examine the examples: a woman whose husband has not paid her prompt dower is not considered a follower (according to Abu Hanifa). A mukatab slave is not a follower because he can travel without permission.
These are nuanced exceptions to the general rule of dependency.
5
Note cross-madhhab difference
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) view qasr as a rukhsa (concession), not an obligation. The Hanafi school's view is that it is a determined obligation ('azima), making it wajib.
This difference affects whether the traveler should intentionally complete four rak'as.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة
صلاة المسافر
والبلوغ وعدم نقصان مدة السفر عن ثلاثة أيام، فلا يقصر من لم يجاوز عمران مقامه، أو جاوز وكان صبيا أو تابعا لم ينو متبوعه السفر كالمرأة مع زوجها والعبد مع مولاه والجندي مع أميره أو ناويا دون الثلاثة، وتعتبر نية الإقامة والسفر من الأصل دون كالزوج والمولى والأمير التبع إن علم نية المتبوع في الأصح، والقصر عزيمة عندنا، فإذا أتم الرباعية وقعد كالعبد والمرأة والجندي القعود الأول صحت صلاته مع الكراهة وإلا فلا تصح إلا إذا نوى الإقامة لما قام مقدار التشهد أي وإن لم يجلس للثالثة، ولا يزال يقصر حتى يدخل مصره أو ينوي إقامته نصف شهر ببلد أو قرية،
المسافر
فلا يقصر : شروع في التفريعات الأربع على الشروط الأربعة من المجاوزة والاستقلال والبلوغ وعدم نقصان المدة، فعدم القصر لمن لم يجاوز العمران؛ لعدم مجاوزته، وهي شرط للقصر، وعدم القصر للصبي؛ لعدم بلوغه، وعدم القصر للتابع؛ لعدم استقلاله بالحكم، فإنه تابع لمتبوعه ولا عبرة لنيته وعدم القصر لمن نوى أقل مسافة السفر؛ لنقصان المدة. كالمرأة مع زوجها أطلقها، وهي مقيدة بما إذا أوفاها معجل مهرها، وإن لم يوفها لم تكن تبعاً له ولو دخل بها؛ لأنه يجوز لها منعه من الوطء والإخراج للمهر عند أبي حنيفة لله مراقي الفلاح بزيادة: ٤٢٤] والعبد مع إلخ أطلقه وهو مقيد بغير المكاتب، فشمل أم الولد والمدبر، وأما المكاتب فقال في "البحر" [۲۱۷/۲] : ينبغي أن لا يكون تبعاً؛ لأن له السفر بغير إذن المولى.
إن علم نية إلخ فلا يلزمه الإتمام بنية الأصل الإقامة حتى يعلم، وهل يجب عليه السؤال من المتبوع أم لا؟ والظاهر الأول. صحت صلاته أما الصحة فلوجود الفرض في محله وهو الجلوس على الركعتين، وتصير الأخريان نافلة له، وأما الكراهة فلتأخير الواجب، وهو السلام عن محله وإن كان عامداً، فإن كان ساهياً يسجد للسهو، ولترك واجب القصر، وترك افتتاح النفل، وخلطه بالفرض وكل ذلك لا يجوز وإلا فلا تصح أي وإن لم يكن قد جلس قدر التشهد على رأس الركعتين الأوليين فلا تصح صلاته؛ لتركه فرض الجلوس في محله واختلاط النفل بالفرض قبل كماله. [مراقي الفلاح: ٤٢٩]
حتى يدخل مصره أطلق في دخول مصره، فشمل ما إذا نوى الإقامة به أو لا. البحر الرائق: ٢٠٧/٢] ينوى إقامته : أطلق النية، فشمل الحكمية كما لو وصل الحاج إلى الشام وعلم أن القافلة إنما تخرج بعد خمسة عشر يوماً، وعزم أن لا يخرج إلا معهم لا يقصر؛ لأنه كناوي الإقامة وشمل ما إذا نواها في خلال الصلاة في الوقت فإنه يتم، سواء كان في أولها أو أوسطها أو في آخرها وسواء كان منفرداً أو مقتدياً أو مدركاً أو مسبوقاً، وقيد بنصف شهر؛ لأن نية إقامة ما دونها لا توجب الإتمام وقيد بالبلد والقرية؛ لأن نية الإقامة لا تصح في غيرهما، فلا تصح في مفازة ولا جزيرة ولا بحر ولا سفينة البحر الرائق ملخصاً: ٢٠٨/٢]

كتاب الصلاة
١٤١
صلاة المسافر
نعت لما قبله
وقصر إن نوى أقل منه أو لم ينو وبقي سنين، ولا تصح نية الإقامة ببلدتين لم يعين المبيت بإحداهما، ولا في مفازة لغير أهل الأخبية ولا لعسكرنا بدار الحرب، ولا بدارنا في محاصرة أهل البغي، وإن اقتدى مسافر بمقيم في الوقت صح وأتمها أربعاً، وبعده لا يصح، وبعكسه صح فيهما، وندب للإمام أن يقول : أتموا صلاتكم، فإني مسافر، بعد التسليمتين في الأصح وينبغي أن يقول ذلك قبل شروعه في الصلاة، ولا يقرأ المقيم فيما يتمه بعد فراغ إمامه المسافر في الأصح، وفائتة السفر والحضر تقضى ركعتين وأربعاً، والمعتبر فيه آخر الوقت، ويبطل الوطن الأصلي بمثله فقط، ويبطل وطن الإقامة بمثله وبالسفر وبالأصلي،
هم لا يصير أهل الأخبية: الأعراب والترك والكرد الذين يسكنون المفازة، وقيد بهم؛ لأن غيرهم لو نوى الإقامة معهم مقيماً عند الإمام، وهو الصحيح. [حاشية الطحطاوي ملخصاً: ٤٢٦] ولا لعسكرنا إلخ: أي ولا تصح نية الإقامة لعسكرنا في دار الحرب ولو حاصروا مصراً؛ لمخالفة حالهم بالتردد بين القرار والفرار. [مراقي الفلاح: ٤٢٦] أما من دخلها بأمان ونوى الإقامة في موضعها، صحت ويتم [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٤٢٦] ولا بدارنا أي ولا تصح نية الإقامة لعسكرنا في دارنا حال كونهم محاصرين أهل البغي والبغاة: قوم خرجوا عن طاعة الإمام الحق ظانين أنهم على الحق، ولا يحكم بفسقهم بالاتفاق؛ لأنهم متمسكون بشبهة وإن كانت فاسدة، فإن لم تكن لهم شبهة فهم لصوص [ حاشية الطحطاوي ومراقي الفلاح ٤٢٦] وبعده لا يصح: أي بعد خروج الوقت لا يصح اقتداء المسافر بالمقيم. تبيين الحقائق: ٥١٥/١] وبعكسه صح إلخ أي بعكس ما ذكره من اقتداء المسافر بالمقيم جائز في الوقت، وبعده، وهو اقتداء المقيم بالمسافر [تبيين الحقائق: ٥١٦/١] ولا يقرأ المقيم إلخ أي إذا صلى المقيم خلف مسافر وفرغ الإمام المسافر عن صلاته، يقوم المؤتم ويؤدّي ما بقي من صلاته، ولكنه لا يقرأ خلفه في الأصح وقال بعض المشايخ يقرأ كالمسبوق. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٤٢٨] وفائتة السفر والحضر إلخ فيه لف ونشر أي فائتة السفر تقضى ركعتين، وفائتة الحضر تقضى أربعاً. تبيين الحقائق: ٥١٦/١] والمعتبر إلخ أي المعتبر في وجوب الأربع أو الركعتين آخر الوقت، فإن كان آخر الوقت مسافراً وجب عليه ركعتان، وإن كان مقيماً وجب عليه الأربع. [تبيين الحقائق: ٥١٩/١] ويبطل إلخ : أي يبطل الوطن الأصلي بالوطن الأصلي، هذا إذا انتقل عن الأول بأهله، وأما إذا لم ينتقل بأهله ولكنه استحدث أهلاً ببلدة أخرى فلا يبطل وطنه الأول ويتم، وقوله: "فقط" أي لا بإنشاء السفر ولا بوطن الإقامة، وكلاهما لا يبطل به الأصلي، وقوله: "وطن الإقامة بمثله" أي يبطل وطن الإقامة بوطن الإقامة :
Book of Prayer: Prayer of the Traveler. And maturity and that the duration of travel is not less than three days. So one who has not passed the built-up area of his residence does not shorten, nor one who has passed but is a child or a dependent whose principal did not intend travel, like a woman with her husband, a slave with his master, a soldier with his commander, or one intending less than three days. And the intention of residence and travel is considered from the original without... like the husband, master, and commander, the follower if he knows the intention of the principal in the most correct view. And shortening is a determined obligation with us. So if he completes the four-rak'a prayer and sits the first sitting like the slave, woman, and soldier, his prayer is valid but disliked. Otherwise it is not valid unless he intended residence when he stood for the amount of tashahhud, even if he did not sit for the third. And he continues shortening until he enters his city or intends residence for half a month in a town or village. The traveler: He does not shorten: beginning of the four sub-cases on the four conditions: passing beyond, independence, puberty, and sufficiency of duration. So no shortening for one who has not passed the built-up area because he has not passed beyond, which is a condition for shortening. And no shortening for a child because he has not reached puberty. And no shortening for a follower because he is not independent in ruling, for he is a follower of his principal and his intention is not considered. And no shortening for one who intends less than the travel distance because of insufficiency of duration. Like a woman with her husband - he mentioned it absolutely, and it is restricted to when he has paid her prompt dower; if he has not paid her, she is not his follower even if he has consummated, because it is permissible for her to prevent him from intercourse for the dower according to Abu Hanifa - [reference]. And the slave etc. he mentioned absolutely, and it is restricted to non-mukatab, so it includes umm walad and mudabbar. As for the mukatab, it is said in 'al-Bahr' that he should not be a follower because he can travel without the master's permission. If he knows the intention etc.: he is not obliged to complete because of the principal's intention of residence until he knows. And is he obliged to ask his principal? The apparent is the first. His prayer is valid: as for validity, because the obligatory act exists in its place, which is sitting after two rak'as, and the other two become supererogatory for him. As for the dislike, because of delaying an obligatory duty, which is the salutation from its place, even if intentional; if forgetful, he performs the prostration of forgetfulness, and for leaving the obligatory shortening, and leaving the beginning of the supererogatory, and mixing it with the obligatory - all that is not permissible. Otherwise it is not valid: i.e., if he did not sit for the amount of tashahhud at the end of the first two rak'as, his prayer is not valid, because he left the obligatory sitting in its place and mixed the supererogatory with the obligatory before its completion. [Maraqi al-Falah: 429] Until he enters his city: he used the absolute term for entering his city, so it includes whether he intended residence there or not. [al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 2/207] He intends his residence: he used the absolute term for intention, so it includes implicit intention, as if a pilgrim arrives in Sham and knows that the caravan leaves only after fifteen days, and he resolves not to leave except with them, he does not shorten because he is like one intending residence. And it includes if he intends it during the prayer while in time, then he completes, whether at the beginning, middle, or end of his prayer, and whether he is alone, following, catching up, or lagging behind. And it is restricted to half a month because intending residence for less does not necessitate completion. And it is restricted to town and village because intention of residence is not valid elsewhere, so it is not valid in a desert, island, sea, or ship. [al-Bahr al-Ra'iq summarized: 2/208] Book of Prayer: page 141. Prayer of the Traveler. Description of what preceded. And he shortens if he intends less than that or does not intend and remains for years. And intention of residence in two towns without specifying overnight stay in one is not valid. Nor in a desert for non-tent dwellers, nor for our army in dar al-harb, nor in our dar while besieging rebels. And if a traveler follows a resident in time, it is valid and he completes four rak'as. After time, it is not valid. And the opposite is valid in both. And it is recommended for the imam to say: 'Complete your prayer, for I am a traveler' after the two taslims in the most correct view. And he should say that before beginning the prayer. And the resident does not recite in what he completes after his traveler imam finishes in the most correct view. And missed prayer of travel and residence are made up as two and four rak'as respectively. And consideration is for the end of time. And the original homeland is nullified only by another original homeland. And the residence homeland is nullified by another residence homeland, by travel, and by the original homeland. They do not become... Tent dwellers: bedouins, Turks, and Kurds who live in the desert. And it is restricted to them because if others intend residence with them, they become residents according to the Imam, and that is the correct view. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi summarized: 426] Nor for our army etc.: i.e., intention of residence is not valid for our army in dar al-harb even if they besiege a city, because their situation is contrary due to fluctuation between staying and fleeing. [Maraqi al-Falah: 426] As for one who enters with aman and intends residence in its place, it is valid and he completes. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 426] Nor in our dar: i.e., intention of residence is not valid for our army in our dar while they are besieging rebels. And rebels are a people who have left obedience to the rightful imam thinking they are right, and they are not judged as sinners by consensus because they adhere to a doubt even if corrupt. If they have no doubt, they are thieves. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi and Maraqi al-Falah: 426] And after it is not valid: i.e., after the time is out, a traveler following a resident is not valid. [Tabyin al-Haqa'iq: 1/515] And the opposite is valid etc.: i.e., the opposite of what he mentioned - a traveler following a resident is permissible in time and after, which is a resident following a traveler. [Tabyin al-Haqa'iq: 1/516] And the resident does not recite etc.: i.e., if a resident prays behind a traveler and the traveler imam finishes his prayer, the follower stands and performs what remains of his prayer, but he does not recite behind him in the most correct view. And some shaykhs said he recites like a latecomer. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 428] And missed prayer of travel and residence etc.: It contains a chiasm: i.e., missed prayer of travel is made up as two rak'as, and missed prayer of residence as four. [Tabyin al-Haqa'iq: 1/516] And the consideration etc.: i.e., what is considered in the obligation of four or two is the end of time: if at the end of time he is a traveler, two rak'as are obligatory; if a resident, four are obligatory. [Tabyin al-Haqa'iq: 1/519] And it is nullified etc.: i.e., the original homeland is nullified by another original homeland. This is if he moves from the first with his family. If he does not move with his family but acquires a family in another town, his first homeland is not nullified and he completes. And his saying 'only' means not by initiating travel nor by a residence homeland, and both do not nullify the original. And his saying 'the residence homeland by its like' means the residence homeland is nullified by another residence homeland.
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage from Nur al-Idah, with commentary from Maraqi al-Falah, al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, Tabyin al-Haqa'iq, and Hashiyat al-Tahtawi, explains the detailed rules of qasr (shortening prayer) for a traveler in the Hanafi school. The passage begins by listing the conditions for qasr: the traveler must have passed beyond the built-up area of his residence, be an adult (baligh), be independent (not a follower whose principal did not intend travel), and the travel duration must be at least three days (approximately 48 miles or 78 km). The text then elaborates on four sub-cases where qasr is not valid: not passing beyond the built-up area, being a child, being a dependent (like a woman with husband, slave with master, soldier with commander), or intending a distance less than the travel duration. It clarifies that a follower is required to know the principal's intention of travel; otherwise, he does not shorten. The ruling emphasizes that qasr is a determined obligation ('azima), not a concession (rukhsa) in the Hanafi school. If a traveler completes four rak'as while intending qasr, his prayer is valid but disliked (makruh), as he delayed the obligatory sitting after two rak'as and mixed supererogatory with obligatory. If he fails to sit after two rak'as, the prayer is invalid. The traveler continues shortening until he enters his city (even if he does not intend residence) or intends residence for fifteen days in a town or village. Intention of residence for less does not require completion. The text also covers the validity of following: a traveler following a resident in time is valid, and the traveler completes four rak'as; after time it is invalid. The opposite (resident following traveler) is valid in both. It recommends the traveler imam to inform the congregation to complete their prayer. It also discusses missed prayers: a missed travel prayer is made up as two rak'as, and a missed resident prayer as four, with consideration given to the end of the time. Finally, it addresses nullification of homelands: the original homeland is nullified only by another original homeland, while the residence homeland is nullified by another residence homeland, by travel, and by the original homeland. The commentary explains that tent dwellers (bedouins, Turks, Kurds) are a special case for intention of residence in the desert. This passage is foundational for understanding the Hanafi rules of traveler's prayer.

Key Terms
قصر (qasr): Shortening the four-rak'a prayers (zuhr, asr, isha) to two rak'as while traveling.
مسافر (musafir): A person traveling a distance of three days (approximately 78 km) who has passed the built-up area of his residence.
نية الإقامة (niyyat al-iqama): Intention to stay in a place for fifteen days or more, which obligates the traveler to complete prayers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a condition for qasr according to the Hanafi school?
A) The traveler must have passed the built-up area of his residence.
B) The traveler must be an adult (baligh).
C) The traveler must be traveling alone and not with a group.
D) The travel duration must be at least three days.

Key Takeaway
Only travelers who meet all four conditions – passing beyond built-up area, adulthood, independence, and three-day travel – are obliged to shorten prayer.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Qasr as 'Azima: Ruling on Completing Four Rak'as
Ruling on traveler completing four rak'as, with and without first sitting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on a traveler who completes four rak'as and distinguish between valid-with-dislike and invalid scenarios.

Core Idea
Completing four rak'as while qasr is wajib: valid but makruh if the first sitting is done; invalid if the first sitting is omitted.

The previous lesson established that qasr is wajib. But what if a traveler forgets or intentionally prays four rak'as? The Hanafi school gives a nuanced ruling based on whether the traveler sits after the first two rak'as. This lesson unpacks that ruling and its rationale, drawing from the source passage and its commentary.

Guided Path
1
Recall the hukm of qasr
Qasr is a determined obligation ('azima). The traveler is required to pray two rak'as instead of four for zuhr, asr, and isha.
2
Identify the act being ruled: completing four rak'as
The passage addresses a traveler who, instead of shortening, prays the full four rak'as. The ruling depends on whether he sits after the first two rak'as (i.e., performs the first tashahhud).
The first sitting is a rukn in Hanafi prayer; the second sitting is also a rukn but the first is specifically for the traveler's case.
3
Analyze the first scenario: with first sitting
If the traveler sits for the first tashahhud (qada al-ula) after two rak'as, his prayer is valid (sahih) but disliked (makruh). Validity because the obligatory sitting was performed; dislike for delaying the wajib of shortening and mixing supererogatory (the extra two rak'as) with obligatory.
The extra two rak'as become nafil (supererogatory) for him.
4
Analyze the second scenario: without first sitting
If he does not sit after two rak'as and instead stands directly for the third, the prayer is invalid (la tasihh). Reason: he left the obligatory sitting (qada al-ula) which is a rukn, and the extra two rak'as are now mixed with the fard before its completion.
This is a clearer case of violation.
5
Apply the ruling to the follower cases (slave, woman, soldier)
The text specifically mentions that if a dependent traveler (like a woman with husband, slave, soldier) completes four rak'as and sits the first sitting, the same ruling applies: valid but makruh. The dependency does not affect this aspect.
This shows the ruling is general for all travelers who meet the conditions.

Source Text

كتاب الصلاة
صلاة المسافر
والبلوغ وعدم نقصان مدة السفر عن ثلاثة أيام، فلا يقصر من لم يجاوز عمران مقامه، أو جاوز وكان صبيا أو تابعا لم ينو متبوعه السفر كالمرأة مع زوجها والعبد مع مولاه والجندي مع أميره أو ناويا دون الثلاثة، وتعتبر نية الإقامة والسفر من الأصل دون كالزوج والمولى والأمير التبع إن علم نية المتبوع في الأصح، والقصر عزيمة عندنا، فإذا أتم الرباعية وقعد كالعبد والمرأة والجندي القعود الأول صحت صلاته مع الكراهة وإلا فلا تصح إلا إذا نوى الإقامة لما قام مقدار التشهد أي وإن لم يجلس للثالثة، ولا يزال يقصر حتى يدخل مصره أو ينوي إقامته نصف شهر ببلد أو قرية،
المسافر
فلا يقصر : شروع في التفريعات الأربع على الشروط الأربعة من المجاوزة والاستقلال والبلوغ وعدم نقصان المدة، فعدم القصر لمن لم يجاوز العمران؛ لعدم مجاوزته، وهي شرط للقصر، وعدم القصر للصبي؛ لعدم بلوغه، وعدم القصر للتابع؛ لعدم استقلاله بالحكم، فإنه تابع لمتبوعه ولا عبرة لنيته وعدم القصر لمن نوى أقل مسافة السفر؛ لنقصان المدة. كالمرأة مع زوجها أطلقها، وهي مقيدة بما إذا أوفاها معجل مهرها، وإن لم يوفها لم تكن تبعاً له ولو دخل بها؛ لأنه يجوز لها منعه من الوطء والإخراج للمهر عند أبي حنيفة لله مراقي الفلاح بزيادة: ٤٢٤] والعبد مع إلخ أطلقه وهو مقيد بغير المكاتب، فشمل أم الولد والمدبر، وأما المكاتب فقال في "البحر" [۲۱۷/۲] : ينبغي أن لا يكون تبعاً؛ لأن له السفر بغير إذن المولى.
إن علم نية إلخ فلا يلزمه الإتمام بنية الأصل الإقامة حتى يعلم، وهل يجب عليه السؤال من المتبوع أم لا؟ والظاهر الأول. صحت صلاته أما الصحة فلوجود الفرض في محله وهو الجلوس على الركعتين، وتصير الأخريان نافلة له، وأما الكراهة فلتأخير الواجب، وهو السلام عن محله وإن كان عامداً، فإن كان ساهياً يسجد للسهو، ولترك واجب القصر، وترك افتتاح النفل، وخلطه بالفرض وكل ذلك لا يجوز وإلا فلا تصح أي وإن لم يكن قد جلس قدر التشهد على رأس الركعتين الأوليين فلا تصح صلاته؛ لتركه فرض الجلوس في محله واختلاط النفل بالفرض قبل كماله. [مراقي الفلاح: ٤٢٩]
حتى يدخل مصره أطلق في دخول مصره، فشمل ما إذا نوى الإقامة به أو لا. البحر الرائق: ٢٠٧/٢] ينوى إقامته : أطلق النية، فشمل الحكمية كما لو وصل الحاج إلى الشام وعلم أن القافلة إنما تخرج بعد خمسة عشر يوماً، وعزم أن لا يخرج إلا معهم لا يقصر؛ لأنه كناوي الإقامة وشمل ما إذا نواها في خلال الصلاة في الوقت فإنه يتم، سواء كان في أولها أو أوسطها أو في آخرها وسواء كان منفرداً أو مقتدياً أو مدركاً أو مسبوقاً، وقيد بنصف شهر؛ لأن نية إقامة ما دونها لا توجب الإتمام وقيد بالبلد والقرية؛ لأن نية الإقامة لا تصح في غيرهما، فلا تصح في مفازة ولا جزيرة ولا بحر ولا سفينة البحر الرائق ملخصاً: ٢٠٨/٢]

نعت لما قبله
وقصر إن نوى أقل منه أو لم ينو وبقي سنين، ولا تصح نية الإقامة ببلدتين لم يعين المبيت بإحداهما، ولا في مفازة لغير أهل الأخبية ولا لعسكرنا بدار الحرب، ولا بدارنا في محاصرة أهل البغي، وإن اقتدى مسافر بمقيم في الوقت صح وأتمها أربعاً، وبعده لا يصح، وبعكسه صح فيهما، وندب للإمام أن يقول : أتموا صلاتكم، فإني مسافر، بعد التسليمتين في الأصح وينبغي أن يقول ذلك قبل شروعه في الصلاة، ولا يقرأ المقيم فيما يتمه بعد فراغ إمامه المسافر في الأصح، وفائتة السفر والحضر تقضى ركعتين وأربعاً، والمعتبر فيه آخر الوقت، ويبطل الوطن الأصلي بمثله فقط، ويبطل وطن الإقامة بمثله وبالسفر وبالأصلي،
هم لا يصير أهل الأخبية: الأعراب والترك والكرد الذين يسكنون المفازة، وقيد بهم؛ لأن غيرهم لو نوى الإقامة معهم مقيماً عند الإمام، وهو الصحيح. [حاشية الطحطاوي ملخصاً: ٤٢٦] ولا لعسكرنا إلخ: أي ولا تصح نية الإقامة لعسكرنا في دار الحرب ولو حاصروا مصراً؛ لمخالفة حالهم بالتردد بين القرار والفرار. [مراقي الفلاح: ٤٢٦] أما من دخلها بأمان ونوى الإقامة في موضعها، صحت ويتم [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٤٢٦] ولا بدارنا أي ولا تصح نية الإقامة لعسكرنا في دارنا حال كونهم محاصرين أهل البغي والبغاة: قوم خرجوا عن طاعة الإمام الحق ظانين أنهم على الحق، ولا يحكم بفسقهم بالاتفاق؛ لأنهم متمسكون بشبهة وإن كانت فاسدة، فإن لم تكن لهم شبهة فهم لصوص [ حاشية الطحطاوي ومراقي الفلاح ٤٢٦] وبعده لا يصح: أي بعد خروج الوقت لا يصح اقتداء المسافر بالمقيم. تبيين الحقائق: ٥١٥/١] وبعكسه صح إلخ أي بعكس ما ذكره من اقتداء المسافر بالمقيم جائز في الوقت، وبعده، وهو اقتداء المقيم بالمسافر [تبيين الحقائق: ٥١٦/١] ولا يقرأ المقيم إلخ أي إذا صلى المقيم خلف مسافر وفرغ الإمام المسافر عن صلاته، يقوم المؤتم ويؤدّي ما بقي من صلاته، ولكنه لا يقرأ خلفه في الأصح وقال بعض المشايخ يقرأ كالمسبوق. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٤٢٨] وفائتة السفر والحضر إلخ فيه لف ونشر أي فائتة السفر تقضى ركعتين، وفائتة الحضر تقضى أربعاً. تبيين الحقائق: ٥١٦/١] والمعتبر إلخ أي المعتبر في وجوب الأربع أو الركعتين آخر الوقت، فإن كان آخر الوقت مسافراً وجب عليه ركعتان، وإن كان مقيماً وجب عليه الأربع. [تبيين الحقائق: ٥١٩/١] ويبطل إلخ : أي يبطل الوطن الأصلي بالوطن الأصلي، هذا إذا انتقل عن الأول بأهله، وأما إذا لم ينتقل بأهله ولكنه استحدث أهلاً ببلدة أخرى فلا يبطل وطنه الأول ويتم، وقوله: "فقط" أي لا بإنشاء السفر ولا بوطن الإقامة، وكلاهما لا يبطل به الأصلي، وقوله: "وطن الإقامة بمثله" أي يبطل وطن الإقامة بوطن الإقامة :
Book of Prayer: Prayer of the Traveler. And maturity and that the duration of travel is not less than three days. So one who has not passed the built-up area of his residence does not shorten, nor one who has passed but is a child or a dependent whose principal did not intend travel, like a woman with her husband, a slave with his master, a soldier with his commander, or one intending less than three days. And the intention of residence and travel is considered from the original without... like the husband, master, and commander, the follower if he knows the intention of the principal in the most correct view. And shortening is a determined obligation with us. So if he completes the four-rak'a prayer and sits the first sitting like the slave, woman, and soldier, his prayer is valid but disliked. Otherwise it is not valid unless he intended residence when he stood for the amount of tashahhud, even if he did not sit for the third. And he continues shortening until he enters his city or intends residence for half a month in a town or village. The traveler: He does not shorten: beginning of the four sub-cases on the four conditions: passing beyond, independence, puberty, and sufficiency of duration. So no shortening for one who has not passed the built-up area because he has not passed beyond, which is a condition for shortening. And no shortening for a child because he has not reached puberty. And no shortening for a follower because he is not independent in ruling, for he is a follower of his principal and his intention is not considered. And no shortening for one who intends less than the travel distance because of insufficiency of duration. Like a woman with her husband - he mentioned it absolutely, and it is restricted to when he has paid her prompt dower; if he has not paid her, she is not his follower even if he has consummated, because it is permissible for her to prevent him from intercourse for the dower according to Abu Hanifa - [reference]. As for the mukatab, it is said in 'al-Bahr' that he should not be a follower because he can travel without the master's permission. His prayer is valid: as for validity, because the obligatory act exists in its place, which is sitting after two rak'as, and the other two become supererogatory for him. As for the dislike, because of delaying an obligatory duty, which is the salutation from its place, even if intentional; if forgetful, he performs the prostration of forgetfulness, and for leaving the obligatory shortening, and leaving the beginning of the supererogatory, and mixing it with the obligatory - all that is not permissible. Otherwise it is not valid: i.e., if he did not sit for the amount of tashahhud at the end of the first two rak'as, his prayer is not valid, because he left the obligatory sitting in its place and mixed the supererogatory with the obligatory before its completion. [Maraqi al-Falah: 429] Until he enters his city: he used the absolute term for entering his city, so it includes whether he intended residence there or not. [al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 2/207] He intends his residence: he used the absolute term for intention, so it includes implicit intention, as if a pilgrim arrives in Sham and knows that the caravan leaves only after fifteen days, and he resolves not to leave except with them, he does not shorten because he is like one intending residence. And it includes if he intends it during the prayer while in time, then he completes, whether at the beginning, middle, or end of his prayer, and whether he is alone, following, catching up, or lagging behind. And it is restricted to half a month because intending residence for less does not necessitate completion. And it is restricted to town and village because intention of residence is not valid elsewhere, so it is not valid in a desert, island, sea, or ship. [al-Bahr al-Ra'iq summarized: 2/208] Book of Prayer: page 141. Prayer of the Traveler. Description of what preceded. And he shortens if he intends less than that or does not intend and remains for years. And intention of residence in two towns without specifying overnight stay in one is not valid. Nor in a desert for non-tent dwellers, nor for our army in dar al-harb, nor in our dar while besieging rebels. And if a traveler follows a resident in time, it is valid and he completes four rak'as. [Maraqi al-Falah: 426] As for one who enters with aman and intends residence in its place, it is valid and he completes. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 426] Nor in our dar: i.e., intention of residence is not valid for our army in our dar while they are besieging rebels. And rebels are a people who have left obedience to the rightful imam thinking they are right, and they are not judged as sinners by consensus because they adhere to a doubt even if corrupt. If they have no doubt, they are thieves. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi and Maraqi al-Falah: 426] And after it is not valid: i.e., after the time is out, a traveler following a resident is not valid. [Tabyin al-Haqa'iq: 1/515] And the opposite is valid etc.: i.e., the opposite of what he mentioned - a traveler following a resident is permissible in time and after, which is a resident following a traveler. [Tabyin al-Haqa'iq: 1/516] And the resident does not recite etc.: i.e., if a resident prays behind a traveler and the traveler imam finishes his prayer, the follower stands and performs what remains of his prayer, but he does not recite behind him in the most correct view. And some shaykhs said he recites like a latecomer. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 428] And missed prayer of travel and residence etc.: It contains a chiasm: i.e., missed prayer of travel is made up as two rak'as, and missed prayer of residence as four. [Tabyin al-Haqa'iq: 1/516] And the consideration etc.: i.e., what is considered in the obligation of four or two is the end of time: if at the end of time he is a traveler, two rak'as are obligatory; if a resident, four are obligatory. [Tabyin al-Haqa'iq: 1/519] And it is nullified etc.: i.e., the original homeland is nullified by another original homeland. This is if he moves from the first with his family. If he does not move with his family but acquires a family in another town, his first homeland is not nullified and he completes. And his saying 'only' means not by initiating travel nor by a residence homeland, and both do not nullify the original. And his saying 'the residence homeland by its like' means the residence homeland is nullified by another residence homeland.
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage from Nur al-Idah, with commentary from Maraqi al-Falah, al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, Tabyin al-Haqa'iq, and Hashiyat al-Tahtawi, explains the detailed rules of qasr (shortening prayer) for a traveler in the Hanafi school. The passage begins by listing the conditions for qasr: the traveler must have passed beyond the built-up area of his residence, be an adult (baligh), be independent (not a follower whose principal did not intend travel), and the travel duration must be at least three days (approximately 48 miles or 78 km). The text then elaborates on four sub-cases where qasr is not valid: not passing beyond the built-up area, being a child, being a dependent (like a woman with husband, slave with master, soldier with commander), or intending a distance less than the travel duration. It clarifies that a follower is required to know the principal's intention of travel; otherwise, he does not shorten. The ruling emphasizes that qasr is a determined obligation ('azima), not a concession (rukhsa) in the Hanafi school. If a traveler completes four rak'as while intending qasr, his prayer is valid but disliked (makruh), as he delayed the obligatory sitting after two rak'as and mixed supererogatory with obligatory. If he fails to sit after two rak'as, the prayer is invalid. The traveler continues shortening until he enters his city (even if he does not intend residence) or intends residence for fifteen days in a town or village. Intention of residence for less does not require completion. The text also covers the validity of following: a traveler following a resident in time is valid, and the traveler completes four rak'as; after time it is invalid. The opposite (resident following traveler) is valid in both. It recommends the traveler imam to inform the congregation to complete their prayer. It also discusses missed prayers: a missed travel prayer is made up as two rak'as, and a missed resident prayer as four, with consideration given to the end of the time. Finally, it addresses nullification of homelands: the original homeland is nullified only by another original homeland, while the residence homeland is nullified by another residence homeland, by travel, and by the original homeland. The commentary explains that tent dwellers (bedouins, Turks, Kurds) are a special case for intention of residence in the desert. This passage is foundational for understanding the Hanafi rules of traveler's prayer.

Key Terms
قصر (qasr): Shortening the four-rak'a prayers (zuhr, asr, isha) to two rak'as while traveling.
مسافر (musafir): A person traveling a distance of three days (approximately 78 km) who has passed the built-up area of his residence.
نية الإقامة (niyyat al-iqama): Intention to stay in a place for fifteen days or more, which obligates the traveler to complete prayers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a traveler completes four rak'as of zuhr and sits for the first tashahhud, what is the ruling?
A) The prayer is invalid because he did not shorten.
B) The prayer is valid but disliked (makruh).
C) The prayer is valid and recommended (sunnah).
D) The prayer is invalid because he needed to sit again after the fourth.

Key Takeaway
A traveler who completes four rak'as with the first sitting has a valid but disliked prayer; without the first sitting, the prayer is invalid.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
12 min
Ending Qasr: Intention of Residence and Following Rules
Termination of qasr, intention of residence rules, and following between traveler and resident

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain when a traveler must stop shortening (entering city or intending fifteen days) and state the rules for a traveler following a resident imam and vice versa.

Core Idea
Shortening ends upon entering one's city or intending residence for fifteen days; a traveler following a resident in time completes four rak'as.

Qasr does not last forever. The Hanafi school defines clear boundaries: the traveler continues shortening until he enters his city (migr) or intends to stay in a town/village for fifteen days. Additionally, congregational prayer between travelers and residents follows specific rules. This lesson covers these termination points and the rules of following (iqtida'), along with related topics from the passage.

Guided Path
1
Identify when qasr ends
Two scenarios: (1) entering one's original city (migr), even without intention to stay; (2) intending residence (niyyat al-iqama) for fifteen days in a town or village. The intention can be explicit or implicit (e.g., knowing a caravan leaves after 15 days).
Intentions for less than 15 days do not end qasr; one continues shortening even if staying years, as long as no residence intention.
2
Understand the conditions for valid intention of residence
The intention must be for a settled place (town or village); not valid in desert, island, sea, or ship for non-tent dwellers. For army in dar al-harb or besieging rebels, intention is not valid due to unstable situation.
Tent dwellers (ahl al-akhbiya) like bedouins can have valid intention in the desert.
3
Examine the rules of following: traveler following resident
If a traveler follows a resident imam within the prayer time, the traveler must complete four rak'as (because the imam's prayer is full). After time, it is not valid. This is because the traveler's obligation changes by following a resident.
The traveler's intention to shorten is overridden by following a resident.
4
Examine the opposite: resident following traveler
A resident may follow a traveler imam at any time (in or out of time). The imam will pray two rak'as, and after the imam's taslim, the resident completes the remaining two rak'as silently.
It is recommended for the traveler imam to announce 'Complete your prayer, for I am a traveler'.
5
Note the rulings on missed prayers and homeland nullification
Missed travel prayers are made up as two rak'as; missed resident prayers as four, based on the situation at the end of the prayer time. The original homeland is only nullified by another original homeland (moving with family); residence homeland is nullified by another residence, travel, or original homeland.
These rules affect future qasr.

صلاة المسافر
والبلوغ وعدم نقصان مدة السفر عن ثلاثة أيام، فلا يقصر من لم يجاوز عمران مقامه، أو جاوز وكان صبيا أو تابعا لم ينو متبوعه السفر كالمرأة مع زوجها والعبد مع مولاه والجندي مع أميره أو ناويا دون الثلاثة، وتعتبر نية الإقامة والسفر من الأصل دون كالزوج والمولى والأمير التبع إن علم نية المتبوع في الأصح، والقصر عزيمة عندنا، فإذا أتم الرباعية وقعد كالعبد والمرأة والجندي القعود الأول صحت صلاته مع الكراهة وإلا فلا تصح إلا إذا نوى الإقامة لما قام مقدار التشهد أي وإن لم يجلس للثالثة، ولا يزال يقصر حتى يدخل مصره أو ينوي إقامته نصف شهر ببلد أو قرية،
المسافر
فلا يقصر : شروع في التفريعات الأربع على الشروط الأربعة من المجاوزة والاستقلال والبلوغ وعدم نقصان المدة، فعدم القصر لمن لم يجاوز العمران؛ لعدم مجاوزته، وهي شرط للقصر، وعدم القصر للصبي؛ لعدم بلوغه، وعدم القصر للتابع؛ لعدم استقلاله بالحكم، فإنه تابع لمتبوعه ولا عبرة لنيته وعدم القصر لمن نوى أقل مسافة السفر؛ لنقصان المدة. كالمرأة مع زوجها أطلقها، وهي مقيدة بما إذا أوفاها معجل مهرها، وإن لم يوفها لم تكن تبعاً له ولو دخل بها؛ لأنه يجوز لها منعه من الوطء والإخراج للمهر عند أبي حنيفة لله مراقي الفلاح بزيادة: ٤٢٤] والعبد مع إلخ أطلقه وهو مقيد بغير المكاتب، فشمل أم الولد والمدبر، وأما المكاتب فقال في "البحر" [۲۱۷/۲] : ينبغي أن لا يكون تبعاً؛ لأن له السفر بغير إذن المولى.
إن علم نية إلخ فلا يلزمه الإتمام بنية الأصل الإقامة حتى يعلم، وهل يجب عليه السؤال من المتبوع أم لا؟ والظاهر الأول. صحت صلاته أما الصحة فلوجود الفرض في محله وهو الجلوس على الركعتين، وتصير الأخريان نافلة له، وأما الكراهة فلتأخير الواجب، وهو السلام عن محله وإن كان عامداً، فإن كان ساهياً يسجد للسهو، ولترك واجب القصر، وترك افتتاح النفل، وخلطه بالفرض وكل ذلك لا يجوز وإلا فلا تصح أي وإن لم يكن قد جلس قدر التشهد على رأس الركعتين الأوليين فلا تصح صلاته؛ لتركه فرض الجلوس في محله واختلاط النفل بالفرض قبل كماله. [مراقي الفلاح: ٤٢٩]
حتى يدخل مصره أطلق في دخول مصره، فشمل ما إذا نوى الإقامة به أو لا. البحر الرائق: ٢٠٧/٢] ينوى إقامته : أطلق النية، فشمل الحكمية كما لو وصل الحاج إلى الشام وعلم أن القافلة إنما تخرج بعد خمسة عشر يوماً، وعزم أن لا يخرج إلا معهم لا يقصر؛ لأنه كناوي الإقامة وشمل ما إذا نواها في خلال الصلاة في الوقت فإنه يتم، سواء كان في أولها أو أوسطها أو في آخرها وسواء كان منفرداً أو مقتدياً أو مدركاً أو مسبوقاً، وقيد بنصف شهر؛ لأن نية إقامة ما دونها لا توجب الإتمام وقيد بالبلد والقرية؛ لأن نية الإقامة لا تصح في غيرهما، فلا تصح في مفازة ولا جزيرة ولا بحر ولا سفينة البحر الرائق ملخصاً: ٢٠٨/٢]
