١٤١
صلاة المسافر
نعت لما قبله
وقصر إن نوى أقل منه أو لم ينو وبقي سنين، ولا تصح نية الإقامة ببلدتين لم يعين المبيت بإحداهما، ولا في مفازة لغير أهل الأخبية ولا لعسكرنا بدار الحرب، ولا بدارنا في محاصرة أهل البغي، وإن اقتدى مسافر بمقيم في الوقت صح وأتمها أربعاً، وبعده لا يصح، وبعكسه صح فيهما، وندب للإمام أن يقول : أتموا صلاتكم، فإني مسافر، بعد التسليمتين في الأصح وينبغي أن يقول ذلك قبل شروعه في الصلاة، ولا يقرأ المقيم فيما يتمه بعد فراغ إمامه المسافر في الأصح، وفائتة السفر والحضر تقضى ركعتين وأربعاً، والمعتبر فيه آخر الوقت، ويبطل الوطن الأصلي بمثله فقط، ويبطل وطن الإقامة بمثله وبالسفر وبالأصلي،
هم لا يصير أهل الأخبية: الأعراب والترك والكرد الذين يسكنون المفازة، وقيد بهم؛ لأن غيرهم لو نوى الإقامة معهم مقيماً عند الإمام، وهو الصحيح. [حاشية الطحطاوي ملخصاً: ٤٢٦] ولا لعسكرنا إلخ: أي ولا تصح نية الإقامة لعسكرنا في دار الحرب ولو حاصروا مصراً؛ لمخالفة حالهم بالتردد بين القرار والفرار. [مراقي الفلاح: ٤٢٦] أما من دخلها بأمان ونوى الإقامة في موضعها، صحت ويتم [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٤٢٦] ولا بدارنا أي ولا تصح نية الإقامة لعسكرنا في دارنا حال كونهم محاصرين أهل البغي والبغاة: قوم خرجوا عن طاعة الإمام الحق ظانين أنهم على الحق، ولا يحكم بفسقهم بالاتفاق؛ لأنهم متمسكون بشبهة وإن كانت فاسدة، فإن لم تكن لهم شبهة فهم لصوص [ حاشية الطحطاوي ومراقي الفلاح ٤٢٦] وبعده لا يصح: أي بعد خروج الوقت لا يصح اقتداء المسافر بالمقيم. تبيين الحقائق: ٥١٥/١] وبعكسه صح إلخ أي بعكس ما ذكره من اقتداء المسافر بالمقيم جائز في الوقت، وبعده، وهو اقتداء المقيم بالمسافر [تبيين الحقائق: ٥١٦/١] ولا يقرأ المقيم إلخ أي إذا صلى المقيم خلف مسافر وفرغ الإمام المسافر عن صلاته، يقوم المؤتم ويؤدّي ما بقي من صلاته، ولكنه لا يقرأ خلفه في الأصح وقال بعض المشايخ يقرأ كالمسبوق. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٤٢٨] وفائتة السفر والحضر إلخ فيه لف ونشر أي فائتة السفر تقضى ركعتين، وفائتة الحضر تقضى أربعاً. تبيين الحقائق: ٥١٦/١] والمعتبر إلخ أي المعتبر في وجوب الأربع أو الركعتين آخر الوقت، فإن كان آخر الوقت مسافراً وجب عليه ركعتان، وإن كان مقيماً وجب عليه الأربع. [تبيين الحقائق: ٥١٩/١] ويبطل إلخ : أي يبطل الوطن الأصلي بالوطن الأصلي، هذا إذا انتقل عن الأول بأهله، وأما إذا لم ينتقل بأهله ولكنه استحدث أهلاً ببلدة أخرى فلا يبطل وطنه الأول ويتم، وقوله: "فقط" أي لا بإنشاء السفر ولا بوطن الإقامة، وكلاهما لا يبطل به الأصلي، وقوله: "وطن الإقامة بمثله" أي يبطل وطن الإقامة بوطن الإقامة :
Book of Prayer: Prayer of the Traveler. And maturity and that the duration of travel is not less than three days. So one who has not passed the built-up area of his residence does not shorten, nor one who has passed but is a child or a dependent whose principal did not intend travel, like a woman with her husband, a slave with his master, a soldier with his commander, or one intending less than three days. And the intention of residence and travel is considered from the original without... like the husband, master, and commander, the follower if he knows the intention of the principal in the most correct view. And shortening is a determined obligation with us. So if he completes the four-rak'a prayer and sits the first sitting like the slave, woman, and soldier, his prayer is valid but disliked. Otherwise it is not valid unless he intended residence when he stood for the amount of tashahhud, even if he did not sit for the third. And he continues shortening until he enters his city or intends residence for half a month in a town or village. The traveler: He does not shorten: beginning of the four sub-cases on the four conditions: passing beyond, independence, puberty, and sufficiency of duration. So no shortening for one who has not passed the built-up area because he has not passed beyond, which is a condition for shortening. And no shortening for a child because he has not reached puberty. And no shortening for a follower because he is not independent in ruling, for he is a follower of his principal and his intention is not considered. And no shortening for one who intends less than the travel distance because of insufficiency of duration. Like a woman with her husband - he mentioned it absolutely, and it is restricted to when he has paid her prompt dower; if he has not paid her, she is not his follower even if he has consummated, because it is permissible for her to prevent him from intercourse for the dower according to Abu Hanifa - [reference]. And the slave etc. he mentioned absolutely, and it is restricted to non-mukatab, so it includes umm walad and mudabbar. As for the mukatab, it is said in 'al-Bahr' that he should not be a follower because he can travel without the master's permission. If he knows the intention etc.: he is not obliged to complete because of the principal's intention of residence until he knows. And is he obliged to ask his principal? The apparent is the first. His prayer is valid: as for validity, because the obligatory act exists in its place, which is sitting after two rak'as, and the other two become supererogatory for him. As for the dislike, because of delaying an obligatory duty, which is the salutation from its place, even if intentional; if forgetful, he performs the prostration of forgetfulness, and for leaving the obligatory shortening, and leaving the beginning of the supererogatory, and mixing it with the obligatory - all that is not permissible. Otherwise it is not valid: i.e., if he did not sit for the amount of tashahhud at the end of the first two rak'as, his prayer is not valid, because he left the obligatory sitting in its place and mixed the supererogatory with the obligatory before its completion. [Maraqi al-Falah: 429] Until he enters his city: he used the absolute term for entering his city, so it includes whether he intended residence there or not. [al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 2/207] He intends his residence: he used the absolute term for intention, so it includes implicit intention, as if a pilgrim arrives in Sham and knows that the caravan leaves only after fifteen days, and he resolves not to leave except with them, he does not shorten because he is like one intending residence. And it includes if he intends it during the prayer while in time, then he completes, whether at the beginning, middle, or end of his prayer, and whether he is alone, following, catching up, or lagging behind. And it is restricted to half a month because intending residence for less does not necessitate completion. And it is restricted to town and village because intention of residence is not valid elsewhere, so it is not valid in a desert, island, sea, or ship. [al-Bahr al-Ra'iq summarized: 2/208] Book of Prayer: page 141. Prayer of the Traveler. Description of what preceded. And he shortens if he intends less than that or does not intend and remains for years. And intention of residence in two towns without specifying overnight stay in one is not valid. Nor in a desert for non-tent dwellers, nor for our army in dar al-harb, nor in our dar while besieging rebels. And if a traveler follows a resident in time, it is valid and he completes four rak'as. After time, it is not valid. And the opposite is valid in both. And it is recommended for the imam to say: 'Complete your prayer, for I am a traveler' after the two taslims in the most correct view. And he should say that before beginning the prayer. And the resident does not recite in what he completes after his traveler imam finishes in the most correct view. And missed prayer of travel and residence are made up as two and four rak'as respectively. And consideration is for the end of time. And the original homeland is nullified only by another original homeland. And the residence homeland is nullified by another residence homeland, by travel, and by the original homeland. They do not become... Tent dwellers: bedouins, Turks, and Kurds who live in the desert. And it is restricted to them because if others intend residence with them, they become residents according to the Imam, and that is the correct view. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi summarized: 426] Nor for our army etc.: i.e., intention of residence is not valid for our army in dar al-harb even if they besiege a city, because their situation is contrary due to fluctuation between staying and fleeing. [Maraqi al-Falah: 426] As for one who enters with aman and intends residence in its place, it is valid and he completes. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 426] Nor in our dar: i.e., intention of residence is not valid for our army in our dar while they are besieging rebels. And rebels are a people who have left obedience to the rightful imam thinking they are right, and they are not judged as sinners by consensus because they adhere to a doubt even if corrupt. If they have no doubt, they are thieves. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi and Maraqi al-Falah: 426] And after it is not valid: i.e., after the time is out, a traveler following a resident is not valid. [Tabyin al-Haqa'iq: 1/515] And the opposite is valid etc.: i.e., the opposite of what he mentioned - a traveler following a resident is permissible in time and after, which is a resident following a traveler. [Tabyin al-Haqa'iq: 1/516] And the resident does not recite etc.: i.e., if a resident prays behind a traveler and the traveler imam finishes his prayer, the follower stands and performs what remains of his prayer, but he does not recite behind him in the most correct view. And some shaykhs said he recites like a latecomer. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 428] And missed prayer of travel and residence etc.: It contains a chiasm: i.e., missed prayer of travel is made up as two rak'as, and missed prayer of residence as four. [Tabyin al-Haqa'iq: 1/516] And the consideration etc.: i.e., what is considered in the obligation of four or two is the end of time: if at the end of time he is a traveler, two rak'as are obligatory; if a resident, four are obligatory. [Tabyin al-Haqa'iq: 1/519] And it is nullified etc.: i.e., the original homeland is nullified by another original homeland. This is if he moves from the first with his family. If he does not move with his family but acquires a family in another town, his first homeland is not nullified and he completes. And his saying 'only' means not by initiating travel nor by a residence homeland, and both do not nullify the original. And his saying 'the residence homeland by its like' means the residence homeland is nullified by another residence homeland.
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage from Nur al-Idah, with commentary from Maraqi al-Falah, al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, Tabyin al-Haqa'iq, and Hashiyat al-Tahtawi, explains the detailed rules of qasr (shortening prayer) for a traveler in the Hanafi school. The passage begins by listing the conditions for qasr: the traveler must have passed beyond the built-up area of his residence, be an adult (baligh), be independent (not a follower whose principal did not intend travel), and the travel duration must be at least three days (approximately 48 miles or 78 km). The text then elaborates on four sub-cases where qasr is not valid: not passing beyond the built-up area, being a child, being a dependent (like a woman with husband, slave with master, soldier with commander), or intending a distance less than the travel duration. It clarifies that a follower is required to know the principal's intention of travel; otherwise, he does not shorten. The ruling emphasizes that qasr is a determined obligation ('azima), not a concession (rukhsa) in the Hanafi school. If a traveler completes four rak'as while intending qasr, his prayer is valid but disliked (makruh), as he delayed the obligatory sitting after two rak'as and mixed supererogatory with obligatory. If he fails to sit after two rak'as, the prayer is invalid. The traveler continues shortening until he enters his city (even if he does not intend residence) or intends residence for fifteen days in a town or village. Intention of residence for less does not require completion. The text also covers the validity of following: a traveler following a resident in time is valid, and the traveler completes four rak'as; after time it is invalid. The opposite (resident following traveler) is valid in both. It recommends the traveler imam to inform the congregation to complete their prayer. It also discusses missed prayers: a missed travel prayer is made up as two rak'as, and a missed resident prayer as four, with consideration given to the end of the time. Finally, it addresses nullification of homelands: the original homeland is nullified only by another original homeland, while the residence homeland is nullified by another residence homeland, by travel, and by the original homeland. The commentary explains that tent dwellers (bedouins, Turks, Kurds) are a special case for intention of residence in the desert. This passage is foundational for understanding the Hanafi rules of traveler's prayer.

Key Terms
قصر (qasr): Shortening the four-rak'a prayers (zuhr, asr, isha) to two rak'as while traveling.
مسافر (musafir): A person traveling a distance of three days (approximately 78 km) who has passed the built-up area of his residence.
نية الإقامة (niyyat al-iqama): Intention to stay in a place for fifteen days or more, which obligates the traveler to complete prayers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A traveler follows a resident imam for asr prayer, but the time for asr has already expired (qada prayer). What is the ruling?
A) The traveler's prayer is valid and he completes four rak'as.
B) The traveler's prayer is invalid.
C) The traveler's prayer is valid but he must pray two rak'as only.
D) The traveler must follow but then repeat his prayer later.

Key Takeaway
Qasr ends only by entering one's city or intending 15-day residence in a settled place; following a resident imam in time obligates completion.

Valid and Invalid Intentions to Stay for the Traveler
Rulings on valid and invalid intentions to stay

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions under which a traveler's intention to stay (niyyat al-iqama) is valid or invalid according to the Hanafi school and apply these rulings to common travel scenarios.

Core Idea
A traveler's intention to stay is valid only for 15+ days in one place, except for armies in war or rebellion and non-Bedouins in deserts.

This passage from Nur al-Idah, with later Hanafi commentaries, presents the precise conditions that make a traveler's intention to stay (niyyat al-iqama) legally effective. Understanding these exceptions is crucial for determining when the traveler must pray full salah (4 rak'ahs) instead of shortening (qasr).

Guided Path
1
Identify the general principle
The passage begins by stating that a traveler shortens prayer if he intends less than 15 days or has no intention at all, even if he stays for years. The intention to stay for 15+ days makes him a resident (muqim) requiring full prayers.
The 15-day minimum is unique to the Hanafi school.
2
Analyze the first exception: two towns without specifying overnight
If a traveler intends to stay in two different towns without specifying in which he will spend the night, the intention is invalid because the place of residence is ambiguous.
Overnight stay (mabit) must be clearly assigned to one location.
3
Analyze the second exception: desert intention for non-Bedouins
Intending to stay in a desert (mufazah) is valid only for non-Bedouins. Bedouins (ahl al-akhiba) are always considered travelers, so their intention to stay is irrelevant. For others, if they intend to stay with Bedouins, they become residents.
Ahl al-akhiba includes Bedouins, Turks, and Kurds living in deserts.
4
Analyze the third exception: army in Dar al-Harb
If our army is in enemy territory (Dar al-Harb), intention to stay is invalid even if besieging a city, due to the constant uncertainty of staying or retreating. However, a civilian entering with aman (safe passage) can validly intend to stay.
The army's situation is inherently unstable (taraddud bayn al-qarar wal-firar).
5
Analyze the fourth exception: army besieging rebels in our territory
If our army is in our own territory (Dar al-Islam) besieging rebels (ahl al-baghy), intention to stay is invalid for similar reasons of instability. Rebels with a shubha (doubt) are not deemed sinful; otherwise, they are bandits.
The passage clarifies that rebels (bughat) are not fasiq if they have a misinterpretation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقصر إن نوى أقل منه أو لم ينو وبقي سنين، ولا تصح نية الإقامة ببلدتين لم يعين المبيت بإحداهما ، ولا في مفازة لغير أهل الأخبية ولا لعسكرنا بدار الحرب، ولا بدارنا في محاصرة أهل البغي، أهل الأخبية: الأعراب والترك والكرد الذين يسكنون المفازة، وقيد بهم؛ لأن غيرهم لو نوى الإقامة معهم مقيماً عند الإمام، وهو الصحيح. [حاشية الطحطاوي ملخصاً: ٤٢٦] ولا لعسكرنا إلخ: أي ولا تصح نية الإقامة لعسكرنا في دار الحرب ولو حاصروا مصراً؛ لمخالفة حالهم بالتردد بين القرار والفرار. [مراقي الفلاح: ٤٢٦] أما من دخلها بأمان ونوى الإقامة في موضعها، صحت ويتم [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٤٢٦] ولا بدارنا أي ولا تصح نية الإقامة لعسكرنا في دارنا حال كونهم محاصرين أهل البغي والبغاة: قوم خرجوا عن طاعة الإمام الحق ظانين أنهم على الحق، ولا يحكم بفسقهم بالاتفاق؛ لأنهم متمسكون بشبهة وإن كانت فاسدة، فإن لم تكن لهم شبهة فهم لصوص [ حاشية الطحطاوي ومراقي الفلاح ٤٢٦]
He shortens if he intended less than it (15 days) or did not intend and remained for years. And the intention to stay in two towns is not valid if he did not specify overnight stay in one of them. Nor in a desert for other than people of tents (Ahl al-Akhiba), nor for our army in the abode of war, nor in our abode while besieging the people of rebellion. The people of tents: the Bedouins, Turks, and Kurds who dwell in the desert; restricted to them because others besides them, if they intend to stay with them, are considered residents according to Imam [Abu Hanifa], and that is correct. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi summarised: 426] And 'nor for our army' etc.: i.e., the intention to stay for our army in the abode of war is not valid even if they besiege a city; due to their state being contrary [to stability] as they fluctuate between settling and fleeing. [Maraqi al-Falah: 426] But whoever enters with safety and intends to stay in its place, it is valid and he completes [the prayer]. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 426] And 'nor in our abode': i.e., the intention to stay for our army is not valid in our abode while they are besieging the people of rebellion. And the rebels: a group who have gone out of obedience to the rightful Imam, thinking they are upon the truth; they are not judged as sinful by consensus because they cling to a doubt even if it is invalid. But if they have no doubt, then they are bandits. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi and Maraqi al-Falah: 426]
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage from Nur al-Idah, with commentary from later Hanafi scholars, states the rulings on when a traveler's intention to stay (niyyat al-iqama) is valid or invalid. The matn begins by stating the general rule: a traveler shortens prayer if he intends to stay less than fifteen days or has no intention at all and remains for years. Then it lists exceptions where intention to stay does not take effect: if he intends to stay in two towns without specifying where he will spend the night; or in a desert for a non-Bedouin (since Bedouins are considered always traveling); or for our army in enemy territory (Dar al-Harb) because of the uncertainty of their situation; or for our army in our own territory while besieging rebels (Ahl al-Baghy). The commentary explains each point. For the desert exception, it defines Ahl al-Akhiba as Bedouins, Turks, and Kurds who live in the desert; others who intend to stay with them are considered residents according to Imam Abu Hanifa, which is the correct view. For the army in Dar al-Harb, even if they besiege a city, their intention is invalid due to the possibility of retreat. However, a civilian who enters safely can validly intend to stay. For the army besieging rebels (baghi) in our own land, intention is also invalid because of the temporary nature of the campaign. The rebels are defined as those who rebel against the rightful Imam based on a misinterpretation; they are not deemed sinful due to their doubt, but if they have no doubt, they are treated as bandits.

Key Terms
نية الإقامة (niyyat al-iqama): The traveler's intention to stay in a particular place for fifteen days or more, which changes his status from traveler (musafir) to resident (muqim).
أهل الأخبية (ahl al-akhiba): People of tents (Bedouins, Turks, Kurds) who dwell in deserts and are always considered travelers, so intention to stay does not affect them.
بغاة (bughat): Rebels who have a misinterpretation (shubha) of the truth; they are not deemed sinful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following makes a traveler's intention to stay (niyyat al-iqama) invalid according to the Hanafi school?
A) Intending to stay in a single town for 20 days.
B) Intending to stay in two towns without specifying where to spend the night.
C) Intending to stay in a desert as a non-Bedouin.
D) A civilian entering Dar al-Harb with aman and intending to stay for a month.

Key Takeaway
A traveler's intention to stay (niyyat al-iqama) is valid only for 15+ days in one definite location, except for specific exceptions (armies in war/rebellion and Bedouins).

Validity of Following Across Travel Status
Rulings on validity of iqtida' across travel status

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four cases of validity when a traveler and resident follow each other in prayer, and identify the condition that distinguishes valid from invalid following.

Core Idea
A traveler following a resident is valid only within the prayer time; the reverse is always valid.

When a traveler and a resident pray together, the validity of the follower's prayer depends on whether the imam's prayer is offered in its proper time or as a make-up. This lesson covers the core rulings from Nur al-Idah, explaining when a traveler may follow a resident imam and when a resident may follow a traveler imam, along with the recommended announcement for the traveler imam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the two parties
Determine whether the follower is a traveler (musafir) or resident (muqim) and whether the imam is a traveler or resident. The ruling differs based on these statuses.
Traveler shortens four-rak'ah prayers to two; resident prays full.
2
Check the time of prayer
Is the prayer being performed within its prescribed time (ada') or after the time has exited (qada')? This is critical for the case of a traveler following a resident.
The text uses 'fi al-waqt' (in time) and 'ba'dahu' (after it).
3
Apply the rule for traveler following resident
If the imam is resident and prays within the time, the traveler may follow and must complete four rak'ahs. If the imam is praying a make-up prayer (after time), the traveler may not follow.
Because the traveler's make-up prayer is two rak'ahs, not four.
4
Apply the rule for resident following traveler
A resident may follow a traveler imam regardless of whether the imam is praying in time or after time. The resident must complete the remaining rak'ahs after the imam's salam.
This is valid because the resident's obligation is four rak'ahs, which he completes.
5
Note the recommended announcement
The traveler imam should announce before starting the prayer that he is a traveler, so that resident followers know to complete their prayers after his salam.
This is a sunnah (recommended) act to prevent confusion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن اقتدى مسافر بمقيم في الوقت صح وأتمها أربعاً، وبعده لا يصح، وبعكسه صح فيهما، وندب للإمام أن يقول : أتموا صلاتكم، فإني مسافر، وينبغي أن يقول ذلك قبل شروعه في الصلاة، ولا يقرأ المقيم فيما يتمه بعد فراغ إمامه المسافر في الأصح، وبعده لا يصح: أي بعد خروج الوقت لا يصح اقتداء المسافر بالمقيم. تبيين الحقائق: ٥١٥/١] وبعكسه صح إلخ أي بعكس ما ذكره من اقتداء المسافر بالمقيم جائز في الوقت ،وبعده، وهو اقتداء المقيم بالمسافر [تبيين الحقائق: ٥١٦/١] ولا يقرأ المقيم إلخ أي إذا صلى المقيم خلف مسافر وفرغ الإمام المسافر عن صلاته، يقوم المؤتم ويؤدّي ما بقي من صلاته، ولكنه لا يقرأ خلفه في الأصح وقال بعض المشايخ يقرأ كالمسبوق. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٤٢٨]
And if a traveler follows a resident in time, it is valid and he completes it as four. After time it is not valid. And the opposite is valid in both. And it is recommended for the imam to say: 'Complete your prayer, for I am a traveler.' And he should say that before starting the prayer. And the resident does not recite in what he completes after his traveler imam finishes, according to the most sound opinion. After time it is not valid: i.e., after the exit of the time, the traveler following a resident is not valid. [Tabyin al-Haqa'iq: 1/515] And the opposite is valid etc.: i.e., the reverse of what was mentioned, that a traveler following a resident is permissible in time and after it, which is when a resident follows a traveler. [Tabyin al-Haqa'iq: 1/516] And the resident does not recite etc.: i.e., when a resident prays behind a traveler and the traveler imam finishes his prayer, the follower stands and performs what remains of his prayer, but he does not recite behind him according to the most sound opinion. And some mashayikh say he recites like a latecomer (masbuq). [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 428]
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage from Nur al-Idah, with commentary from Tabyin al-Haqa'iq and Hashiyat al-Tahtawi, covers the rules of iqtida' (following) between a traveler and a resident. The matn states four cases: (1) If a traveler follows a resident imam within the prayer time, it is valid and the traveler must complete four rak'ahs (since following a resident obligates the traveler to pray complete). (2) If the traveler follows the resident after the time has exited (i.e., the resident is praying a make-up prayer), it is not valid because the traveler's make-up prayer is different (two rak'ahs). (3) The opposite case, a resident following a traveler imam, is valid both within and after time. (4) It is recommended for the traveler imam to announce before the prayer that he is a traveler so that residents can complete their prayers on their own. (5) When a resident follows a traveler and the traveler finishes his two rak'ahs, the resident stands to complete his remaining two rak'ahs, but he does not recite (Qira'ah) during those additional rak'ahs according to the soundest opinion, although some scholars say he should recite like a masbuq (latecomer).

Key Terms
اقتداء (iqtida'): Following an imam in prayer; the follower (muqtadi) aligns with the imam.
مسافر (musafir): A person undertaking a journey of three days and nights (according to Hanafi) who is allowed to shorten prayers.
مقيم (muqim): A resident who is not traveling; prays full four rak'ahs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is it valid for a traveler to follow a resident imam?
A) Only if the imam prays within the prayer time.
B) Only if the imam prays after the time.
C) Both within and after the time.
D) Never valid.

Key Takeaway
A traveler may only follow a resident imam within the prayer time, completing four rak'ahs; a resident may follow a traveler regardless of time, completing his prayer after the imam's salam.

Recitation by the Resident Follower After the Traveler Imam
Intra-Hanafi dispute on recitation by resident follower

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the two Hanafi opinions on whether the resident follower recites in the remaining rak'ahs after the traveler imam's salam, and state the relied-upon view.

Core Idea
The resident follower does not recite the remaining rak'ahs, unlike a masbuq, according to the soundest Hanafi opinion.

When a resident prays behind a traveler imam, after the imam finishes his two rak'ahs, the resident stands to complete his remaining two. A debated issue within the Hanafi school is whether the resident recites (Qira'ah) during those additional rak'ahs. This lesson examines the two positions and the reasoning behind the preferred view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
A resident prays behind a traveler imam. The imam performs two rak'ahs (shortened) and gives salam. The resident then stands to complete the remaining two rak'ahs of his four-rak'ah prayer.
This is permitted because resident following traveler is valid regardless of time.
2
Recognize the disputed issue
The question: Should the resident recite Quran during the two rak'ahs he performs after the imam's salam?
The matn states he does not recite 'in the most sound' opinion, indicating a difference.
3
State the two opinions
First opinion (most sound): He does not recite, because he remains in the state of a follower (muqtadi) even after the imam's salam. Second opinion: He recites like a masbuq (latecomer) who completes missed rak'ahs with recitation.
The text says 'fì al-ashah' (in the most sound) and then mentions some scholars analogize to masbuq.
4
Analyze the reasoning
The first opinion treats the resident as still following the imam in the sense that his entire prayer is linked to the imam's. The second opinion views the additional rak'ahs as independent, like those of a masbuq who missed part of the prayer.
The key difference: a masbuq missed the beginning, so he recites; the resident was present throughout, so he remains a follower.
5
Determine the tarjih
The text explicitly grades the first opinion as 'al-ashah' (most sound), and this is the relied-upon view in the Hanafi school. The commentator al-Tahtawi confirms that this is the preferred position.
Thus, in practice, the resident should not recite in his remaining rak'ahs.

Qada' of Missed Prayers: Number of Rak'ahs Based on End of Time
Ruling on missed prayer compensation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi criterion for the number of rak'ahs in qada' based on the status at the end of the original time.

Core Idea
The missed prayer is made up according to the status at the end of the time, not when it was missed.

Have you ever missed a prayer while traveling and later settled down? How should you make it up? The Hanafi school provides a clear rule: look at the end of the prayer's due time. This lesson explains that rule and helps you apply it correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is making up a missed obligatory prayer. The ruling is that it is wajib. The number of rak'ahs is based on whether the original prayer was a travel prayer (2) or residence prayer (4).
2
Determine the criterion
The text explicitly says: 'المعتبَر فيه آخر الوقت' (the consideration is the end of the time). This means you look at the person's status as traveler or resident at the last moment of the prayer's time.
3
Apply to scenarios
If a traveler missed Zuhr but became a resident before the time ends, he prays 4 rak'ahs. If a resident missed Zuhr but traveled before the end, he prays 2 rak'ahs.
4
Note the consistency
This rule applies to all missed prayers (fawa'it) regardless of when they are made up later.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفائتة السفر والحضر تقضى ركعتين وأربعاً، والمعتبر فيه آخر الوقت، ويبطل الوطن الأصلي بمثله فقط، ويبطل وطن الإقامة بمثله وبالسفر وبالأصلي، وفائتة السفر والحضر إلخ فيه لف ونشر أي فائتة السفر تقضى ركعتين، وفائتة الحضر تقضى أربعاً. تبيين الحقائق: ٥١٦/١] والمعتبر إلخ أي المعتبر في وجوب الأربع أو الركعتين آخر الوقت، فإن كان آخر الوقت مسافراً وجب عليه ركعتان، وإن كان مقيماً وجب عليه الأربع. [تبيين الحقائق: ٥١٩/١] ويبطل إلخ : أي يبطل الوطن الأصلي بالوطن الأصلي، هذا إذا انتقل عن الأول بأهله، وأما إذا لم ينتقل بأهله ولكنه استحدث أهلاً ببلدة أخرى فلا يبطل وطنه الأول ويتم، وقوله: "فقط" أي لا بإنشاء السفر ولا بوطن الإقامة، وكلاهما لا يبطل به الأصلي، وقوله: "وطن الإقامة بمثله" أي يبطل وطن الإقامة بوطن الإقامة : = كتاب الصلاة ١٤٢ صلاة المسافر والوطن الأصلي: هو الذي ولد فيه، أو تزوج، أو لم يتزوج وقصد التعيش لا الارتحال عنه، ووطن الإقامة : موضع نوى الإقامة فيه نصف شهر فما فوقه، ولم يعتبر المحققون وطن السكنى وهو ما ينوي الإقامة فيه دون نصف شهر. وقوله: "بالسفر وبالأصلي" أي ويبطل بإنشاء السفر وبالوطن الأصلي، وفائدة هذه الأوطان أن يتم صلاته فيها إذا دخلها، وهو مسافر قبل أن تبطل. ولم يعتبر اعلم أن عامة المشايخ قسموا الأوطان على ثلاثة وطن أصلي وهو مولد الرجل أو البلد الذي تأهل فيه، ووطن الإقامة: وهو البلد الذي ينوي المسافر فيه الإقامة خمسة عشر يوما ويسمى وطن سفر، ووطن السكنى وهو البلد الذي ينوي المسافر فيه الإقامة أقل من خمسة عشر يوما والمحققون منهم قسموا إلى الوطن الأصلي ووطن الإقامة، ولم يعتبروا وطن السكنى وهو الصحيح؛ لأنه لم تثبت فيه الإقامة، بل حكم السفر فيه باق. [العناية شرح الهداية]
The missed prayer of travel and residence is made up as two and four rak'ahs respectively. And the consideration in it is the end of the time. And the original homeland is nullified only by its like. And the homeland of residence is nullified by its like, by travel, and by the original homeland. ... [commentary] ... And the original homeland: it is the place where he was born, or married, or if not married, intends to settle and not leave. And the homeland of residence: a place where he intends to stay for half a month or more. And the verifying scholars did not consider the homeland of dwelling (watan al-sukna), which is where he intends to stay less than half a month. ...
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage from Nur al-Idah with commentary from Tabyin al-Haqa'iq and al-Inayah covers two topics: (1) How to make up missed prayers: a missed prayer that was due during travel is made up as two rak'ahs; if due during residence, as four. The determining factor for the number is the status at the end of the original prayer time: if at that moment he was a traveler, he makes up two; if a resident, four. (2) The definitions of homelands (watan) and what nullifies them. There are two types: al-watan al-asli (original homeland) is where a person was born, or married, or intends to settle permanently. It is only nullified by acquiring another original homeland (e.g., moving with family to another place). Travel or a temporary residence does not nullify it. Al-watan al-iqama (residence homeland) is a place where a traveler intends to stay for fifteen days or more. It is nullified by another watan iqama, by undertaking a journey, or by the original homeland. The verifying scholars (al-muhaqqiqun) do not recognize watan al-sukna (dwelling homeland, less than 15 days), considering the traveler's status to remain. The purpose of these homelands is to determine when a traveler must complete his prayer: upon entering his original homeland, he becomes a resident; upon entering a watan iqama, he completes because he has made it a residence.

Key Terms
فائتة (fà'itah): A missed prayer that must be made up (qada').

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A resident misses 'Isha while traveling. He returns home 30 minutes after 'Isha time began. The 'Isha time expires while he is at home. How many rak'ahs does he make up?
A) 2
B) 4
C) 3 (since 'Isha is 4 but qasr?)
D) He does not need to make up

Key Takeaway
The number of rak'ahs for a missed prayer depends on the status at the end of the original time, not when it was missed.

Definitions of Watan and Their Nullification
Definitions and nullification of homelands

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define al-watan al-asli and watan al-iqama, and state what nullifies each according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
The original homeland is permanent and only nullified by another; the residence homeland is temporary and nullified by many things.

Travelers often wonder when they need to complete their prayers. The Hanafi school defines two types of homelands: the original homeland, which is permanent, and the homeland of residence, which is temporary. Understanding these concepts helps a traveler know when to perform full prayers. This lesson explains the definitions and what nullifies each.

Guided Path
1
Define the original homeland (watan asli)
It is the place where a person was born, married, or intends to settle permanently. It is only nullified by another original homeland.
2
Define the homeland of residence (watan iqama)
It is a place where a traveler intends to stay for 15 days or more. It is nullified by another watan iqama, by starting a journey, or by the original homeland.
3
Understand the nullification rules
The original homeland is strong: travel and temporary residence do not nullify it. The residence homeland is weaker: it can be nullified by various factors.
4
Note the rejection of watan al-sukna
Some scholars recognized a third type (dwelling homeland for less than 15 days), but the verifying scholars (muhaqqiqun) did not. The correct view is that such a place does not break the traveler's status.

Source Text

وطن الإقامة (watan al-iqama): A place where a traveler intends to stay for fifteen days or more.

Key Takeaway

Classification of Homelands for the Traveler's Prayer
Commentary defining watan asli, iqama, and sukna with the verified opinion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the three types of homelands in Hanafi fiqh and state the relied-upon position regarding watan al-sukna.

Core Idea
Only two homelands affect the traveler's prayer: the original homeland and a residence of fifteen days or more; a short stay does not break travel status.

This passage from Al-Inayah clarifies the classification of homelands for the traveler. While many earlier Hanafi scholars recognized three categories, the verifying scholars (al-muhaqqiqun) settled on two. Understanding which homelands change the traveler's prayer from qasr to full is essential for correctly applying the rulings of travel.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three homelands mentioned
The passage lists three: original homeland (watan asli), homeland of residence (watan iqama), and homeland of dwelling (watan sukna). List them in your mind.
2
Define al-watan al-asli
The original homeland is where the person was born, or married, or if unmarried intended to settle permanently without intending to leave.
This homeland never changes unless a new original homeland is established.
3
Define watan al-iqama
This is a place where the traveler intends to reside for fifteen days or more. Upon that intention, he becomes a resident (muqim) for prayer purposes.
The minimum is fifteen days; less than that does not break travel status.
4
Understand watan al-sukna and its status
It is a place where the traveler intends to stay for less than fifteen days. The verifying scholars do not consider this a separate category because residence is not established; the ruling of travel remains.
This is the relied-upon opinion.
5
Apply the ruling: which homelands trigger full prayer?
When a traveler enters his original homeland or a place where he has established a watan iqama, he prays full prayers. Entering a watan sukna does not change his traveler status.
The benefit of these homelands is to know when the traveler completes his prayer upon entry.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة
صلاة المسافر
والوطن الأصلي: هو الذي ولد فيه، أو تزوج، أو لم يتزوج وقصد التعيش لا الارتحال عنه، ووطن الإقامة : موضع نوى الإقامة فيه نصف شهر فما فوقه، ولم يعتبر المحققون وطن السكنى وهو ما ينوي الإقامة فيه دون نصف شهر.
وقوله: "بالسفر وبالأصلي" أي ويبطل بإنشاء السفر وبالوطن الأصلي، وفائدة هذه الأوطان أن يتم صلاته فيها إذا دخلها، وهو مسافر قبل أن تبطل. ولم يعتبر اعلم أن عامة المشايخ قسموا الأوطان على ثلاثة وطن أصلي وهو مولد الرجل أو البلد الذي تأهل فيه، ووطن الإقامة: وهو البلد الذي ينوي المسافر فيه الإقامة خمسة عشر يوما ويسمى وطن سفر، ووطن السكنى وهو البلد الذي ينوي المسافر فيه الإقامة أقل من خمسة عشر يوما والمحققون منهم قسموا إلى الوطن الأصلي ووطن الإقامة، ولم يعتبروا وطن السكنى وهو الصحيح؛ لأنه لم تثبت فيه الإقامة، بل حكم السفر فيه باق. [العناية شرح الهداية]
The Book of Prayer. Prayer of the traveler. And the original homeland: is that in which he was born, or married, or if he did not marry and intended to settle, not to depart from it. And the homeland of residence: a place in which he intends to reside for half a month or more. And the verifying scholars did not consider the homeland of dwelling, which is that in which he intends to reside for less than half a month. And his statement: 'by travel and by original' meaning that (the traveler's prayer) is invalidated by initiating travel and by (entering) the original homeland. The benefit of these homelands is that he completes his prayer in them when he enters them, while he is a traveler before it is invalidated. Know that the majority of scholars divided the homelands into three: original homeland, which is a man's birthplace or the city in which he settled; homeland of residence: which is the city in which the traveler intends to reside for fifteen days and is called the homeland of travel; and homeland of dwelling: which is the city in which the traveler intends to reside for less than fifteen days. And the verifying scholars among them divided into original homeland and homeland of residence, and did not consider the homeland of dwelling, and that is correct because residence is not established in it; rather the ruling of travel remains in it. [Al-Inayah Sharh al-Hidayah]
Source pages p. 143

Commentary
This passage defines the three types of homelands relevant to the traveler's prayer according to the majority of scholars, and then clarifies the position of the verifying scholars (al-muhaqqiqin). The original homeland (watan asli) is where a person was born, or married, or if unmarried intended to settle permanently without intending to leave. The homeland of residence (watan iqama) is where a traveler intends to stay for fifteen days or more, which turns him into a resident (muqim) who prays full prayers. The homeland of dwelling (watan sukna) is for less than fifteen days; the verifying scholars do not recognize it as a separate category because residence is not firmly established, so the traveler remains in the legal status of travel. The commentary explains that the purpose of these categories is to determine when the traveler completes his prayer (i.e., prays full prayers) upon entering a homeland while he is still a traveler before his travel is invalidated. The relied-upon opinion is to disregard watan sukna, as stated by the author of Al-Inayah.

Key Terms
الوطن الأصلي (al-watan al-asli): The original homeland where a person was born, married, or if unmarried intended to settle permanently without intending to leave.
وطن الإقامة (watan al-iqama): A place where a traveler intends to reside for fifteen days or more, after which he becomes a resident and prays full prayers.
وطن السكنى (watan al-sukna): A place where a traveler intends to reside for less than fifteen days; the verifying scholars do not consider this a separate category.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the verifying scholars, which of the following homelands is not recognized as affecting the traveler's prayer?
A) Original homeland
B) Homeland of residence
C) Homeland of dwelling
D) All of the above

Key Takeaway
Only the original homeland and a residence of fifteen days or more break the traveler's status; a short stay does not affect the travel ruling.

Rulings on Prayer for the Sick
Rulings on sick person's prayer with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rulings for a sick person's prayer by identifying when sitting or gesturing is permitted, the required sitting posture, and the conditions for valid gestures.

Core Idea
A sick person prays according to ability: sitting with bowing if standing impossible, gesturing if even bowing impossible — but the gesture for prostration must be lower.

This lesson covers the detailed Hanafi rulings on how a sick person performs Salah when unable to stand, bow, or prostrate. It addresses the conditions that permit leaving standing, the flexibility of the sitting posture, the validity of using supports, and the precise requirements for head gestures when even bowing and prostration are impossible.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three levels of inability
The passage distinguishes between inability to stand (total or partial) and inability to bow and prostrate. Determine which level applies to the sick person.
Total inability to stand permits sitting with actual ruku and sujud; partial inability requires standing as much as possible.
2
Determine the conditions excusing from standing
Excusing conditions include severe pain, fear of increased illness, or delayed recovery. The fear must be based on previous experience or a trustworthy Muslim doctor's report.
Mild discomfort does not excuse standing; only severe hardship.
3
Analyze the sitting posture ruling
The sick may sit however comfortable during recitation and bowing (Abu Hanifa's view), but must sit in the tashahhud position during the final sitting. Zufar's opposing view requires spreading the left leg throughout.
The relied-upon view is Abu Hanifa's flexibility.
4
Understand gesture requirements
When bowing and prostration are impossible, the sick prays sitting with head gestures. The gesture for prostration must be lower than that for bowing; otherwise the prayer is invalid.
Using an object to prostrate on is valid only if the head is lowered onto it; raising an object to the face is not allowed.
5
Recognize the ruling on leaning for support
If the sick can stand with support (leaning on a person, stick, or wall), it is considered ability and he must do so. This is especially emphasized by Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (al-Shaybani).
Even if he can only stand for the opening takbir and one verse, that much is obligatory.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب صلاة المريض
إذا تعذر على المريض كل القيام أو تعسر بوجود ألم شديد أو خاف زيادة المرض أو إبطاءه به صلى قاعدا بركوع وسجود، ويقعد كيف شاء في الأصح، وإلا قام بقدر ما يمكنه، وإن تعذر الركوع والسجود صلى قاعدا بالإيماء، وجعل إيماءه للركوع والسجود برأسه للسجود أخفض من إيمائه للركوع، فإن لم يخفضه عنه لا تصح، ولا يرفع لوجهه شيئا يسجد عليه، فإن فعل وخفض رأسه صح وإلا لا، كحجر وخشبة وضع شيئا فسجد عليه. أي وإن لم يخفض صلاته. ألم كدوران رأس ووجع ضرس أو شقيقة أو رمد، أطلقه فشمل ما إذا حدث ذلك الصلاة أو قبلها، ومثل الألم خوف لحوق الضرر من عدو آدمي أو غيره على نفسه أو ماله لو صلى قائما. شديد: قيده بالشديد؛ لأنه إن لحقه نوع من المشقة لم يجز ترك القيام. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٤٣١] خاف زيادة إلخ بأن غلب في ظنه بتجربة سابقة، أو إخبار طبيب مسلم حاذق غير ظاهر الفسق، أو ظهور الحال بأن كان يظهر له من حاله أنه لو قام زاد مرضه أو يبطئ برؤه، ولو قدر على القيام متكئا أو على عصا أو حائط، لا يجزيه إلا كذلك خصوصا على قولهما؛ لأنهما يجعلان قدرة الغير قدرة له. معتمدا. [حاشية الطحطاوي ومراقي الفلاح: ٤٣٠] كيف شاء: أي كيف تيسر له بغير ضرر من تربع أو غيره. [مراقي الفلاح: ٤٣١] في الأصح: اعلم أنه إذا صلى المريض قاعدا بركوع وسجود أو بإيماء كيف يقعد! أما في حال التشهد فإنه يجلس كما يجلس للتشهد بالإجماع، وأما في حالة القراءة وحال الركوع روي عن أبي حنيفة أنه يجلس كيف شاء من غير كراهة إن شاء محتبيا، وإن شاء متربعا، وإن شاء على ركبتيه كما في التشهد وقال زفر له يفترش رجله اليسرى في جميع صلاته والصحيح ما روي عن أبي حنيفة. [البحر الرائق: ١٧٩/٢] وإلا قام إلخ: أي وإن لم يتعذر عليه كل القيام بأن قدر على بعض القيام، قام بقدر ما يمكنه بلا زيادة مشقة، ولو بالتحريمة وقراءة آية. [مراقي الفلاح وحاشية الطحطاوي: ٤٣١] تعذر الركوع وقدر على القعود ولو مستندا. والسجود إلخ وكذا لو عجز عن السجود وقدر على الركوع هما، واختلفوا في التعذر، فقيل: ما يبيح الإفطار، وقيل: التيمم، وقيل: بحيث لو قام سقط، وقيل: ما يعجزه عن القيام بحوائجه، والأصح أن يلحقه ضرر بالقيام كذا في "النهاية" و "المجتبى" وغيرهما. وخفض رأسه أي خفض رأسه للسجود عن إيمائه للركوع وإلا لا أي وإن لم يخفض رأسه للسجود أنزل عن الركوع بأن جعلهما سواء، لا تصح صلاته؛ لترك فرض الإيماء للسجود. [مراقي الفلاح: ٤٣٣] يومئ.
Chapter on the Prayer of the Sick. When all standing is impossible for the sick person or becomes difficult due to severe pain, or he fears increase of illness or its prolongation, he prays sitting with bowing and prostration, and he sits however he wishes according to the most correct view. Otherwise, he stands as much as he can. And if bowing and prostration are impossible, he prays sitting with gestures, and he makes his gesture for bowing and prostration with his head, making the gesture for prostration lower than his gesture for bowing. If he does not lower it, his prayer is invalid. And he does not raise something to his face to prostrate on; if he does so and lowers his head, it is valid, otherwise not, like a stone and wood he places something and prostrates on it. That is, even if he does not lower his prayer. Pain like vertigo, toothache, migraine, or ophthalmia; he terms it generally so it includes when that occurs during prayer or before it. And similar to pain is fear of harm from a human enemy or other on himself or his property if he were to pray standing. Severe: he qualified it with severe because if he experiences some hardship, it is not permissible to leave standing. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 431] He fears increase etc. by being predominant in his opinion due to previous experience or information from a skilled Muslim physician not outwardly sinful, or apparent condition such that it appears to him from his state that if he were to stand his illness would increase or his recovery delayed. And if he is able to stand leaning on someone or on a stick or wall, it is not sufficient for him except similarly, especially according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) because they consider the ability of another as his ability. Leaning. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi and Maraqi al-Falah: 430] However he wishes: i.e., however it is facilitated for him without harm, whether cross-legged or otherwise. [Maraqi al-Falah: 431] In the most correct: Know that when the sick person prays sitting with bowing and prostration or with gestures, how does he sit? As for the state of tashahhud, he sits as one sits for tashahhud by consensus. As for the state of recitation and bowing, it is narrated from Abu Hanifa that he sits however he wishes without dislike: if he wishes, sitting on his buttocks with knees raised, or cross-legged, or on his knees as in tashahhud. Zufar said he spreads his left leg in all his prayer, but the correct is what is narrated from Abu Hanifa. [Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 2/179] And otherwise he stands etc.: i.e., if all standing is not impossible but he is able to do some standing, he stands as much as he can without extra hardship, even if it be the opening takbir and reciting one verse. [Maraqi al-Falah and Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 431] Bowing is impossible but he is able to sit even if leaning. And prostration etc., similarly if he is unable to prostrate but able to bow both. They differed on what constitutes impossibility: some said what permits breaking the fast, others said tayammum, others said such that if he would stand he would fall, others said what incapacitates him from his needs. The most correct is that hardship would befall him by standing, as in al-Nihaya and al-Mujtaba and others. And he lowers his head: i.e., he lowers his head for prostration from his gesture for bowing; otherwise no: i.e., if he does not lower his head for prostration lower than for bowing but makes them equal, his prayer is invalid due to leaving the obligatory gesture for prostration. [Maraqi al-Falah: 433] He gestures.
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage provides detailed rulings on how a sick person performs prayer. It begins with the base ruling: if standing is impossible or severely difficult (due to pain, fear of worsening illness, or prolongation), the sick person may pray sitting with actual bowing and prostration. The sitting posture is flexible; the most correct view is that he may sit in any manner that is comfortable without harm. If he can stand partially, he must stand as much as possible. When even bowing and prostration are impossible, he prays sitting with gestures (ishaarah), making the gesture for prostration lower than for bowing. The text emphasizes that the gesture for prostration must be lower; otherwise the prayer is invalid. It also discusses situations where the sick person might use an object to prostrate on, clarifying that if he raises an object to his face and lowers his head onto it, the prayer is valid; otherwise not. The commentary touches on definitions of 'severe pain' and 'fear of increase'—the latter is based on reasonable certainty from experience or a trustworthy Muslim doctor. The ability to stand with support (leaning on a person, stick, or wall) is considered ability, particularly according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (al-Shaybani). A notable intra-madhhab difference is mentioned: regarding the posture of the sick person during recitation and bowing, Abu Hanifa allows flexible sitting (like folding legs, cross-legged, or on knees), while Zufar requires spreading the left leg; the relied-upon position is Abu Hanifa's. The passage concludes with details on the degree of lowering the head for prostration gesture and the invalidation if the gestures are equal.

Key Terms
تعذر (ta'addhura): Impossibility; here meaning the sick person is unable to perform standing, bowing, or prostration at all.
الإيماء (al-imaa'): Gesturing with the head as a substitute for bowing and prostration when the sick person cannot perform them.
الأصح (al-asahh): The most correct view among Hanafi scholars on a particular ruling; here regarding the sitting posture of the sick.
تعسر (ta'assur): Severe difficulty, a lesser degree than impossibility but still excusing from standing if accompanied by severe pain or fear.
الم شديد (alam shadid): Severe pain; a condition that allows the sick to leave standing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a sick person gestures for bowing and prostration but does not make the gesture for prostration lower than that for bowing, what is the ruling?
A) The prayer is valid but disliked
B) The prayer is invalid because the obligatory gesture for prostration was omitted
C) The prayer is valid if he recited properly
D) He must repeat the prayer with correct gestures

Key Takeaway
A sick person must pray according to his ability: standing if possible (even with support), sitting with actual bowing/prostration if not, and gesturing with head if even those are impossible, ensuring the gesture for prostration is lower.

Ruling for Sick Person Unable to Stand – Conditions and Manner of Sitting
Ruling for sick person with conditions and manner of sitting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions that permit a sick person to pray sitting and apply the Hanafi ruling on the manner of sitting, distinguishing the correct position from the opinion of Zufur.

Core Idea
A sick person may pray sitting only when standing is impossible or severely difficult; partial ability requires partial standing.

This passage from Nur al-Idah addresses the concessions granted to a sick person in prayer. The ruling balances the obligation to stand with the principle of ease (yusr). You will learn the precise conditions that trigger the permission to sit, including severe pain and fear of harm, and how the Hanafi school resolves the internal dispute about the correct sitting posture.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two triggers for sitting
Distinguish between impossibility (ta'adhdhur) and severe difficulty ('usr shadid). The latter includes severe pain, fear of worsening illness, or delay in recovery.
The text adds fear from a human enemy or harm to wealth as equivalent to pain.
2
Determine the extent of standing required
If the sick person can stand partially (e.g., for takbir and one verse), he must do so. This shows the principle of scaling obligation to capacity.
Partial ability must be utilized; otherwise the prayer is valid but deficient.
3
Analyze the conditions for valid fear
Fear of increased illness must be based on previous experience, a trustworthy Muslim doctor's report, or clear indication. Subjective fear alone is insufficient.
The doctor must be Muslim and not outwardly sinful.
4
Resolve the intra-Hanafi dispute on sitting posture
Abu Hanifa allows any comfortable sitting posture (cross-legged, knees drawn, etc.), while Zufur requires iftirash (sitting on left foot) throughout. The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view.
The majority view prioritizes the purpose of the concession – ease.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Chapter of the prayer of the sick. If it is impossible for the sick person to stand completely, or it is difficult due to the presence of severe pain, or he fears an increase in his illness or its delay, he prays sitting with bowing and prostration, and he sits however he wishes in the most correct view, otherwise he stands as much as he is able. [Commentary on severe pain: includes dizziness, toothache, migraine, or ophthalmia; he made it general to include whether that occurs during the prayer or before it. Also included in pain is fear of harm from a human enemy or other to himself or his wealth if he prays standing. 'Severe': he qualified it with 'severe'; because if a type of hardship befalls him, it is not permissible to leave standing. The fear of increase etc.: that is overcome in his mind by previous experience, or the report of a Muslim skilled physician who is not apparently sinful, or the manifestation of the situation such that it appears to him from his condition that if he stood his illness would increase or his recovery would be delayed. And if he is able to stand leaning or on a staff or a wall, it is not sufficient for him except as such, especially according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad); because they consider the ability of another as ability for him. 'How he wishes': i.e., however becomes easy for him without harm, such as sitting cross-legged or otherwise. 'In the most correct': know that when the sick person prays sitting with bowing and prostration or with gesture, how does he sit? As for the state of tashahhud, he sits as he sits for tashahhud by consensus. As for the state of recitation and the state of bowing, it is narrated from Abu Hanifa that he sits however he wishes without dislike: if he wishes, sitting with knees drawn up; if he wishes, cross-legged; if he wishes, on his knees as in tashahhud. And Zufur said: he should spread his left foot in all his prayer, and the correct is what is narrated from Abu Hanifa. 'Otherwise he stands etc.': i.e., if complete standing is not impossible for him, but he is able to stand partially, he stands as much as he can without extra hardship, even if just for the takbir and reciting one verse.
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage from Nur al-Idah presents the ruling for a sick person who cannot stand for prayer. The ruling is a concession (rukhsah) based on hardship. The matn first outlines the conditions: either inability to stand entirely or severe difficulty due to pain or fear of worsening illness. The commentary clarifies that severe pain includes specific ailments like migraine and toothache, and that the fear must be based on reasonable grounds such as past experience or a trustworthy Muslim doctor. Importantly, if the person can stand with support (leaning on a staff or wall), he must do so; this is especially according to the two Sahibayn who consider external support as enabling ability. The most correct view is that the sick person may sit in any manner that is comfortable without harm, though there is an opinion from Zufur that he must sit on his left foot throughout. The ruling emphasizes that even partial ability to stand must be utilized, even if only for the opening takbir and one verse. This shows the Hanafi principle that obligations are scaled according to capacity.

Key Terms
تعذر (taʿadhdhura): Impossibility; here it means that standing is completely impossible for the sick person without severe harm.
عسر (ʿusur): Severe difficulty; here it refers to a level of hardship that justifies the concession to sit, such as severe pain or fear of worsening illness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
A sick person may pray sitting only when standing is impossible or severely difficult; any partial ability to stand must be utilized, and the sitting posture can be any comfortable position according to the mufta bihi view.

Gesture Prayer (Īmā’) for the Sick: Distinguishing Rukūʿ and Sujūd
Ruling when bowing and prostration are impossible, using gesture (ima') with head.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for valid gesture prayer (ima') when unable to bow and prostrate, and apply the rule that the prostration gesture must be lower than the bowing gesture.

Core Idea
Gesture prayer is invalid if the head is not lowered more for sujud than ruku.

When a sick person can sit but cannot physically bow or prostrate, the Sharīʿah allows gesture (īmā’) with the head. However, this concession comes with a precise condition: the gesture for prostration must be distinctly lower than that for bowing. Failure to observe this distinction renders the prayer invalid. In this lesson, we unpack the ruling, its conditions, and the definition of 'inability' that triggers this concession.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The person is unable to perform actual bowing and prostration but can sit. The ruling is that this person must pray by gesture (ima') with the head. This is obligatory (wajib).
The obligation is to gesture for both rukūʿ and sujūd.
2
Understand the specific condition for validity
The gesture for prostration must be lower than the gesture for bowing. If the two gestures are equal, the prayer is invalid. This is a fard of the gesture prayer.
The text says: 'make his gesture for prostration lower than his gesture for bowing'.
3
Note the consequence of violating the condition
If the head is not lowered more for sujud as compared to ruku, the prayer is invalid (la tasihh). The reason is that the lower gesture for sujud is a fard (integral) of the gesture prayer.
The commentary explicitly states: 'due to leaving the obligatory gesture for prostration'.
4
Define 'inability' (taʿadhdhur)
The most correct definition in the Hanafi school is that harm (ḍarar) would result from performing the act. Other definitions (e.g., what permits breaking fast or tayammum) are less preferred.
The text cites al-Nihāya and al-Mujtabā affirming the harm definition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن تعذر الركوع والسجود صلى قاعدا بالإيماء، وجعل إيماءه للركوع والسجود برأسه للسجود أخفض من إيمائه للركوع، فإن لم يخفضه عنه لا تصح، ولا يرفع لوجهه شيئا يسجد عليه، فإن فعل وخفض رأسه صح وإلا لا،
تعذر الركوع وقدر على القعود ولو مستنداً. والسجود إلخ وكذا لو عجز عن السجود وقدر على الركوع هما، واختلفوا في التعذر ، فقيل: ما يبيح الإفطار، وقيل: التيمم، وقيل: بحيث لو قام سقط، وقيل: ما يعجزه عن القيام بحوائجه، والأصح أن يلحقه ضرر بالقيام كذا في "النهاية" و "المجتبى" وغيرهما. وخفض رأسه أي خفض رأسه للسجود عن إيمائه للركوع وإلا لا أي وإن لم يخفض رأسه للسجود أنزل عن الركوع بأن جعلهما سواء، لا تصح صلاته؛ لترك فرض الإيماء للسجود. [مراقي الفلاح: ٤٣٣]

And if bowing and prostration are impossible, he prays sitting with gesture, and he makes his gesture for bowing and prostration with his head, making the gesture for prostration lower than his gesture for bowing. If he does not lower it (the prostration gesture) compared to it (the bowing gesture), his prayer is not valid. And he does not raise anything to his face to prostrate upon. If he does so and lowers his head, it is valid, otherwise not. [Commentary: Inability for bowing and prostration, and he is able to sit even if leaning. And prostration etc. Likewise, if he is unable to prostrate but able to bow for both. And they differed regarding 'inability': some say it is what permits breaking the fast; some say it is what permits tayammum; some say it is such that if he stood he would fall; some say it is what prevents him from standing for his needs. And the most correct is that harm would befall him by standing, as in al-Nihaya and al-Mujtaba and others. 'And he lowers his head' i.e., he lowers his head for prostration from his gesture for bowing. 'Otherwise no' i.e., if he does not lower his head for prostration lower than bowing, making them equal, his prayer is not valid due to leaving the obligatory gesture for prostration.] He gestures.
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage addresses the situation where the sick person can sit but cannot perform actual bowing and prostration. The ruling is that he must gesture with his head, making the gesture for prostration distinctly lower than that for bowing. The commentary clarifies the definition of 'inability' (ta'addhur) in this context. Several opinions are cited: some equate it with the inability that permits breaking the fast in Ramadan, some with the inability that permits tayammum, some with the inability that causes falling when standing, and some with the inability to attend to one's needs. The preferred view is that it is when standing would cause harm. Importantly, if a person can bow but not prostrate, he must do both by gesture - he cannot just bow and omit prostration. The key point is that the difference in height between the two gestures is an obligatory element (fard); failure to distinguish invalidates the prayer. This shows the meticulousness of Hanafi fiqh in preserving the symbolism of prostration even in concessionary forms.

Key Terms
إيماء (īmā’): Gesture with the head to indicate bowing and prostration when actual movements are impossible.
تعذر (taʿadhdhur): Inability; here specifically the inability to perform bowing and prostration, defined as harm to the person if attempted.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) He must perform sajdah al-sahw.

Key Takeaway
A sick person who cannot bow or prostrate must perform gesture prayer with a distinct lower gesture for prostration; failure invalidates the prayer.

Ruling for a Sick Person Unable to Sit
Ruling when sitting is impossible: pray lying on back or side, with head toward qibla.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a sick person who cannot sit in prayer, identify the preferred posture, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the choice between lying on the back and side.

Core Idea
When sitting is impossible, the sick pray by gesture on their back or side; the back is preferred, but the choice is accepted.

This lesson addresses a crucial concession in salah for the sick. When even sitting is impossible, the obligation of prayer continues, but its form changes to gestures while lying down. The Hanafi school provides a detailed ruling that includes a preference for lying on the back, while also allowing the side. We will examine the primary ruling, the conditions, and the internal Hanafi debate on the best posture.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition triggering the concession
The ruling applies when sitting is truly difficult (ta'assur al-qu'ud) meaning the person cannot sit without harm or leaning.
The commentary clarifies that leaning with harm is not required.
2
Recognize the two permissible postures
The sick person may pray while lying on his back (istilqa') or on his side (idtija'). Both are valid.
Lying on the back is mentioned first, indicating preference.
3
Understand the preference and its basis
Lying on the back is preferable (awla) because it allows the face to face the qibla more easily by using a pillow.
This preference is not a requirement.
4
Note the additional etiquettes
The head should be elevated so the face faces the qibla, not the sky. Knees should be raised to avoid extending legs toward the qibla, which is disliked.
These show respect for the qibla even in concession.
5
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
There are three opinions: (1) free choice between back and side (azhar), (2) back only if side impossible, (3) side only if back impossible. The first is mufta bihi.
This dispute shows the breadth of Hanafi scholarship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

وهو الاستلقاء على قفاه المستلقي
وسادة ليصير وجهه إلى القبلة لا السماء، وينبغي نصب ركبتيه إن قدر حتى لا يمدهما
أي لا إلى السماء للمريض
إلى القبلة،
وإن تعسر : فلم يقدر عليه متكنا ولا مستندا إلى حائط أو غيره بلا ضرر [مراقي الفلاح: ٤٣٣] وأما إذا قدر على الاتكاء بضرر فلا يلزمه [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٤٣٣] والأول أولى: اعلم أن في المسألة ثلاثة أقوال: أظهرها: أنه بالخيار بين الاستلقاء والاضطجاع، وهو جواب الكتب المشهورة كـ الهداية وشروحها، ثانيها: أن الاستلقاء إنما يجوز إذا عجز عن الاضطجاع كمذهب الشافعي ثالثها: أن الاضطجاع إنما يجوز إذا عجز عن الاستلقاء.
حاشية الطحطاوي: ٤٣٣] إلى القبلة قيد به؛ لأن مد الرجلين إلى القبلة مكروه للقادر على الامتناع عنه.
And if sitting is difficult, he gestures while lying on his back or on his side, and the first (on the back) is preferable. And he places under his head something that allows the gesture on the back of his head. He is the one lying on his back. A pillow so that his face faces the qibla, not the sky. And he should raise his knees if he is able so that he does not extend them, i.e., not toward the sky for the sick person, toward the qibla. [Commentary: 'And if sitting is difficult': meaning he is not able to sit firmly nor leaning against a wall or other without harm. But if he is able to lean with harm, it is not required of him. 'And the first is preferable': know that there are three opinions in this matter: the most apparent is that he has a choice between lying on the back and lying on the side, and this is the answer of the famous books like al-Hidayah and its commentaries. The second: lying on the back is only permitted if unable to lie on the side, like the Shafi'i school. The third: lying on the side is only permitted if unable to lie on the back. To the qibla: he qualified it with 'to the qibla' because extending the legs toward the qibla is disliked for one who is able to avoid it.]
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This passage covers the case where the sick person cannot sit at all. The ruling is that he prays by gesture while lying on his back (istilqa') or on his side (idtija'), with the back position being preferable. The key requirement is that his face must face the qibla, achieved by placing a pillow under his head, not by tilting the head upward. The commentary engages in an intra-Hanafi dispute: three opinions exist on the preferred position. The most apparent (azhar) view is that he has a free choice between back and side, as in the famous books. The second opinion restricts back to when side is impossible, similar to the Shafi'i school. The third restricts side to when back is impossible. The preferred view is the first. Additionally, it is recommended (yumbaghi) to raise the knees toward the qibla to avoid extending the legs toward the qibla, which is disliked. This shows that even in extreme concession, respect for the qibla is maintained.

Key Terms
مستلقياً (mustalqiyan): Lying on the back, face upward, with a pillow under the head to face qibla.
اضطجاع (iḍṭijāʿ): Lying on the side (usually the right side) facing the qibla.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the most apparent (azhar) opinion regarding the position for prayer when sitting is impossible?
A) He must lie on his back only.
B) He must lie on his side only.
C) He has a choice between lying on his back and on his side.
D) He must sit leaning against something.

Key Takeaway
When sitting is impossible, the sick may pray by gesture on back or side; the back is preferable but not obligatory, and the mufta bihi grants a choice.

Ruling When Even Gesture Is Impossible
Ruling when gesture is impossible; delay and conditions for qada.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qada when a sick person cannot gesture, and explain the intra-madhhab dispute based on duration and consciousness.

Core Idea
If a sick person cannot even gesture, qada is required for up to a day and night but waived beyond.

This lesson addresses an extreme case: a sick person who cannot even move their head to gesture during prayer. The Hanafi school distinguishes between short-term and long-term inability, and between conscious and unconscious states. We will explore the ruling derived from ta'lil (reasoning) and the preferred view in fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and initial ruling
Read the opening statement: if gesture (ima') is impossible, the prayer is delayed (not dropped) as long as the person understands speech. Note that this is the initial ruling before considering duration.
The delay is a postponement, not a waiver.
2
Understand the four-case framework
The commentary breaks down the issue into four cases based on duration (more/less than a day and night) and consciousness. For each case, determine whether qada is required by consensus or disputed.
The key pivot is the combination of consciousness and duration.
3
Trace the Hanafi reasoning (ta'lil)
The text uses analogies (qiyas) from the cases of insanity and fainting. In those cases, if the condition lasts more than a day and night, qada is waived; if less, qada is required. This principle is extended to the sick person who cannot gesture.
Also note the rebuttal regarding the limbless person: that case was for certain permanent inability.
4
Determine the preferred view (mufta bihi)
Several later authorities (Qadikhan, Shaykh al-Islam, etc.) preferred the view that qada is waived if inability exceeds a day and night (approx. 5 prayers), even if conscious. This is the relied-upon position.
The author of al-Hidayah held qada required as long as conscious, but the later consensus leans toward lenience.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

[حاشية الطحطاوي: ٤٣٣]
وصححه قاضي خان واستشهد قاضي خان بما عن محمد فيمن قطعت يداه من المرفقين ورجلاه من الساقين لا صلاة عليه، ودفع بأن ذاك في العجز المتيقن امتداده إلى الموت، وكلامنا فيما إذا صح المريض بعد ذلك لا فيما إذا مات قبل القدرة على القضاء، فلا يجب عليه ولا الإيصاء به كالمسافر والمريض إذا أفطرا في رمضان وماتا قبل الإقامة والصحة، ومن تأمل تعليل الأصحاب في الأصول للمجنون يفيق في أثناء الشهر، ولو ساعة يلزمه قضاء كل الشهر، وكذا الذي جن أو أغمي عليه أكثر من صلاة يوم لا يقضي وفيما دونها يقضي، انقدح في ذهنه إيجاب القضاء على هذا المريض إلى يوم وليلة حتى يلزم الإيصاء به إن قدر عليه بطريق، وسقوطه إن زاد، ثم رأيت عن بعض المشايخ إن كانت الفوائت أكثر من يوم وليلة لا يجب عليه القضاء، وإن كانت أقل وجب، قال في "الينابيع": وهو الصحيح. [فتح القدير: ٤٥٩/١]
And if gesture is impossible, it (the prayer) is delayed for him as long as he understands speech. He said in al-Hidayah: this is correct. And the author of al-Hidayah affirmed in al-Tajnīs wa al-Mazīd that the qada is waived if his inability to gesture continues for more than five prayers, even if he understands speech. Qadikhan confirmed this, and similar is in al-Muhīt, and it was chosen by Shaykh al-Islam and Fakhr al-Islam. Khawāhar Zādah al-Sarakhsī. [Commentary: ... know that the matter has four aspects: if his inability lasts for six prayers and he is unconscious, qada is waived by consensus. If it is less and he is conscious, he makes qada by consensus. If it lasts six prayers and he is conscious, or less and he is unconscious, then there is a difference of opinion among the mashāyikh: some say qada is required - this is the choice of the author of al-Hidayah; some say it is not required - this is the choice of al-Bazdawī al-Saghīr. And Qadikhan confirmed it, and Qadikhan cited as evidence from Muhammad regarding one whose hands are cut off at the elbows and legs at the shins: there is no prayer upon him. And it was refuted that this is in the case of certain inability extending to death, while our discussion is when the sick person recovers later, not when he dies before ability to make qada. So he is not required to make qada nor to make a bequest for it, like the traveler and the sick who break fast in Ramadan and die before residence and health. And whoever considers the reasoning of the scholars in the principles regarding the insane who becomes sane during the month, even for an hour, he must make qada for the entire month. Likewise, one who goes insane or faints for more than one prayer time does not make qada, and for less he makes qada. It becomes clear in his mind the obligation of qada for this sick person up to a day and a night, so that he is required to make a bequest if he is able to do so in some way, and it falls if it exceeds. Then I saw from some mashāyikh: if the missed prayers exceed a day and a night, he does not have to make qada; if they are less, he must. It is said in al-Yanābi': this is correct.]
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This passage addresses the extreme case where the sick person cannot even gesture with his head. The initial ruling is that the prayer is postponed (not waived) as long as he retains consciousness (understands speech). However, the commentary reveals a significant intra-Hanafi dispute on whether qada (making up the prayer) is required when the inability persists. The famous view from al-Hidayah is that qada is waived if the inability lasts for more than five prayers (i.e., a day and a night), even if conscious. The commentary systematizes the issue into four scenarios based on duration and consciousness. The dispute centers on whether the scholar's principle from the case of insanity and fainting should apply: a short period (less than a day and night) requires qada, a longer period does not. Qadikhan supports the view that qada is not required for inability exceeding five prayers, using an analogy (istidlal) from the case of a person with severed limbs. The passage ultimately concludes with the preferred view from al-Yanābi': if the missed prayers are more than a day and night, qada is not required; if less, it is required. This shows the Hanafi methodology of ta'lil (reasoning) and tarjih (preference) in deriving rulings for new cases based on established principles.

Key Terms
الإيماء (al-īmā’): Gesture; here specifically the ability to move the head to indicate bowing and prostration. Inability to do so triggers this ruling.
القضاء (al-qaḍā’): Making up missed prayers after recovery; the dispute here is whether it is obligatory when inability was prolonged.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) When the inability lasts for more than five prayers (a day and night) and he is conscious.
B) When the inability lasts for any period, qada is always required.
C) When he is unconscious for any period.
D) When he recovers after more than a year.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school waives qada for a sick person unable to gesture if the inability persists beyond a day and night, even if conscious, based on qiyas to insanity.
