Making Up the Pre-Zuhr Sunnah: Order of Prayer
Ruling on making up the pre-Zuhr sunnah and its place

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on making up the sunnah before Zuhr, explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad on the order, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
The sunnah before Zuhr is made up; the preferred view is to pray it before the fard.

Making up a missed sunnah prayer is a matter of some detail in the Hanafi school. This passage focuses on the sunnah before Zuhr: it affirms that it is to be made up, but the timing relative to the fard is disputed between the two great disciples of Abu Hanifa. Understanding their reasoning and the final tarjih will clarify the practice for a mufti.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
The text first states that the sunnah before Zuhr is made up in its time before the fard pair. Recognize that the ruling is that the sunnah is to be performed, not omitted.
The phrase 'wa qada al-sunnah...' establishes the obligation to make up (qada) for a missed sunnah mu'akkadah.
2
Recognize the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
The text then reports a difference between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding the order: Abu Yusuf places the two rak'ahs of sunnah before the fard, Muhammad after.
Both views are transmitted in the Hanafi corpus; they represent legitimate ikhtilaf within the school.
3
Analyze the Reasoning
Abu Yusuf argues that since the four rak'ahs missed the sunnah place, we should avoid making the two rak'ahs miss their place again without necessity. Muhammad's reasoning (implied) is that the fard is more important and should be prioritized.
The text mentions support from the fact that the four rak'ahs are treated as one prayer (no separate istiftah in the second pair).
4
Understand the Tarjih
Fath al-Qadir (Al-Marghinani) prefers Abu Yusuf's view, making it the mufta bihi. The reason is to not intentionally cause the two rak'ahs to lose their proper place without necessity.
The tarjih is based on the principle of avoiding unnecessary delay of the sunnah.
5
Apply the Mufta Bihi
In practice, when one misses the sunnah before Zuhr and still has time, they should pray the two rak'ahs of sunnah first, then join the fard jama'ah or pray it individually.
The same ruling applies to the sunnah before Jumu'ah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقضى السنة التي قبل الظهر في وقته قبل شفعه - والظاهر ما صححه المشايخ؛ لأنه لا شك أن في التسليم على رأس الركعتين إبطال وصف السنية لا لإكمال، وتقدم أنه لا يجوز، ويشهد لهم إثبات أحكام الصلاة الواحدة للأربع من عدم الاستفتاح والتعوذ في الشفع الثاني إلى غير ذلك. [البحر الرائق: ١٢٤/٢] وقضى السنة إلخ بيان لشيئين: أحدهما: القضاء، والثاني: محله، أما الأول: ففيه اختلاف، والصحيح أنها تقضى، وأما الثاني فاختلف فيه النقل عن الشيخين، فذكر في الجامع الصغير للحسامي أن أبا يوسف يقدم الركعتين ومحمد يؤخرهما، وفي "المنظومة" وشرحها على العكس، ورجّح في فتح القدير تقديم الركعتين؛ لأن الأربع فاتت عن الموضع المسنون، فلا يفوت الركعتين عن موضعهما قصداً بلا ضرورة، وحكم الأربع قبل الجمعة كالأربع قبل الظهر. [البحر الرائق: ١٣٠/٢]
And he makes up the sunnah that is before Zuhr in its time before its [fard] pair. The apparent view is what the mashayikh have corrected, because there is no doubt that praying two rak'ahs and giving salam invalidates the sunnah quality by not completing it, and it has preceded that this is not permissible. They are supported by the fact that the four rak'ahs are considered one prayer, as there is no istiftah or ta'awwudh in the second pair, etc. [Al-Bahr al-Raiq 2/124] 'And he makes up the sunnah' etc. explains two things: one is the making up, and the other is its place. As for the first, there is difference, and the correct is that it is made up. As for the second, there is difference in the transmission from the two shaykhs: in al-Jami' al-Saghir by al-Husami, Abu Yusuf puts the two rak'ahs first, and Muhammad puts them after. In al-Manzumah and its commentary, it is the opposite. In Fath al-Qadir, he preferred putting the two rak'ahs first because the four missed the sunnah place, so he does not intentionally make the two miss their place without necessity. The ruling of the four before Jumu'ah is like the four before Zuhr. [Al-Bahr al-Raiq 2/130]
Source pages p. 151

Commentary
This passage deals with making up the sunnah before Zuhr (the four rak'ahs) when one misses it. The text first presents the preferred view: the sunnah should be made up before the fard pair (i.e., before the two rak'ahs of fard). This is argued on the basis that if one prays two rak'ahs and then gives salam, he has not completed the four, which would invalidate the sunnah aspect. Additionally, the four are treated as a single prayer (no separate istiftah or ta'awwudh in the second pair). Then the text discusses the issue of making up: there is difference, but the correct view is that it is made up. Regarding the place (before or after the fard), there is a famous intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf holds that the two rak'ahs (the sunnah) should be prayed first, then the fard, while Muhammad holds they should be after. In Fath al-Qadir, the preference is for Abu Yusuf's position. The same applies to the sunnah before Jumu'ah.

Key Terms
الشفع (al-shaf'): The pair (two rak'ahs) of the fard prayer; in Zuhr, the fard is four, but the sunnah is also four. The 'shaf' may refer to the fard pair.
الشيخان (al-shaykhan): Here refers to Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad (the two disciples of Abu Hanifa).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Abu Hanifa
B) Abu Yusuf
C) Muhammad al-Shaybani
D) Al-Husami

Key Takeaway
The sunnah before Zuhr is made up; the mufta bihi is to pray it before the fard, following Abu Yusuf's view.

Ruling on Supererogatory Prayer Before the Obligatory Prayer
Ruling on performing supererogatory prayers before fard

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between sunnah mu'akkadah (rawatib) and other supererogatory prayers, and state the ruling on when to perform them before the fard prayer.

Core Idea
Sunnah rawatib are obligatory to pray before the fard when safe from missing time; non-rawatib are optional.

The general rule states that one may perform voluntary prayers before the fard only if there is no risk of missing the obligatory time. However, this requires detail. This lesson breaks down the categories of supererogatory prayer—sunnah mu'akkadah (rawatib) and non-mu'akkadah—and explains the ruling based on whether one prays in congregation or alone.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of tatawwu'
The passage divides supererogatory prayers into sunnah mu'akkadah (the regular rawatib) and non-mu'akkadah (other voluntary prayers). Understand that the rawatib are emphasized and associated with each fard.
Rawatib include 2 before Fajr, 4 before Zuhr, 2 after Zuhr, etc.
2
Determine the scenario: praying in congregation
When performing the fard in congregation, the rawatib must be performed before the fard if time allows, without choice, because they are mu'akkadah.
This is the relied-upon view (mufta bihi).
3
Determine the scenario: praying alone
When alone, there is a difference in narration: one narration says the rawatib must still be performed; another says the person has a choice. The preferred view is to perform them.
Both narrations are within the Hanafi school.
4
Recognize the ruling for non-rawatib supererogatory prayers
For any voluntary prayer beyond the rawatib, the praying person has complete freedom to perform or omit them, regardless of being in congregation or alone.
These are not emphasized; they are mubah or nafl.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويتطوع قبل الفرض إن أمن فوت الوقت وإلا فلا وإلا فلا أي وإن لم يأمن لا يتطوع، وهذا الكلام مجمل يحتاج فيه إلى التفصيل، فنقول: إن التطوع على وجهين: سنة مؤ كدة وهي السنن الرواتب وغير مؤكدة وهو ما زاد عليها والمصلي لا يخلو: إما أن الفرض بجماعة أو منفرداً، فإن كان يؤديه بجماعة، فإنه يصلي السنن الرواتب قطعاً، ولا يتخير فيها مع الإمكان؛ لكونها مؤكدة، وإن كان يؤديه منفرداً فكذلك الجواب في رواية وقيل يتخير وأما ما زاد على السنن الرواتب من التطوع يتخير المصلي فيه مطلقاً. [تبيين الحقائق: ٤٥٥/١]
And he performs supererogatory prayer before the fard if he is safe from missing the time, otherwise no. 'Otherwise no' means if he is not safe he does not perform supererogatory. This statement is general and needs detail. We say: supererogatory prayer is of two types: sunnah mu'akkadah (the rawatib) and non-mu'akkadah (additional). The praying person is either performing the fard in congregation or alone. If he performs it in congregation, he definitely prays the sunnah rawatib, with no choice if possible, because they are mu'akkadah. If he performs it alone, the answer is the same in one narration, and it is said he has a choice. As for supererogatory beyond the rawatib, the praying person has a choice absolutely.
Source pages p. 152

Commentary
This passage clarifies a general rule: one may perform voluntary prayers before the obligatory prayer only if there is no risk of missing the fard time. The commentary then provides necessary detail: supererogatory prayers include both the emphasized sunnah rawatib (e.g., before Zuhr) and non-emphasized ones. If one prays the fard in congregation, he should definitely pray the sunnah rawatib before—if time permits—since they are highly recommended. If praying alone, the same applies in one narration, but another says he may choose. For additional voluntary prayers beyond the rawatib, he may choose either way.

Key Terms
التطوع (al-tatawwu'): Voluntary prayer that is not obligatory, including both sunnah mu'akkadah and non-mu'akkadah.
السنن الرواتب (al-sunan al-rawatib): The regular sunnah prayers associated with the five daily obligatory prayers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) They are optional; one may choose
C) They should not be performed
D) They are only performed when praying alone

Key Takeaway
The performance of sunnah rawatib before the fard is conditional on safety from missing the fard time, and when in congregation they must be performed if possible.

Catching the Rak'ah by Joining the Imam in Ruku'
Ruling on catching a rak'ah by joining imam in ruku'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for catching a rak'ah when joining the imam in ruku' and identify when the rak'ah is not caught.

Core Idea
Catching the rak'ah requires bowing after the imam's ruku' and before he raises, not merely standing or bowing prematurely.

This lesson clarifies the precise conditions for a latecomer to catch a rak'ah by joining the imam in ruku'. Many assume that being present during the imam's ruku' is sufficient, but the Hanafi school requires specific actions and timing. Understanding these rules ensures the follower's prayer is valid and no rak'ahs are missed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act
The act in question is 'catching the rak'ah' by joining the imam while he is in ruku'. The follower must perform a valid ruku' during the imam's ruku'.
The follower is called al-muqtadi.
2
State the Required Actions
The follower must say the takbir while standing and then bow. He must not merely stand and wait. The bow must occur after the imam has begun his ruku' (i.e., after the imam's recitation).
3
Identify Invalid Scenarios
The rak'ah is not caught if: (a) the follower stands and waits until the imam raises his head; (b) the follower bows before the imam's ruku'; (c) the follower goes down immediately without standing and the imam raises his head before the follower's ruku' is complete.
Bowing before the imam invalidates the ruku'.
4
Determine the Consequence
If the follower bows prematurely, his ruku' is invalid and he must re-bow after the imam's ruku'. If he fails to do so and leaves the prayer, his prayer is invalid.
This applies to Jumu'ah and 'Eid prayers as well.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن أدرك إمامه راكعا فكبر ووقف حتى رفع الإمام رأسه لم يدرك الركعة، وإن ركع قبل إمامه بعد قراءة الإمام المقتدي فيه حتى يصلي إلا إذا كان مقيم جماعة أخرى، ووقف إلخ وهو قيد اتفاقي، فإنه إذا لم يقف بل انحط بمجرد إحرامه فرفع الإمام رأسه قبل ركوع المؤتم لم يدرك الركعة أيضاً. وإلا لا وكذا يسقط بخروج وقت الجمعة والعيد] أي وإن لم يدرك الإمام أو أدركه و لم يكن قرأ المفروض قبل ركوع المقتدي، لا يصح ركوعه؛ لكونه قبل أوانه، فيلزمه أن يركع بعده ثانياً، وإن لم يفعل وانصرف من صلاته بطلت. [مراقي الفلاح: ٤٥٦]
And whoever catches his imam in ruku', then says takbir and stands until the imam raises his head, he has not caught the rak'ah. And if he bows before his imam after the imam's recitation, the follower [does...] until he prays except if he is establishing another congregation. 'And stands' etc. is an agreed-upon condition. If he does not stand but goes down immediately upon his ihram, then the imam raises his head before the follower's ruku', he also does not catch the rak'ah. Otherwise no. And likewise it drops with the exit of the time of Jumu'ah and 'Eid. Meaning: If he does not catch the imam, or catches him but he had not read the obligatory [recitation] before the follower's ruku', his ruku' is not valid because it is before its time. So he must bow a second time after that, and if he does not do so and leaves his prayer, it is invalidated. [Maraqi al-Falah: 456]
Source pages p. 152

Commentary
This passage outlines the conditions for catching a rak'ah with the imam. If a latecomer finds the imam in ruku', he must say takbir while standing and then bow. However, if he merely stands and waits until the imam raises his head without bowing, he has not caught that rak'ah. The correct method is to bow immediately after takbir, but he must ensure that he bows after the imam's recitation (i.e., after the imam has begun his ruku'). If he bows before the imam, his ruku' is premature and invalid. Similarly, if he does not pause after ihram but drops straight into ruku', he may miss the rak'ah if the imam raises his head before his ruku'. In that case, he must bow again later. If he fails to do so, his prayer is invalid. This also applies to Jumu'ah and 'Eid prayers: if one misses the imam's ruku', he has missed that rak'ah.

Key Terms
الركوع (al-ruku'): The bending posture in prayer; catching the imam in ruku' means before he raises from it.
المقتدي (al-muqtadi): The follower who prays behind the imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is required to catch the rak'ah when joining the imam in ruku'?
A) Say takbir and stand until the imam raises.
B) Say takbir and bow immediately, but ensure the bow occurs after the imam's recitation.
C) Bow before the imam to show alertness.
D) Stand and then bow after the imam raises.

Key Takeaway
To catch a rak'ah when joining the imam in ruku', the follower must say takbir while standing, then bow after the imam has begun his ruku' and before he raises his head; otherwise, the rak'ah is missed.

Leaving the Mosque After the Adhan Without Praying
Ruling on exiting mosque after adhan without praying

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on leaving the mosque after the adhan without praying and identify the exception when it is permissible.

Core Idea
Leaving the mosque after adhan without praying is severely disliked (makruh tahrimi) unless you are establishing another congregation.

You have entered the mosque, the adhan is called, but you are tempted to leave without praying. What does the Hanafi school say? This lesson unpacks the ruling and its nuance: it is makruh tahrimi, but a valid excuse like setting up another congregation can lift the dislikedness. Let's explore the details.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the default ruling
The act is leaving the mosque after the adhan has been given without performing the prayer. The default ruling is makruh tahrimi (severely disliked).
Makruh tahrimi is close to haram; it requires repentance.
2
Note the exception
The ruling is not absolute. If the person leaves to establish another congregation (i.e., to lead or join a prayer elsewhere), the dislikedness is removed.
The exception is specific to establishing a congregation, not any other reason.
3
Consider the condition of time
The passage clarifies that the ruling applies when the time for prayer has entered. If the congregation delays the prayer (e.g., waiting for the preferred time), leaving and returning to pray may not be disliked.
This nuance is derived from the commentary in Al-Bahr al-Raiq.
4
Apply to a real example
Example: Zayd hears the adhan for Maghrib in the mosque, but decides to leave to pray at home alone. This is makruh tahrimi. However, if he leaves to lead his family in congregation at home, it is permissible.
The key is intention: establishing another congregation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
خروجه من مسجد أذن ما تجوز به الصلاة، فأدركه إمامه فيه صح وإلا لا، وکړه فيه تحريما حتى يصلي إلا إذا كان مقيم جماعة أخرى، من الأذان فيه هو مسجد أذن فيه إلخ: أطلقه المصنف، فشمل ما إذا أذن فيه وهو داخله أو دخل بعد الأذان، والظاهر أن مرادهم دخول الوقت وهو داخله، سواء أذن فيه أو في غيره كما أن الظاهر من الخروج من غير صلاة الصلاة مع الجماعة، سواء خرج أو كان ماكثاً في المسجد من غير صلاة كما نشاهده في زماننا من بعض الفسقة، حتى لو كانت الجماعة يؤخرون لدخول الوقت المستحب كالصبح مثلاً، فخرج إنسان من المسجد بعد دخول الوقت، ثم رجع وصلى مع الجماعة ينبغي أن لا يكون مكروهاً. [البحر الرائق: ١٢٧/٢]
His exiting from a mosque in which the adhan was given – so if his imam catches him in it, it is valid, otherwise no. And it is severely disliked to remain in it until he prays, unless he is establishing another congregation. 'From the adhan in it is a mosque in which the adhan was given' etc.: The author made it general, so it includes if the adhan was given while he was inside or he entered after the adhan. The apparent meaning is the entry of time while he is inside, whether the adhan was given in it or elsewhere. Also the apparent meaning is that exiting without prayer is [leaving] the prayer with the congregation, whether he exits or remains in the mosque without praying, as we see in our time from some immoral people. Even if the congregation delays for the entry of the preferred time, like Fajr for example, and a person exits the mosque after the time has entered, then returns and prays with the congregation, it should not be disliked. [Al-Bahr al-Raiq 2/127]
Source pages p. 152

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on leaving a mosque after the adhan has been given without having prayed. The basic rule is that it is severely disliked (makruh tahrimi) to leave without praying, unless one intends to establish another congregation elsewhere. The commentary explains that the adhan being given in the mosque is the trigger; once the time has entered and the adhan is called, one should not leave until he has prayed with that congregation. However, if the congregation delays the prayer (e.g., waiting for a preferred time), and a person leaves and then returns to pray, it may not be disliked because the congregation is still ongoing. The ruling applies whether one was inside during the adhan or entered after. It is analogous to staying in the mosque without praying idly, which is also discouraged.

Key Terms
مكروه تحريما (makruh tahrimi): An action that is sinful and forbidden, but less severe than haram; it is established by a zanni evidence.
الأذان (al-adhan): The call to prayer made at the mosque to announce the time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on leaving the mosque after the adhan has been given without praying?
A) Permissible (mubah)
B) Lightly disliked (makruh tanzih)
C) Severely disliked (makruh tahrimi)
D) Forbidden (haram)

Key Takeaway
Leaving the mosque after the adhan without praying is severely disliked (makruh tahrimi), unless one leaves to establish another congregation or has a valid reason like returning for a delayed congregation.

Oath Implications of Catching Partial Congregation
Ruling and intra-Hanafi dispute on catching partial congregation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on whether an oath to pray in congregation is broken by catching the majority of the prayer, and explain the basis for the difference between Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani and the apparent answer.

Core Idea
Catching most of the prayer does not count as full congregation for an oath—part of a thing is not the thing.

In the Hanafi school, catching even one rak'ah of a congregational prayer gives one the virtue of praying in congregation. But what if someone swears not to pray a particular prayer in congregation, and then catches only part of it? This lesson examines a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute about whether catching the majority (three of four or two of three) constitutes the full prayer for oath purposes. We will follow the reasoning of the scholars and identify the relied-upon ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial ruling on catching one rak'ah
The passage first states that catching even one rak'ah gives the virtue of congregation. This is the basis for the oath scenario.
2
Understand the oath scenario
If someone swears 'I will not pray Zuhr (or Maghrib) in congregation', what happens if they catch three of the four rak'ahs (or two of three)? The passage presents two views.
3
Analyze Shams al-A'imma's view
Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani argues that the oath is broken because 'the majority has the ruling of the whole' (al-akthar ka al-kull).
This principle is used in other areas of fiqh, e.g., what dominates a contract.
4
Analyze the apparent answer
The apparent answer (zahir al-jawab) holds that the oath is not broken because 'part of a thing is not the thing' (ba'd al-shay' laysa bi al-shay'). The person only prayed part of the prayer with congregation.
This is the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position.
5
Conclude with the preferred view
The text states 'wa huwa al-zahir' (it is the apparent), signaling that the second view is preferred. The oath is not broken.
The preference is based on caution in oath-breaking and literal interpretation of the oath wording.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولم يصل الظهر جماعة بإدراك ركعة بل أدرك فضلها واختلف في مدرك الثلاث أو ركعتين
أدرك فضلها: ولهذا لو حلف لا يدرك الجماعة يحنث إذا أدرك الإمام في آخر الصلاة، ولو في التشهد [تبيين الحقائق: ٤٥٥/١] واختلف إلخ: فإذا حلف لا يصلي الظهر أو المغرب جماعة اختار شمس الأئمة أنه يحنث؛ لأن للأكثر حكم الكل، وعلى ظاهر الجواب لا يحنث؛ لأنه لم يصلها بل بعضها بجماعة وبعض الشيء ليس بالشيء، وهو الظاهر. [مراقي الفلاح: ٤٥٣] الثلاث: من رباعية أو الثنتين من الثلاثية. [مراقي الفلاح: ٤٥٣]
If one did not pray Zuhr in congregation but caught one rak'ah, he has caught its virtue. And there is disagreement about one who catches three or two [rak'ahs]. He caught its virtue: for this reason, if one swears that he will not catch the congregation, he breaks his oath if he catches the imam at the end of the prayer, even in the tashahhud. And as for the disagreement, etc.: If one swears not to pray Zuhr or Maghrib in congregation, Shams al-A'imma chose that he breaks his oath because the majority has the ruling of the whole. According to the apparent answer, he does not break his oath because he did not pray it but rather part of it with congregation, and part of a thing is not the thing. And that is apparent. The three: from a four-rak'ah [prayer], or the two from a three-rak'ah.
Source pages p. 152

Commentary
This passage addresses the legal effect of catching only part of a congregational prayer, specifically for oath purposes. The initial statement establishes that even catching one rak'ah of Zuhr in congregation yields the virtue of congregational prayer, but then notes a difference of opinion (ikhtilaf) regarding catching three rak'ahs of a four-rak'ah prayer or two of a three-rak'ah prayer. The commentary expands with a relevant oath scenario: if someone swears not to 'catch the congregation', catching the imam at the very end (even in tashahhud) breaks the oath. But a more specific scenario is considered: if someone swears not to 'pray Zuhr (or Maghrib) in congregation', and catches three of four or two of three, does the oath break? Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani argued that it does, applying the principle 'the majority takes the ruling of the whole' (al-akthar ka al-kull). However, the relied-upon position (al-zahir) is that the oath is not broken, because the person did not pray the entire prayer in congregation—only a part. The principle is that 'part of a thing is not the thing' (ba'd al-shay' laysa bi al-shay'). Thus, for a valid oath of this nature, the entire prayer must be performed with the congregation. The final line clarifies: 'three' refers to three rak'ahs of a four-rak'ah prayer, and 'two' to two of a three-rak'ah prayer (i.e., Maghrib). This ruling is relevant for anyone swearing about congregational attendance.

Key Terms
مدرك الفريضة (mudrik al-farīḍah): One who catches part of the congregational obligatory prayer.
الثلاث (al-thalāth): Three rak'ahs in a four-rak'ah prayer (like Zuhr), considered the majority.
الركعتين (al-rak‘atayn): Two rak'ahs in a three-rak'ah prayer (like Maghrib), considered the majority.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone swears he will not pray Zuhr in congregation, and he catches three rak'ahs of the four-rak'ah prayer with the congregation, what is the relied-upon ruling according to the text?
A) He breaks his oath because three is the majority.
B) He does not break his oath because he did not pray the entire prayer.
C) He breaks his oath only if he catches all four rak'ahs.
D) The oath is nullified.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi jurisprudence, an oath to pray an entire prayer in congregation is not broken by catching only the majority of the prayer; part of a thing is not the thing.

Catching the Imam in Ruku': Conditions and Consequences
Ruling on validity of rak'ah when catching imam in ruku' and follower's ruku' timing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for catching a rak'ah when joining the imam in ruku' and identify the ruling when a follower bows before the imam.

Core Idea
To catch the rak'ah, you must bow before the imam rises; bowing ahead of the imam invalidates that ruku' and requires repetition.

In congregational prayer, timing is crucial. This passage from Nur al-Idah clarifies two related scenarios: what happens if you join the imam mid-ruku' and what happens if you bow before the imam does. Understanding these rules preserves the validity of your prayer and your connection to the imam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario: joining the imam in ruku'
A latecomer finds the imam already in ruku' and says takbir but does not bow; he remains standing until the imam raises his head.
This is the mudrik al-imam raki'an scenario.
2
Determine the ruling for that scenario
The passage states that such a person has not caught the rak'ah. The takbir alone does not count; he must actually bow while the imam is still in ruku'.
The key condition is performing ruku' before the imam rises.
3
Identify the second scenario: follower bows before the imam
After the imam has finished his recitation but before the imam bows, the follower goes into ruku' ahead of the imam.
This is raka'a qabla imamih.
4
Determine the ruling for bowing ahead
The follower's ruku' is invalid because it occurred before its proper time. He must bow again after the imam bows.
If he does not repeat the ruku', his prayer becomes invalid.
5
Note the extra ruling on recitation dropping
The passage adds that similar to the follower's recitation being waived, the obligation is dropped by the exit of the time for Friday and Eid prayers.
This is a separate point about when recitation is not required.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن أدرك إمامه راكعا فكبر ووقف حتى رفع الإمام رأسه لم يدرك الركعة، وإن ركع قبل إمامه بعد قراءة الإمام المقتدي لا يصح ركوعه؛ لكونه قبل أوانه، فيلزمه أن يركع بعده ثانياً، وإن لم يفعل وانصرف من صلاته بطلت. [مراقي الفلاح: ٤٥٦] وإلا لا وكذا يسقط بخروج وقت الجمعة والعيد
And whoever catches his imam in ruku' and says takbir and stands until the imam raises his head has not caught the rak'ah. And if he bows before his imam after the recitation of the imam the follower's bowing is not valid because it is before its proper time. He must then bow a second time after him. If he does not do so and departs from his prayer, it becomes invalid. Otherwise not, and similarly it is dropped by the exit of the time of Friday and Eid.
Source pages p. 152

Commentary
This passage provides two important rulings related to following the imam in ruku'. First, if a person joins the prayer when the imam is in ruku', he must say takbir and then go into ruku' and remain there long enough that he bows before the imam raises his head. Simply standing and then waiting without bowing until the imam raises his head means he has missed that rak'ah; his takbir alone does not count. Second, if a follower bows before the imam does, specifically after the imam has completed his recitation but before the imam bows, then the follower's ruku' is invalid because it occurred before its proper time. In such a case, the follower must bow again after the imam bows. If he does not do so and instead leaves the prayer, the entire prayer becomes invalid. The final phrase 'وإلا لا' likely means otherwise (if he does not bow again) it is not valid, and 'وكذا يسقط بخروج وقت الجمعة والعيد' adds that similar to the follower's recitation being waived in certain cases, the obligation of the follower's recitation is dropped when the time for Friday or Eid prayers exits (i.e., if one catches only part of the Friday prayer, the recitation requirement adjusts).

Key Terms
مدرك الإمام راكعا (mudrik al-imām rāki‘an): A latecomer who joins the prayer when the imam is in ruku'.
ركع قبل إمامه (raka‘a qabla imāmih): The follower bows before the imam bows, which is invalid and requires a second ruku' after the imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a latecomer joins the imam in ruku' but stands still until the imam raises his head, what is the ruling?
A) He has caught the rak'ah because he said takbir.
B) He has not caught the rak'ah.
C) His prayer is invalid.
D) He must repeat the entire prayer.

Key Takeaway
To catch a rak'ah behind the imam, you must actually bow while the imam is still in ruku'; bowing before the imam is invalid unless repeated after him.

Ruling on Leaving the Mosque After Adhan
Ruling on leaving mosque after adhan with commentary expansion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on leaving the mosque after the adhan and identify the conditions that make it disliked or permissible.

Core Idea
Leaving the mosque after adhan is disliked unless you have a valid excuse or are establishing another congregation.

This passage from Nur al-Idah, with its commentary in Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, clarifies when it is disliked to leave the mosque after the adhan. The ruling aims to preserve the congregational prayer and discourage laziness. Understanding the conditions and exceptions helps apply the ruling correctly in various scenarios.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default ruling
The act is leaving the mosque after the adhan. The default ruling is that it is disliked (makruh) if one intends to pray elsewhere.
The ruling applies whether the adhan was called while you were inside or you entered later.
2
Determine when the disliked ruling applies
The disliked applies when the time for prayer has entered while you are inside the mosque, you have no valid excuse (like travel or illness), and you are not intending to establish another congregation.
If the time has not entered, leaving is not disliked.
3
Understand the exceptions
If you have a valid excuse (mā tajūzu bihi al-ṣalāh), leaving is not disliked. Also, if you leave to establish another congregation elsewhere, it is permissible.
Establishing a second congregation in the same mosque while the first is ongoing is itself disliked, so this exception refers to establishing elsewhere.
4
Apply to a scenario
Consider a case where the congregation delays the prayer to the preferred time (e.g., Fajr). If you step out after the time enters and then return to pray with them, this is not disliked because you did not intend to abandon the congregation.
This shows the ruling is based on intention and actual participation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويكره خروجه من مسجد أذن فيه ما تجوز به الصلاة، فأدركه إمامه فيه صح وإلا لا، ویکره فيه حتى يصلي إلا إذا كان مقيم جماعة أخرى،
أطلقه المصنف، فشمل ما إذا أذن فيه وهو داخله أو دخل بعد الأذان، والظاهر أن مرادهم دخول الوقت وهو داخله، سواء أذن فيه أو في غيره كما أن الظاهر من الخروج من غير صلاة الصلاة مع الجماعة، سواء خرج أو كان ماكثاً في المسجد من غير صلاة كما نشاهده في زماننا من بعض الفسقة، حتى لو كانت الجماعة يؤخرون لدخول الوقت المستحب كالصبح مثلاً، فخرج إنسان من المسجد بعد دخول الوقت، ثم رجع وصلى مع الجماعة ينبغي أن لا يكون مكروهاً. [البحر الرائق: ١٢٧/٢]
And it is disliked for him to leave a mosque in which the adhan was called, with which prayer is permissible. So if the imam catches him in it, it is valid; otherwise not. And it is disliked for him to remain in it until he prays, unless he is establishing another congregation. The author made it general, so it includes whether the adhan was called while he was inside or he entered after the adhan. The apparent meaning is that they mean the time entered while he was inside, whether the adhan was in it or elsewhere. Likewise, the apparent meaning of 'leaving without praying' is leaving without praying with the congregation, whether he exits or remains in the mosque without praying, as we see in our time from some evildoers. Even if the congregation delays for the entry of the preferred time, like for Fajr for example, and a person leaves the mosque after the time enters, then returns and prays with the congregation, it should not be disliked.
Source pages p. 152

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on leaving a mosque after the adhan has been called and before the congregational prayer is performed. The basic ruling is that it is disliked (makruh) to leave the mosque after the adhan if one intends to pray elsewhere, provided that no valid excuse prevents prayer. If the imam (i.e., the congregation) catches him still in the mosque, his prayer is valid; otherwise it is not (i.e., if he leaves, his prayer elsewhere does not carry the same reward). It is also disliked to remain in the mosque without praying (i.e., idling) unless one is establishing another congregation. The commentary explains that the ruling applies whether one was in the mosque at the time of adhan or entered later. The key condition is that the time for prayer has entered while one is inside the mosque. This ruling is designed to prevent laziness and abandoning the congregation. However, if the congregation delays the prayer to the preferred time (e.g., for Fajr, delaying slightly), and one leaves the mosque after the time has entered but then returns and prays with the congregation, it should not be disliked because he did not intend to abandon the congregation. This is a concession for those who may step out briefly.

Key Terms
ما تجوز به الصلاة (mā tajūzu bihi al-ṣalāh): A valid excuse that makes it permissible not to pray, e.g., travel or illness.
مقيم جماعة أخرى (muqīm jamā‘atin ukhrā): One who intends to establish another congregational prayer (e.g., as a second imam for a later group).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person leaves the mosque after the adhan for Zuhr without praying, returns later, and prays with the congregation, what is the ruling?
A) It is always disliked.
B) It is permissible and not disliked if the congregation had delayed the prayer.
C) It is forbidden.
D) It is obligatory to pray immediately upon return.

Key Takeaway
Leaving the mosque after the adhan is disliked (makruh) unless you have a valid excuse or are establishing another congregation, and the ruling depends on whether the prayer time has entered while you are inside.

Joining Congregation as Mutanaffil and the Prohibition of Repeating a Similar Prayer
Ruling on leaving after praying alone and multiple interpretations of a prohibition hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on joining a Zuhr or Isha congregation as a voluntary follower (mutanaffil) after praying alone and evaluate the various interpretations of the hadith 'لا يصلى بعد صلاة مثلها'.

Core Idea
Joining a congregation as a voluntary follower for Zuhr and Isha is permissible; the hadith against repeating prayers is interpreted to avoid unnecessary repetition, not to forbid all repetition.

This lesson addresses a common scenario: you have prayed Zuhr or Isha alone, but then the congregation begins. Should you leave? The Hanafi school provides a specific ruling that allows you to join with the intention of nafl. We also examine the famous hadith 'One should not pray after a similar prayer' and understand its nuanced interpretations, which prevent absolutism.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and Its Conditions
Find the default ruling for leaving after praying alone. When does it become disliked (makruh)? Which prayers are included?
Focus on the exception for Zuhr and Isha.
2
Define Mutanaffil
Understand the concept of praying as a voluntary follower. How does this circumvent the prohibition of repeating a fard prayer?
Key term: mutanaffil – intention is nafl, not fard.
3
Analyze the Hadith and Its Interpretations
List the four interpretations given in the commentary. What common theme do they share?
The hadith is used to discourage unnecessary repetition, not to absolutely forbid it.
4
Determine the Hanafi Tarjih
Which interpretation is operative for fatwa? How is the permissibility of joining as mutanaffil reconciled with the hadith?
The Hanafi school adopts a contextual and flexible approach.
5
Apply the Ruling to a New Scenario
Suppose someone has prayed Asr alone and the congregation starts after he sits. Does the same ruling apply? Why or why not?
The exception is specifically for Zuhr and Isha; other prayers may have different rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن خرج بعد صلاته منفردا لا يكره إلا إذا أقيمت الجماعة قبل خروجه في الظهر والعشاء، فيقتدي فيهما متنفلا، ولا يصلى بعد صلاة مثلها.
ولا يصلى بعد صلاة إلخ: هذا لفظ الحديث قيل : معناه لا يصلى ركعتان بقراءة وركعتان بغير قراءة، فيكون بياناً لفرض القراءة في ركعات النفل كلها، كذا في الشرح، وقيل: نهوا عن الإعادة لطلب الأجر، وقيل: نهي عن الإعادة بمجرد توهم الفساد لدفع الوسوسة، وقيل: نهي عن تكرار الجماعة في المسجد على الهيئة الأولى أو عن إعادة الفرائض مخافة الخلل في المؤدّى. [حاشية الطحطاوي ومراقي الفلاح: ٤٥٨]
And if he leaves after praying alone, it is not disliked unless the congregation is established before his exit in Zuhr and Isha. In that case, he joins as a voluntary follower in both, and one should not pray after a similar prayer. 'One should not pray after a similar prayer' etc.: This is the wording of a hadith. It is said its meaning is that one should not pray two rak'ahs with recitation and two rak'ahs without recitation, thus it is an explanation of the obligation of recitation in all rak'ahs of nafl. This is in the commentary. And it is said they were prohibited from repeating for seeking reward. And it is said it is a prohibition of repeating merely due to an imagined invalidity to ward off waswasa. And it is said it is a prohibition of repeating the congregation in the mosque in the same manner, or repeating obligatory prayers due to fear of defect in the one performed.
Source pages p. 153

Commentary
This passage contains two rulings. First, if someone prays the obligatory prayer alone (i.e., not in congregation) and then leaves the mosque, it is not disliked (makruh) unless the congregational prayer is established before he leaves. In that case, for Zuhr and Isha specifically, he should join the congregation as a voluntary follower (mutanaffil) meaning he prays the same prayer again but with the intention of nafl. The second part is the hadith 'One should not pray after a similar prayer' (لا يصلى بعد صلاة مثلها). The commentary provides multiple interpretations of this hadith. One interpretation is that it means one should not pray two rak'ahs with recitation and two without, clarifying that recitation is obligatory in every rak'ah of nafl. Another interpretation is that it prohibits repeating the same prayer to seek extra reward. A third is that it prohibits repeating due to mere doubt about the first prayer's validity (to prevent obsessive thoughts). A fourth is that it prohibits repeating the congregation in the same mosque in the same manner, or repeating obligatory prayers altogether due to fear of introducing defects. The variety of interpretations shows that the hadith is used as a general prohibition against unnecessary repetition, but with exceptions for certain cases like joining as a voluntary follower when one already prayed alone.

Key Terms
متنفلا (mutanaffilan): As a voluntary prayer; one prays with the congregation with the intention of nafl, not fard.
لا يصلى بعد صلاة مثلها (lā yuṣallā ba‘da ṣalātin mithlihā): A hadith prohibiting repeating a prayer similar to one already performed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if someone has already prayed Zuhr alone and then the congregation is established before he leaves, what should he do?
A) He should leave immediately to avoid repetition.
B) He should join the congregation with the intention of nafl.
C) He should pray again with the intention of fard.
D) He cannot join the congregation because he already prayed.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits joining a Zuhr or Isha congregation as a voluntary follower if one has already prayed alone, and interprets the hadith prohibiting repetition as a general discouragement, not an absolute ban.

Joining the Congregation After Praying Alone: The Hanafi Ruling
Ruling on joining congregation after individual prayer with hadith interpretations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on joining the congregation as nafl after praying fard alone, explain the exception for Zuhr and Isha, and identify the relied-upon interpretation of the hadith.

Core Idea
If the congregation stands for Zuhr or Isha before you leave, join as nafl — do not repeat the same fard in congregation.

The Hanafi school teaches that if you have already prayed an obligatory prayer alone and then a congregation is established for the same prayer, you should not repeat it as fard. Instead, you may join the congregation as a nafl prayer, but only for Zuhr and Isha if the congregation forms before you leave. This nuanced ruling is based on a hadith which has been interpreted in several ways.

Guided Path
1
Identify the basic scenario
A person prays a fard prayer alone (not in congregation). After finishing, he plans to leave, but a congregation for the same prayer is established. What should he do?
The default ruling is that leaving is permissible and not disliked.
2
Recognize the exception
The exception applies only to Zuhr and Isha. If the congregation is established before the person leaves, it is sunnah to join the congregation as a nafl worshipper.
This is a recommended act, not obligatory.
3
Understand the prohibition
The hadith states: 'Do not pray a prayer like it after a prayer.' The Hanafi interpretation is that this prohibits repeating the same fard prayer in congregation, not an absolute ban on any nafl after fard.
Thus, joining as nafl is allowed, but repeating the fard as a second congregation is not.
4
Explore alternative interpretations
The commentary lists several other possible meanings of the hadith, such as a rule about recitation in nafl, or a prohibition against repeating for worldly gain. The Hanafi school adopts the interpretation that avoids confusion about the validity of the first prayer.
This shows how the same dalil can be understood differently, and the Hanafi tarjih is based on established usul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إدراك الفريضة
وإن خرج بعد صلاته منفردا لا يكره إلا إذا أقيمت الجماعة قبل خروجه في الظهر والعشاء، فيقتدي فيهما متنفلا، ولا يصلى بعد صلاة مثلها.
ولا يصلي بعد صلاة إلخ: هذا لفظ الحديث قيل : معناه لا يصلى ركعتان بقراءة وركعتان بغير قراءة، فيكون بياناً لفرض القراءة في ركعات النفل كلها، كذا في الشرح، وقيل: نهوا عن الإعادة لطلب الأجر، وقيل: نهي عن الإعادة بمجرد توهم الفساد لدفع الوسوسة، وقيل: نهي عن تكرار الجماعة في المسجد على الهيئة الأولى أو عن إعادة الفرائض مخافة الخلل في المؤدّى. [حاشية الطحطاوي ومراقي الفلاح: ٤٥٨]
Catching the obligatory prayer. And if he leaves after his prayer alone, it is not disliked unless the congregation is established before his departure in Zuhr and Isha, then he follows in them as a supererogatory worshipper, and he should not pray a prayer like it after a prayer. 'And he should not pray after a prayer' etc.: this is the wording of the hadith. It is said: its meaning is that he should not pray two rak'ahs with recitation and two rak'ahs without recitation, so it is an explanation of the obligatory nature of recitation in all supererogatory rak'ahs, as in the commentary. And it is said: they were prohibited from repetition for seeking reward. And it is said: prohibition of repetition due to mere illusion of invalidity to repel waswasa. And it is said: prohibition of repeating the congregation in the mosque in the first manner, or repeating obligatory prayers for fear of defect in what has been performed. [Margin of al-Tahtawi and Mityftah al-Falah: 458]
Source pages p. 153

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with its proof and expansions. The matn states: if a person prays the fard alone and then leaves, it is not makruh (disliked). However, an exception is made for Zuhr and Isha: if the congregation is established before he leaves, he should join the congregation as a nafl (supererogatory) worshipper, meaning he makes the intention for nafl and follows the imam. Moreover, he should not after that prayer pray another prayer like it—i.e., he should not repeat the same fard prayer in congregation. The hashya then provides several interpretations of the hadith 'لا يصلى بعد صلاة مثلها' (do not pray after a prayer a like prayer). These interpretations range from a ruling about recitation in nafl, to a prohibition against repeating prayers for worldly reward or due to obsessive doubts. The relied-upon interpretation is that it prohibits repeating the congregational prayer in the same manner, to avoid creating confusion about the validity of the first prayer. The Hanafi position is that joining the congregation as nafl is mustahabb (recommended) when the congregation stands before one leaves, but leaving without joining is not sinful.

Key Terms
متنفلا (mutanaffilan): As a supererogatory (nafl) worshipper, meaning intending a voluntary prayer while following the imam.
لا يكره (la yukrah): It is not disliked; i.e., it is permissible (mubah) and not blameworthy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is it sunnah to join the congregation as nafl after praying fard alone?
A) In all five daily prayers.
B) Only in Zuhr and Isha, if the congregation is established before one leaves.
C) Only in Fajr and Maghrib.
D) Only if one intends to repeat the fard prayer.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits joining a congregation as nafl after praying fard alone, but only for Zuhr and Isha, based on a nuanced interpretation of the hadith prohibiting repetition of the same fard prayer in congregation.

Obligation of Sujood al-Sahw for Leaving a Wajib
Defines when sujood al-sahw becomes wajib and its details

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of sujood al-sahw for leaving a wajib, identify when it is wajib, and distinguish between forgetful and intentional omission.

Core Idea
Sujood al-sahw is wajib only for leaving a wajib forgetfully; intentional omission requires repeating the prayer, not prostrations.

This passage from Nur al-Idah lays out the core Hanafi ruling on prostration of forgetfulness (sujood al-sahw). It clarifies that sujood al-sahw is obligatory only when a wajib act is omitted forgetfully, not when omitted intentionally. The text also discusses the sunnah of performing it after the salutation, the makruh nature of prostrating before, and conditions that cancel the obligation. Understanding this ruling helps ensure one's prayer is completed correctly according to the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what sujood al-sahw is and its hukm level. The text states it is wajib (obligatory) when a wajib act is forgotten.
Wajib is a level between fard and sunnah.
2
Distinguish forgetful vs intentional omission
Read the condition: 'for leaving a wajib forgetfully' vs 'if its leaving was intentional'. For intentional omission, the prayer is invalid and must be repeated; sujood al-sahw is not performed.
The exception (قيل) for three intentional cases is not the relied-upon view.
3
Note the sunnah and makruh rulings
Identify that performing sujood after the salutation is sunnah, and before is makruh tanzihi. One salutation to the right is permissible in the most correct view.
The preferred view is two salutations as in the hadith.
4
Understand when sujood al-sahw is dropped
If sunrise occurs after salutation in Fajr, or redness in Asr, the sujood is dropped. Also if something prevents building (like nullifying the prayer) after salutation.
These conditions are specific to certain prayers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب سجود السهو
يجب سجدتان بتشهد وتسليم لترك واجب سهوا وإن تكرر، وإن كان تركه عمدا أثم ووجب إعادة الصلاة لجبر نقصها، ولا يسجد في العمد للسهو، وقيل: إلا في ثلاث: ترك القعود الأول أو تأخيره سجدة من الركعة الأولى إلى آخر الصلاة، وتفكره عمدا حتى شغله عن ركن، ويسن الإتيان بسجود السهو بعد السلام، ويكتفي بتسليمة واحدة عن يمينه في الأصح، فإن سجد قبل السلام كره تنزيها، ويسقط سجود السهو بطلوع الشمس بعد السلام في الفجر، واحمرارها في العصر، وبوجود ما يمنع البناء بعد السلام.
أي تغير بتشهد: ويأتي فيه بالصلاة على النبي والدعاء على المختار. وتسليم: أطلق المصنف في السلام فانصرف إلى المعهود في الصلاة، وهو تسليمتان كما هو في الحديث. لترك واجب: أطلقه، فشمل ما إذا كان بتقديم أو تأخير أو نقص، وخرج به السنة؛ لأن الصلاة لا توصف بالنقصان على الإطلاق بترك السنة، وسجدتا السهو لجبر النقصان والفرض؛ لأنه يفوت بفواته أصل الصلاة لا الوصف فلا يتخير لغيره. وإن إلخ كترك الفاتحة والاطمئنان في الركوع والسجود والجلوس الأول، وتأخير القيام للثالثة بزيادة قدر أداء ركن ولو ساكتا. تكرر أطلقه، فشمل ما إذا كان من جنس أو جنسين، فلا يجب أكثر من السجدتين بالإجماع. لجبر نقصها: اختلفوا في الصلاة المعادة فقيل: إنها مكملة وسقط الفرض بالأولى، وقيل: تكون الثانية فرضاً، فهي المسقطة. في ثلاث بل في خمس الأول: ما لو صلى على النبي في القعود الأول عمداً، والثاني: ما إذا ترك الفاتحة عمداً. الركعة الأولى: الأولى تعبير بعضهم حيث قال: أو أخر إحدى سجدتي ركعة إلى ما بعدها عمداً. الأصح وقيل: تلقاء وجهه فرقاً بين سلام القطع وسلام السهو، قاله فخر الإسلام، وفي الهداية: ويأتي بتسليمتين هو الصحيح. كره تنزيها ولا يعيده لأنه مجتهد فيه، فكان جائزاً. ويسقط إلخ وكذا يسقط بخروج وقت الجمعة والعيد.
Chapter of Sujood al-Sahw. Two prostrations are obligatory with tashahhud and salutation for leaving a wajib forgetfully, even if repeated. And if its leaving was intentional, he sins and the prayer must be repeated to compensate its deficiency, and he does not prostrate for intentional [leaving] due to forgetfulness. And it is said: except in three: leaving the first sitting or delaying a prostration from the first rak'ah to the end of the prayer, and his intentional reflection until it distracted him from a pillar. And it is sunnah to perform sujood al-sahw after the salutation, and one suffices with one salutation to his right in the most correct [view]. If he prostrates before the salutation, it is makruh tanzihan. And sujood al-sahw is dropped by sunrise after the salutation in Fajr, and by redness [after Asr], and by the occurrence of something that prevents building after the salutation. [Commentary:] ...
Source pages p. 154

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement on the obligation and details of sujood al-sahw. It first establishes that two prostrations are wajib for leaving a wajib forgetfully, even if the omission is repeated. If the wajib was left intentionally, the prayer is invalid and must be repeated, and sujood al-sahw is not performed because it is only for forgetfulness. There is an opinion (قيل) that sujood al-sahw is also performed for intentional acts in three cases: leaving the first sitting, delaying a prostration, or deliberate thought that distracts from a pillar. However, the relied-upon view is that sujood al-sahw is only for forgetfulness, as stated earlier. It is sunnah to perform sujood al-sahw after the salutation, and one may suffice with one salutation to the right (though the preferred view is two salutations as in the hadith). Prostrating before the salutation is makruh tanzihan. Sujood al-sahw is dropped if sunrise occurs after salutation in Fajr or redness in Asr, as the time for those prayers ends. The commentary then explains each phrase: the tashahhud includes salawat and dua; the salutation is two as per hadith; 'for leaving a wajib' includes any deficiency in wajib acts, not sunnah; repetition of forgetfulness does not multiply the prostration; and there is ikhtilaf on whether a repeated prayer is a completion or a fresh obligation.

Key Terms
سجود السهو (sujood al-sahw): Two extra prostrations performed to compensate for forgetful omission of a wajib in prayer.
واجب (wajib): A required element of prayer that is not fard; its omission requires sujood al-sahw if forgetful.
تشهد (tashahhud): The testimony recited in the sitting position, including salawat and dua in the sujood al-sahw.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling if someone intentionally omits the first sitting (a wajib)?
A) He performs sujood al-sahw
B) He sins and must repeat the prayer
C) The prayer is valid with no penalty
D) He must perform two extra rak'ahs

Key Takeaway
Sujood al-sahw is wajib only for forgetful omission of a wajib; intentional omission requires repeating the prayer, not prostrations.

Sujood al-Sahw for the Ma'mum, Masbuq, and Lahiq
Explains sujood al-sahw obligations for different participants in congregational prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rules of sujood al-sahw for the ma'mum, masbuq, and lahiq, and explain why the masbuq must prostrate separately for his own forgetfulness.

Core Idea
The ma'mum follows the imam's sujood; masbuq duplicates; lahiq avoids—each due to unique prayer status.

In congregational prayer, forgetfulness can affect the imam, the follower, or one who joined late. The Hanafi school provides specific rulings for each role to ensure the prayer's validity. This lesson clarifies the obligations and exceptions for the ma'mum, masbuq, and lahiq regarding sujood al-sahw.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories
Distinguish between ma'mum (follower who caught the entire prayer), masbuq (one who missed one or more rak'ahs), and lahiq (one who started with imam but missed part due to excuse).
2
State the rule for the ma'mum
The ma'mum is bound by the imam's forgetfulness; he does not perform sujood for his own forgetfulness to avoid breaking conformity.
He follows the imam even if he himself forgot something.
3
State the rule for the masbuq
The masbuq first prostrates with the imam, then later completes his missed rak'ahs. If he forgets in that completion, he must perform sujood al-sahw again because his prayer is like two separate prayers.
The double sujood is a key Hanafi position.
4
State the rule for the lahiq
Unlike the masbuq, the lahiq does not perform sujood al-sahw for forgetfulness in his own actions.
He is distinct because he started with the imam.
5
Note the exception for Jumu'ah and Eid
The imam does not perform sujood al-sahw in Jumu'ah and Eid prayers to avoid confusion in large congregations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويلزم المأموم بسهو إمامه لا بسهوه، ويسجد المسبوق إمامه، ثم يقوم بقضاء ما سبق به، ولو سها المسبوق فيما يقضيه سجد له أيضاً لا اللاحق، ولا يأتي الإمام بسجود السهو في الجمعة والعيدين، ومن سها عن القعود الأول من الفرض عاد إليه إماما كان أو منفردا وجوبا ما لم يستو قائما في ظاهر الرواية وهو الأصح والمقتدي كالمتنفل يعود ولو استتم بمعنى ما دام قائما، فإن عاد.
ويلزم المأموم إلخ أي يجب على المقتدي سجود السهو بسهو إمامه، أطلقه فشمل ما إذا كان مقتديا به وقت السهو أو لم يكن، وما إذا سجد سجدة واحدة ثم اقتدى به فإنه يتابعه في الأخرى، ولا يقضى الأولي كما لا يقضيها لو اقتدى به بعد ما سجدهما، وشمل كلامه المدرك والمسبوق واللاحق، فإنه يلزمهم بسهو إمامه، لكن اللاحق لا يتابع الإمام في سجود السهو إذا انتبه في حال اشتغال الإمام بسجود السهو أو جاء إليه من الوضوء في هذه الحالة، وإنما يبدأ بقضاء ما فاته، ثم يسجد في آخر صلاته والمسبوق والمقيم خلف المسافر يتابعان الإمام في سجود السهو، ثم يشتغلان بالإتمام. لا بسهوه: أي لا يجب سجود السهو بسهو نفسه يعني المقتدي؛ لأنه لو سجد وحده كان مخالفاً لإمامه، ولو تابعه الإمام ينقلب التبع أصلاً. ثم يقوم إلخ أتى بـ "ثم" ليفيد تراخي القيام عن سلام الإمام، وينبغي أن يمكث المسبوق بقدر ما علم أنه لا سهو عليه، وله أن يقوم قبل سلامه بعد قعوده قدر التشهد في مواضع: خوف مضي مدة المسح، خروج الوقت لذي عذر، خروج الوقت في صلاة العيد، خروج الوقت لصلاة الجمعة، خروج وقت الفجر، مرور الناس من بين يديه إلى قضاء ما سبق به، ولا ينتظر سلامه. ولو سها المسبوق إلخ مثلا: دخل رجل في صلاة الإمام، وقد فرغ من ثلاث ركعات، ثم سجد الإمام للسهو فسجد المسبوق متابعة له، ثم سلم الإمام، وقام المسبوق يؤدّي ركعات لم يؤدها مع الإمام فسها فيها يجب عليه سجدتا السهو، ولا يجزيه سجوده مع الإمام، وتكرار سجود السهو من حيث إن صلاته كصلاتين حكماً؛ لأنه منفرد فيما يقضيه. أيضاً أي كما سجد مع الإمام يسجد حال انفراده أيضاً. لا اللاحق أي لا يسجد اللاحق إذا سها فيما يفعله، وهو من أدرك أول صلاة الإمام وفاته باقيها بعذر كنوم وغفلة وسبق حدث. من الفرض: ولو كان الفرض عمليا كالوتر. وهو الأصح وفي الهداية والكنز: إن كان إلى القيام أقرب لا يعود. فإن عاد أي الساهي عن القعود الأول.
And the ma'mum is bound by the forgetfulness of his imam, not by his own forgetfulness. And the masbuq prostrates with his imam, then stands to make up what he missed. And if the masbuq forgets in what he makes up, he prostrates for it also; not so for the lahiq. And the imam does not perform sujood al-sahw in Jumu'ah and the two Eids. And whoever forgets the first sitting in a fard prayer returns to it – whether imam or alone – obligatorily as long as he has not stood completely upright, according to the apparent narration and it is the most correct. And the follower is like the supererogatory worshipper: he returns even if he has stood completely. And if he returns... [Commentary continues]
Source pages p. 155

Commentary
This passage covers the rules of sujood al-sahw for followers. The ma'mum is obligated to follow the imam's sujood al-sahw, but does not perform it for his own forgetfulness, as that would break conformity. The masbuq (one who missed some rak'ahs) must first follow the imam in sujood al-sahw, then after the imam's salutation, he stands to complete his missed rak'ahs. If he forgets in that completion, he must perform sujood al-sahw separately; his earlier prostration with the imam does not cover it because his prayer is considered two prayers in one (he was a follower then becomes alone). The lahiq (one who started with the imam but missed part due to sleep or similar) does not perform sujood al-sahw for his own forgetfulness because his situation is different. The imam does not perform sujood al-sahw in Jumu'ah or Eid due to the large congregation and potential confusion. Regarding the first sitting: whoever forgets it must return to it as long as he has not fully stood up; the follower is an exception and may return even after standing. This is the relied-upon view according to the Hidayah and Kanz.

Key Terms
مأموم (ma'mum): A follower who caught the entire prayer with the imam.
مسبوق (masbuq): One who joins the prayer late and misses some rak'ahs.
لاحق (lahiq): One who started with the imam but missed part due to a valid excuse.
القعود الأول (al-qu'ud al-awwal): The first sitting after two rak'ahs; wajib.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a masbuq forgets a wajib in his makeup rak'ahs after the imam has finished, what must he do?
A) He does nothing because he already prostrated with the imam.
B) He performs sujood al-sahw again at the end of his prayer.
C) He repeats the entire prayer.
D) He says istighfar and continues.

Key Takeaway
The masbuq must duplicate sujood al-sahw because his prayer comprises two distinct phases: as a follower and as alone.

Returning to the First Sitting (al-Qu'ud al-Awwal) After Forgetting
Explains when to return to the first sitting after forgetting it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on forgetting the first sitting in a fard prayer and identify when one must return and when it is too late.

Core Idea
Return to the first sitting is wajib until fully stood; the follower may return even after standing.

The first sitting (al-qu'ud al-awwal) is a wajib in prayers of three or more rak'ahs. Forgetting it requires immediate return as long as one has not fully stood up. The Hanafi school has a specific rule for the follower that differs from the imam and alone worshipper. This lesson explains the obligation and the exception for the muqtadi.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The first sitting is a wajib in fard prayers of 3 or 4 rak'ahs. Forgetting it triggers a compulsory return.
2
Determine the time limit for return
One must return as long as he has not fully stood upright (estewa qa'iman). Once fully standing, he should not return but complete the prayer and perform sujood al-sahw.
This is the zahir al-riwayah position and the most correct.
3
Note the exception for the follower
The muqtadi (follower) is like a mutanaffil (supererogatory worshipper) – he returns even after fully standing, as long as he is still standing (dama qa'iman).
This is because following the imam takes precedence.
4
Understand the tarjih
The text states 'huwa al-azhah' (it is the most sound) and references al-Hidayah and al-Kanz for this position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويلزم المأموم بسهو إمامه لا بسهوه، ويسجد المسبوق إمامه، ثم يقوم بقضاء ما سبق به، ولو سها المسبوق فيما يقضيه سجد له أيضاً لا اللاحق، ولا يأتي الإمام بسجود السهو في الجمعة والعيدين، ومن سها عن القعود الأول من الفرض عاد إليه إماما كان أو منفردا وجوبا ما لم يستو قائما في ظاهر الرواية وهو الأصح والمقتدي كالمتنفل يعود ولو استتم بمعنى ما دام قائما، فإن عاد.
ويلزم المأموم إلخ أي يجب على المقتدي سجود السهو بسهو إمامه، أطلقه فشمل ما إذا كان مقتديا به وقت السهو أو لم يكن، وما إذا سجد سجدة واحدة ثم اقتدى به فإنه يتابعه في الأخرى، ولا يقضى الأولي كما لا يقضيها لو اقتدى به بعد ما سجدهما، وشمل كلامه المدرك والمسبوق واللاحق، فإنه يلزمهم بسهو إمامه، لكن اللاحق لا يتابع الإمام في سجود السهو إذا انتبه في حال اشتغال الإمام بسجود السهو أو جاء إليه من الوضوء في هذه الحالة، وإنما يبدأ بقضاء ما فاته، ثم يسجد في آخر صلاته والمسبوق والمقيم خلف المسافر يتابعان الإمام في سجود السهو، ثم يشتغلان بالإتمام. لا بسهوه: أي لا يجب سجود السهو بسهو نفسه يعني المقتدي؛ لأنه لو سجد وحده كان مخالفاً لإمامه، ولو تابعه الإمام ينقلب التبع أصلاً. ثم يقوم إلخ أتى بـ "ثم" ليفيد تراخي القيام عن سلام الإمام، وينبغي أن يمكث المسبوق بقدر ما علم أنه لا سهو عليه، وله أن يقوم قبل سلامه بعد قعوده قدر التشهد في مواضع: خوف مضي مدة المسح، خروج الوقت لذي عذر، خروج الوقت في صلاة العيد، خروج الوقت لصلاة الجمعة، خروج وقت الفجر، مرور الناس من بين يديه إلى قضاء ما سبق به، ولا ينتظر سلامه. ولو سها المسبوق إلخ مثلا: دخل رجل في صلاة الإمام، وقد فرغ من ثلاث ركعات، ثم سجد الإمام للسهو فسجد المسبوق متابعة له، ثم سلم الإمام، وقام المسبوق يؤدّي ركعات لم يؤدها مع الإمام فسها فيها يجب عليه سجدتا السهو، ولا يجزيه سجوده مع الإمام، وتكرار سجود السهو من حيث إن صلاته كصلاتين حكماً؛ لأنه منفرد فيما يقضيه. أيضاً أي كما سجد مع الإمام يسجد حال انفراده أيضاً. لا اللاحق أي لا يسجد اللاحق إذا سها فيما يفعله، وهو من أدرك أول صلاة الإمام وفاته باقيها بعذر كنوم وغفلة وسبق حدث. من الفرض: ولو كان الفرض عمليا كالوتر. وهو الأصح وفي الهداية والكنز: إن كان إلى القيام أقرب لا يعود. فإن عاد أي الساهي عن القعود الأول.
And the ma'mum is bound by the forgetfulness of his imam, not by his own forgetfulness. And the masbuq prostrates with his imam, then stands to make up what he missed. And if the masbuq forgets in what he makes up, he prostrates for it also; not so for the lahiq. And the imam does not perform sujood al-sahw in Jumu'ah and the two Eids. And whoever forgets the first sitting in a fard prayer returns to it – whether imam or alone – obligatorily as long as he has not stood completely upright, according to the apparent narration and it is the most correct. And the follower is like the supererogatory worshipper: he returns even if he has stood completely. And if he returns... [Commentary continues]
Source pages p. 155

Commentary
This passage covers the rules of sujood al-sahw for followers. The ma'mum is obligated to follow the imam's sujood al-sahw, but does not perform it for his own forgetfulness, as that would break conformity. The masbuq (one who missed some rak'ahs) must first follow the imam in sujood al-sahw, then after the imam's salutation, he stands to complete his missed rak'ahs. If he forgets in that completion, he must perform sujood al-sahw separately; his earlier prostration with the imam does not cover it because his prayer is considered two prayers in one (he was a follower then becomes alone). The lahiq (one who started with the imam but missed part due to sleep or similar) does not perform sujood al-sahw for his own forgetfulness because his situation is different. The imam does not perform sujood al-sahw in Jumu'ah or Eid due to the large congregation and potential confusion. Regarding the first sitting: whoever forgets it must return to it as long as he has not fully stood up; the follower is an exception and may return even after standing. This is the relied-upon view according to the Hidayah and Kanz.

Key Terms
القعود الأول (al-qu'ud al-awwal): The first sitting after two rak'ahs in prayers of three or more rak'ahs.
استوى قائما (estewa qa'iman): Fully stood upright.
مقتدي (muqtadi): The follower (same as ma'mum).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when must a person not return to the first sitting after forgetting it?
A) When they have fully stood upright.
B) When they have left the sitting position.
C) When they have intended to stand.
D) When they have started reciting another surah.

Key Takeaway
Return to the first sitting is wajib until fully stood for imam/alone; the follower is an exception and returns even after standing.

Returning to the First Sitting After Forgetting It
Ruling on returning to the first sitting in fard prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on returning to the first sitting when forgotten, identify the threshold for return, and apply the consequence regarding sajdah al-sahw and validity of prayer.

Core Idea
Returning to the first sitting is wajib unless fully standing; the closer to standing determines sajdah al-sahw.

The first sitting (al-qa'd al-awwal) in a prayer of three or more rak'ahs is a wajib element. Forgetting it triggers a specific set of rulings depending on when one realizes. This passage from Nur al-Idah explains the obligation to return, the threshold of standing, and the contested issue of prayer validity if one returns after full standing.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is forgetting the first sitting in fard prayer. The ruling is that one must return to it (wajib) as long as he has not fully stood up.
This applies to both imam and individual.
2
Determine the threshold
The key condition is 'mustawi qa'iman' (fully standing). Before reaching that, return is wajib; after that, the ruling becomes problematic.
Fully standing means the body is upright and straight.
3
Apply the proximity rule for sajdah al-sahw
If one returns when closer to standing (e.g., knees off ground but not fully upright), sajdah al-sahw is required. If closer to sitting (knees still on ground), no sajdah.
The text defines 'closer to sitting' as raising buttocks but knees still on ground, or the lower half not straightened.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute on returning after full standing
If one returns after fully standing, there is a difference of opinion: some say the prayer becomes invalid; others say it does not.
The commentator in Al-Bahr favors invalidity, citing that one abandons a fard for something not fard.
5
Evaluate the mufta bihi
The relied-upon view (mufta bihi) is that returning after full standing invalidates the prayer, as per the commentary in Al-Bahr.
There is an alternative view that it is merely a delay and does not invalidate, analogous to forgetting surah or qunoot.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن سها عن القعود الأول من الفرض عاد إليه إماما كان أو منفردا وجوبا ما لم يستو قائما في ظاهر الرواية وهو الأصح والمقتدي كالمتنفل يعود ولو استتم بمعنى ما دام قائما، فإن عاد وهو إلى القيام أقرب سجد للسهو، وإن كان إلى القعود أقرب لا سجود عليه في الأصح، وإن عاد بعد ما استتم قائماً اختلف التصحيح في فساد صلاته.
من الفرض: ولو كان الفرض عمليا كالوتر. [مراقي الفلاح: ٤٦٦] وهو الأصح وفي "الهداية" و"الكنز": إن كان إلى القيام أقرب لا يعود. مراقي الفلاح: ٤٦٦] فإن عاد : أي الساهي عن العقود الأول. (مراقي الفلاح)
وصلية إلى القعود أقرب بأن رفع أليتيه من الأرض وركبتاه عليها أو ما لم ينتصب النصف الأسفل. [البحر الرائق: ١٦٣/٢] في الأصح وفي "الخلاصة": وفي رواية: إذا قام على ركبتيه لينهض يقعد وعليه السهو، ويستوي فيه القعدة الأولى والثانية، وعليه الاعتماد والحاصل على هذا المعتمد أنه إن كان إلى القعود أقرب، فإنه يعود رفع ركبتيه من الأرض لزمه السجود، وإلا فلا. [البحر الرائق: ١٦٥/٢] اختلف التصحيح أي صحح بعضهم القول بفساد صلاته وبعضهم بعدم فسادها قال في "البحر": ثم لو عاد في موضع وجوب عدمه اختلفوا في فساد صلاته، فصحح الشارح الفساد؛ لتكامل الجناية برفض الفرض بعد الشروع فيه لأجل ما ليس بفرض، وفي "المبتغى" بالغين المعجمة: أنه غلط؛ لأنه ليس بترك، وإنما هو تأخير كما لوسها عن السورة فركع، فإنه يرفض الركوع ويعود إلى القيام ويقرأ لأجل الواجب، وكما لو سها عن القنوت فركع، فإنه لو عاد وقنت لا تفسد على الأصح. [البحر الرائق: ١٦٣/٢]
And whoever forgets the first sitting in the fard prayer returns to it, whether imam or alone, as an obligation, as long as he has not fully stood up, in the apparent narration and it is the most correct. And the follower is like the one performing supererogatory prayer; he returns even if he has fully stood, as long as he remains standing. Then if he returns while he is closer to standing, he prostrates for forgetfulness; and if he is closer to sitting, there is no sajdah upon him in the most correct opinion. And if he returns after having fully stood, there is difference in authentication regarding the invalidity of his prayer. Commentary: 'From the fard': even if the fard is practical like witr. [Maraqi al-Falah: 466] And it is the most correct, and in Al-Hidayah and Al-Kanz: if he is closer to standing, he does not return. [Maraqi al-Falah: 466] 'Then if he returns': meaning the one who forgets the first sitting. (Maraqi al-Falah) 'And he returns etc.': closer to sitting means he raises his buttocks from the ground and his knees are on it, or as long as the lower half has not straightened up. [Al-Bahr al-Raiq: 2/163] In the most correct opinion, and in Al-Khulasa: in one narration, if he stands on his knees to rise, he sits and sajdah al-sahw is upon him, and the first and second sitting are equal in this. And the relied-upon position is that if he is closer to sitting, he returns, and if he raises his knees from the ground, sajdah is required; otherwise not. [Al-Bahr al-Raiq: 2/165] 'There is difference in authentication': meaning some authenticate the opinion of invalidity of his prayer and some authenticate its non-invalidity. He said in Al-Bahr: then if he returns in a place where it is not obligatory, they differed about invalidity. The commentator authenticated invalidity due to the completion of the crime of abandoning the fard after starting it for that which is not fard. And in Al-Mubtagha (with the dotted ghain): it is a mistake because it is not abandonment but rather delay, like if one forgets the surah and bows, then he abandons the bow and returns to standing and recites for the wajib, and like if one forgets the qunoot and bows, then if he returns and performs qunoot, it does not invalidate in the most correct opinion. [Al-Bahr al-Raiq: 2/163]
Source pages p. 155

Key Terms
القعود الأول (al-qa'd al-awwal): The first sitting after the second rak'ah in prayers of three or more rak'ahs.
مستو قائماً (mustawi qa'iman): Fully standing upright, i.e., having completed the action of standing.
سجد للسهو (sajada lil-sahw): Prostration for forgetfulness, performed to compensate for mistakes in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) He must return to sitting, and no sajdah al-sahw is required.
B) He must return to sitting and perform sajdah al-sahw.

D) He should prostrate immediately.

Key Takeaway
Forgetting the first sitting triggers an obligation to return if still not fully standing; the need for sajdah al-sahw depends on proximity; returning after full standing is a contested issue with the preferred view being invalidity.
