Forgetting the Last Sitting and Adding a Rak'ah
Ruling on forgetfulness of last sitting with Hanafi commentary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a person forgets the last sitting in prayer and apply the remedy of adding a rak'ah after prostration.

Core Idea
Forgetting the last sitting after prostration transforms the fard into nafl; add a rak'ah to rectify.

Forgetfulness in prayer sometimes leads to extra rak'ahs. The Hanafi school specifies a clear remedy: if you forget the last sitting and stand for another rak'ah, your prayer becomes nafl once you prostrate. Then you must add a complementary rak'ah (a sixth in 4-rak'ah prayers, a fourth in Fajr) to complete a valid nafl. This lesson explains the conditions, the transformation, and why no sajdah al-sahw is needed after the addition.

Guided Path
1
Determine the moment of forgetfulness
Identify whether the person has prostrated for the extra rak'ah or not. The ruling differs: before prostration, he returns; after, he adds a rak'ah.
Prostration here means the sajda of the extra rak'ah, not the final sitting.
2
Classify the transformed prayer
If he prostrates, the prayer becomes nafl (supererogatory). The original obligation is lifted, and the prayer is no longer a fard obligation.
The prayer is 'ghayr madmuna' – not binding; even if spoiled later, no qada required.
3
Apply the adding rule
After prostration, add one rak'ah: for 4-rak'ah prayers (Zuhr, Asr, Isha) add a sixth; for 2-rak'ah Fajr add a fourth. For Maghrib, no addition because it becomes four rak'ahs automatically.
The addition is optional: he may also give salam on the fifth (or third for Maghrib) and consider the extra rak'ah as nafl.
4
Understand the consequences
After adding the rak'ah, no sajdah al-sahw is required again. The prayer is valid as nafl, and there is no dislike in adding.
If he chooses to give salam on the extra rak'ah, his prayer becomes an odd-numbered nafl (witr).
5
Note the exception for Maghrib
Maghrib is originally three rak'ahs. If he stands for a fourth and prostrates, it becomes four. Adding a fifth is not required; the prayer is already a complete nafl.
Commentators note that the matn's phrase 'in them' (Fajr and Maghrib) is imprecise because Maghrib has no addition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن سها عن القعود الأخير عاد ما لم يسجد، وسجد لتأخيره فرض القعود، فإن سجد صار فرضه نفلا، وضَمَّ سادِسة إن شاء، ولو في العصر، ورابعة في الفجر، ولا كراهة في الضم فيهما.
القعود الأخير: أراد بالأخير القعود المفروض ليشمل الفرض الرباعي والثلاثي والثنائي، فإن قعوده ليس متعددا، إلا أن يقال: إنه يسمى أخيراً باعتبار أنه آخر الصلاة لا باعتبار أنه مسبوق بمثله أطلقه، فشمل ما إذا لم يقعد أصلا، أو جلس جلسة خفيفة أقل من قدر التشهد وإذا عاد احتسب له الجلسة الخفيفة، حتى لو كان كلا الجلستين مقدار التشهد ثم تكلم بعده جازت صلاته. [البحر الرائق: ١٦٥/٢] لتأخيره: أي عن اتصاله بالرفع من السجود. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٤٦٨] إن شاء: أي وإن شاء سلم على الخامسة، ولا شيء عليه فيصير متنفلاً بخمس ركعات وتراً، وصلاته غير مضمونة عند علمائنا الثلاثة حتى لو أفسدها لا شيء عليه [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٤٦٩] ولو في العصر : لأن التنفل قبله قصداً لا يكره، فبالظن أولى. [مراقي الفلاح: ٤٦٩] ورابعة في الفجر وسكت عن المغرب؛ لأنها تصير أربعاً، فلا ضم فيها. [مراقي الفلاح: ٤٦٩] فيهما: أي في صلاة الفجر والمغرب، قال الطحطاوي ولو أفرد الضمير لكان أولى؛ لأن المغرب لا ضم فيها. حاشية الطحطاوي: ٤٦٩]
And if he forgets the last sitting, he returns as long as he has not prostrated, and he prostrates for delaying the fard of sitting. Then if he prostrates, his fard becomes nafl, and he adds a sixth if he wishes, even in Asr, and a fourth in Fajr, and there is no dislike in adding in them. Commentary: 'The last sitting': He meant by 'last' the obligatory sitting, to include the fard of four rak'ahs, three, and two; for his sitting is not multiple, unless it is said: it is called 'last' because it is the end of the prayer, not because it is preceded by another like it. It is absolute, so it includes if he did not sit at all or sat a light sitting less than the amount of tashahhud. And if he returns, the light sitting is counted for him, so that if both sittings were the amount of tashahhud and then he spoke after it, his prayer is valid. [Al-Bahr al-Raiq: 2/165] 'For delaying it': meaning from its connection to raising from prostration. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 468] 'If he wishes': meaning if he wishes he gives salam on the fifth, and nothing is upon him, so he becomes a non-obligatory performer with five rak'ahs as witr, and his prayer is not guaranteed according to our three imams, so that even if he spoils it, nothing is upon him. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 469] 'Even in Asr': because performing nafl before it intentionally is not disliked, so by doubt it is more appropriate. [Maraqi al-Falah: 469] 'And a fourth in Fajr' and he remained silent about Maghrib because it becomes four, so there is no adding in it. [Maraqi al-Falah: 469] 'In them': meaning in Fajr and Maghrib, al-Tahtawi said if he had specified the pronoun it would have been better, because Maghrib has no adding. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 469]
Source pages p. 156

Key Terms
القعود الأخير (al-qa'd al-akhir): The final sitting of the prayer, which is fard (obligatory) in Hanafi school.
غير مضمونة (ghayr madmuna): A prayer that, if invalidated, does not require qada (make-up) because it has become nafl and not obligatory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Return to the fourth sitting and perform sajdah al-sahw.
B) Continue as nafl, adding a sixth rak'ah, then complete the prayer.

Key Takeaway
Forgetting the last sitting after prostration transforms the fard into an optional (nafl) prayer, and the worshipper must add a rak'ah to complete it.

Sujud al-Sahw: The Dispute on Returning After Full Standing
Explains the ruling on sujud al-sahw based on proximity to standing or sitting, and the dispute on returning after fully standing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on sujud al-sahw when a person forgetfully stands up and state the mufta bihi position regarding returning after full standing.

Core Idea
Sujud al-Sahw depends on proximity to standing; returning after fully standing does not invalidate prayer.

This passage tackles a subtle scenario in Salah: what happens when a worshipper forgetfully stands up from the first sitting? The ruling depends on whether he is closer to standing or sitting. If he fully stands and then returns, a dispute arises among Hanafi authorities. This lesson unpacks the dispute and clarifies the relied-upon view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage sets two cases: (a) closer to standing (knees off ground), (b) closer to sitting (knees still on ground). Recognize the physical distinction.
2
State the base ruling for each scenario
If closer to standing, sujud al-sahw is wajib. If closer to sitting, no sujud al-sahw in the most correct view.
This is from Zahir al-Riwayah.
3
Recognize the dispute on returning after full standing
If after fully standing (back upright) he returns to sitting, some Hanafi authorities say prayer is invalid, others say it remains valid.
The dispute is only within the Hanafi school.
4
Trace the arguments of both sides
Invalidation proponents argue he abandoned a fard (standing) for a non-fard act. Opponents argue it is a mere delay, analogous to returning for a forgotten surah or qunut.
The analogy to qunut is key.
5
Identify the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon view is that the prayer remains valid and sujud al-sahw is wajib for the delay. This is supported by al-Hidayah and al-Bahr al-Ra'iq.
The mufta bihi is the view of non-invalidation.

Source Text

سجود السهو وهو إلى القيام أقرب سجد للسهو، وإن كان إلى القعود أقرب لا سجود عليه في الأصح، وإن عاد بعد ما استتم قائماً اختلف التصحيح في فساد صلاته. في الأصح وفي "الخلاصة": وفي رواية: إذا قام على ركبتيه لينهض يقعد وعليه السهو، ويستوي فيه القعدة الأولى والثانية، وعليه الاعتماد والحاصل على هذا المعتمد أنه إن كان إلى القعود أقرب، فإنه يعود رفع ركبتيه من الأرض لزمه السجود، وإلا فلا. [البحر الرائق: ١٦٣/٢] اختلف التصحيح أي صحح بعضهم القول بفساد صلاته وبعضهم بعدم فسادها قال في "البحر": ثم لو عاد في موضع وجوب عدمه اختلفوا في فساد صلاته، فصحح الشارح الفساد؛ لتكامل الجناية برفض الفرض بعد الشروع فيه لأجل ما ليس بفرض، وفي "المبتغى" بالغين المعجمة: أنه غلط؛ لأنه ليس بترك، وإنما هو تأخير كما لوسها عن السورة فركع، فإنه يرفض الركوع ويعود إلى القيام ويقرأ لأجل الواجب، وكما لو سها عن القنوت فركع، فإنه لو عاد وقنت لا تفسد على الأصح. [البحر الرائق: ١٦٣/٢]
Prostration of forgetfulness: when he is closer to standing, he prostrates for forgetfulness; and if he is closer to sitting, there is no prostration upon him in the most correct view. And if he returns after having fully stood, there is disagreement (ikhtilaf) in the correct opinion (tashih) regarding the invalidation of his prayer. In the most correct view and in al-Khulasa: and in one narration: when he stands on his knees to rise, he sits and he owes sujud al-sahw, and the first and second sittings are equal in this. And upon this is reliance, and the conclusion based on this relied-upon view is that if he is closer to sitting, he returns (i.e., should return) and his raising his knees from the ground makes sujud incumbent upon him, otherwise not. [al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 2:163] The disagreement in tashih: that is, some corrected the statement that his prayer is invalid, and some corrected that it is not invalid. He said in al-Bahr: then if he returns in a place where it is obligatory not to return, they disagreed regarding the invalidation of his prayer. The commentator (sharih) corrected the invalidation due to the completeness of the offense by abandoning the fard after having started it for the sake of what is not fard. And in al-Mubtagha (with the dotted ghain): that it is a mistake, because it is not an abandonment, but rather a delay, just as if he forgot the surah and bowed, then he abandons the bowing and returns to standing and recites for the sake of the wajib; and just as if he forgot the qunut and bowed, then if he returns and performs qunut, it does not invalidate in the most correct view. [al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 2:163]
Source pages p. 156

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning sujud al-sahw when one forgetfully stands up in prayer. The base ruling states that if the person is closer to standing (i.e., has lifted his knees from the ground), he must perform Sujud al-Sahw. If he is closer to sitting (knees still on the ground), he does not prostrate, according to the most correct view. However, there is a recognized disagreement if he deliberately returns to sitting after fully standing. Some Hanafi authorities hold that returning invalidates the prayer because it involves abandoning a fard (standing) for something non-obligatory (returning to sitting). Others argue it does not invalidate, drawing analogies to cases like forgetting to recite a surah after al-Fatiha and then returning after bowing, which is permissible for a wajib act. The relied-upon view (mu'tamad) is that if he is closer to sitting, he must return and his prayer remains valid; sujud al-sahw is required for the delay.

Key Terms
سجود السهو (sujud al-sahw): Prostration performed to compensate for forgetfulness in prayer.
القعود (al-qu'ud): Sitting position in prayer.
القيام (al-qiyam): Standing position in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon view, if a person forgetfully stands up and is closer to sitting (i.e., his knees are still on the ground), should he perform sujud al-sahw?
A) Yes, he must
B) No, he should not
C) It depends on the school
D) He must repeat the prayer

Key Takeaway
Sujud al-Sahw is wajib when closer to standing; returning after full standing does not invalidate prayer in the relied-upon Hanafi view.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
6 min
Forgetting the Last Sitting: Return or Add a Rak'ah?
States ruling on forgetfulness of last sitting and consequent options.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for forgetting the last sitting in prayer and determine the valid options for completion.

Core Idea
Forgetting the last sitting transforms fard into nafl; you may add rak'ahs or complete as witr.

This lesson addresses a common scenario in prayer: forgetting the final sitting (al-qu'ud al-akhir). The ruling distinguishes between returning before prostration and what happens if you prostrate. It also covers the options to add rak'ahs without dislike for Asr and Fajr, and the silence on Maghrib.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is forgetting the last sitting (qa'dah akhirah) in a fard prayer. The ruling depends on whether the worshipper has prostrated or not.
The last sitting is fard in Hanafi fiqh.
2
Distinguish the two scenarios
Scenario 1: If the worshipper remembers before prostrating (i.e., before performing the sajdah of the next rak'ah), he must return to sitting, recite tashahhud, and then perform Sujud al-Sahw for the delay. Scenario 2: If he prostrates before remembering, the fard prayer is transformed into a nafl (voluntary) prayer.
The transformation is a unique Hanafi concession based on istihsan.
3
Understand the transformation to nafl
Once the fard becomes nafl, the prayer is no longer obligatory. The worshipper has discretion to complete it as a voluntary prayer with extra rak'ahs or end it early.
The prayer is 'not guaranteed' – if invalidated, no qada is required.
4
List the optional additions
For a four-rak'ah fard (e.g., Zuhr, Asr, Isha), the worshipper may add a sixth rak'ah (making it a six-rak'ah nafl) or perform taslim after the fifth as witr. For Fajr, he may add a fourth rak'ah (making it a four-rak'ah nafl). For Maghrib, no addition is allowed because it would become six rak'ahs, which is not established.
The option to add is not disliked; intentional nafl after Asr or Fajr is disliked, but here it is due to forgetfulness, so the dislike is lifted.
5
Note the exceptions and practical application
The ruling applies similarly to all four-rak'ah fard prayers. For Asr, addition is allowed because voluntary prayer before Asr is not disliked. The source remains silent on Maghrib; according to later scholars, no addition is made.
If the worshipper chooses not to add, he simply performs taslim after the fifth (for four-rak'ah fard) or after the third (for Fajr? Actually Fajr becomes four, so taslim after fourth).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن سها عن القعود الأخير عاد ما لم يسجد، وسجد لتأخيره فرض القعود، فإن سجد صار فرضه نفلا، وضَمَّ سادِسة إن شاء، ولو في العصر، ورابعة في الفجر، ولا كراهة في الضم فيهما. أي كله أو بعضه أي ما دام للسهو فرضه نفلا، وضَمَّ سادِسة إن شاء أي وإن شاء سلم على الخامسة، ولا شيء عليه فيصير متنفلاً بخمس ركعات وتراً، وصلاته غير مضمونة عند علمائنا الثلاثة حتى لو أفسدها لا شيء عليه [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٤٦٩] ولو في العصر : لأن التنفل قبله قصداً لا يكره، فبالظن أولى. [مراقي الفلاح: ٤٦٩] ورابعة في الفجر وسكت عن المغرب؛ لأنها تصير أربعاً، فلا ضم فيها. [مراقي الفلاح: ٤٦٩] فيهما: أي في صلاة الفجر والمغرب، قال الطحطاوي ولو أفرد الضمير لكان أولى؛ لأن المغرب لا ضم فيها. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٤٦٩]
And if he forgets the last sitting, he returns as long as he has not prostrated, and he prostrates for the delay of the obligatory sitting. And if he prostrates, his fard becomes nafl, and he adds a sixth (rak'ah) if he wishes, even in Asr, and a fourth in Fajr, and there is no dislike in adding in these two. That is, all or part of it, as long as it is due to forgetfulness, his fard becomes nafl. And he adds a sixth if he wishes: that is, if he wishes, he may perform taslim after the fifth and nothing is upon him, so he becomes a performer of nafl with five rak'ahs as witr, and his prayer is not guaranteed according to our three scholars, so even if he invalidates it, nothing is upon him. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 469] Even in Asr: because performing nafl before it intentionally is not disliked, so due to forgetfulness it is even more appropriate. [Maraqi al-Falah: 469] And a fourth in Fajr, and he remained silent about Maghrib because it becomes four, so there is no adding in it. [Maraqi al-Falah: 469] In these two: that is, in Fajr and Maghrib prayer. Al-Tahtawi said: if the pronoun had been specific it would have been better, because Maghrib has no adding in it. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 469]
Source pages p. 156

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement about forgetfulness of the last sitting in prayer. The key rule: if one forgets the last sitting and rises, he must return to sitting before prostrating (i.e., before completing the next sajdah). Upon returning, he recites the tashahhud and then performs Sujud al-Sahw for the delay. If he mistakenly prostrates instead of returning, his fard prayer is transformed into a nafl (voluntary) prayer. He then has the option to complete it as nafl: for a four-rak'ah fard, he can add a sixth rak'ah (making it a six-rak'ah nafl) or finish at the fifth as witr. For Asr, this addition is not disliked because voluntary prayer before Asr is not inherently disliked. For Fajr, he adds a fourth rak'ah (making it four). Maghrib is omitted because adding would make it six, which is problematic. The relied-upon view is that there is no dislike in adding in Fajr and Asr due to forgetfulness, as the prohibition applies only to intentional voluntary prayer after Fajr/Asr.

Key Terms
القعود الأخير (al-qu'ud al-akhir): The final sitting of prayer, which is fard.
نفل (nafl): Voluntary supererogatory prayer.
ضم سادسة (damm sādisah): Adding a sixth rak'ah (to a four-rak'ah fard that became nafl).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a four-rak'ah fard prayer, if one forgets the last sitting and prostrates (transforming the prayer to nafl), how many rak'ahs does he need to add if he chooses to add?
A) One rak'ah to make it five
B) Two rak'ahs to make it six
C) None, he can finish as is
D) He must repeat the prayer

Key Takeaway
Forgetting the last sitting transforms a fard prayer into nafl, giving the worshipper flexibility to complete it with extra rak'ahs or as witr.
